    The text "Nan Zhi" states: If the color appears as a deep yellow, it is a damp disease, and the entire body aches. If the color resembles that of an orange, it is a jaundice disease, and the body does not ache.

    For dry jaundice, characterized by dryness, with spontaneous urination, limbs not feeling heavy, and thirst leading to drinking, one should use the Lu Hu Zhi Pi Decoction. For damp jaundice, related to the spleen, with difficulty in urination, heavy limbs, and a sensation of thirst without desire to drink, the Da Yin Chen Decoction is appropriate. If there is spontaneous yellow bowel movement, one should consider the decoction of Yin Chen, Zhi Zi, and Huang Lian.

    For alternating chills and fevers, accompanied by a yellow complexion all over, the Xiao Chai Hu Decoction with Zhi Zi is recommended. According to Tang Shi: If there is body pain, pain in the waist and back, difficulty in urination and feces, and the skin, face, teeth, and nails are all yellow, with urine resembling the color of house dust, those with easy urination are easier to treat, whereas those with difficulty are harder to treat. It is advisable to take Wu Ling San with Yin Chen decoction or Dao Chi San with Yin Chen decoction. If there is heat in the body, Xiao Chai Hu Decoction should be taken, and in severe cases, Cheng Qi Decoction may be administered.[51p]
    In general, cases of jaundice cannot be treated uniformly. The root and branch differ, and so do the symptoms and treatments. This condition may arise from a deficiency of spleen and stomach qi, leading to the absorption of damp heat, which obstructs the pores and manifests on the skin, accumulating and resulting in yellowing. Alternatively, it may stem from weakness of the spleen and stomach, with internal causes attacking and giving rise to symptoms such as yellow skin, protruding belly with blue veins, muscle wasting, lack of external color, and a必黃色a complexion, which relates to wasting disease.

    Treatment: If the jaundice is caused by damp heat, it resembles smoke-induced color; one should use Wuling Powder with Mahuang, boiled with fresh ginger and taken as a decoction, which will induce sweating and lead to recovery. Alternatively, Yinchenshao Decoction combined with Wuling Powder is also effective.

    If it is due to wasting disease, the appearance resembles yellow earth; in this case use the Lingwai San or Huapi Pill to awaken the spleen and resolve accumulations caused by wasting.[52p]
    When the stomach's qi is harmonious and food intake increases, the essence is transformed and refined, nourishing the body and irrigating the organs. The five colors manifest in their respective parts, and the essence and vitality are expressed in one’s appearance, with any yellowish hue fading away. The classics say: "The central yellow corresponds to the spleen." Therefore, jaundice is the color of the spleen. The spirit of a person is more precious when it is contained and quietly utilized; when it is seen externally, it indicates internal deficiency. This is all due to a deficiency of spleen qi, where transformation and transportation fail, causing dampness and heat to linger in the skin, resulting in jaundice. As Qian Zhongyang stated, symptoms like body aches, back weakness, and yellowing of the skin, face, and nails indicate this condition, with brownish urine being difficult to treat. The treatment should focus on strengthening the spleen first; if one relies solely on harsh purgatives and diuretics, it is rarely safe. If jaundice occurs in newborns within the first hundred days or six months, without being due to illness, it is due to stomach heat or fetal jaundice.[53p]
    If there is a large abdomen with soil eating causing spleen dampness, and also accompanied by thirst for cold drinks, use the Huang San. For difficulty in urination, use Yincheng Decoction. If there is yellowing of the body and edema after illness, use Baizhu San. For those with self-regulating bowel movements, cold limbs, and a tendency to lie down, use Yihuang San. If the body is pale yellow and white, use Tiaozhong Wan and add Yincheng to Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction. If there is heat, fullness in the stomach, and the skin and face are all yellow, then modify and use the Huang San.

    If the symptoms include closed eyes, intense heat, continual crying, and red and thin urine with heat in the mouth, this indicates the signs of pregnancy poison from rich food. Both mother and child should take Sheng Di Huang and avoid alcohol, shallots, and hot foods. If one is not careful and injures the spleen and soil, the condition can quickly turn into convulsions and diarrhea, or slowly lead to edema of the limbs, difficulty in urination, and closed eyelids, resulting in many cases of dampness diseases. There are also cases of yellowing due to spleen deficiency; one should seek solutions within the spleen and stomach.[54p]
    Chao Re (Tidal Fever)

    When a child initially suffers from tidal fever or experiences it post-illness, it relates to the excess of food harming the Taiyin Spleen Meridian. It is advisable to use Shen Ling Bai Zhu San. If there are sores or boils accompanying the tidal fever, modify Ba Zhen Tang by adding Bei Mu.

    General Theories on Child Health

    When a child has body heat that is warm but not excessively strong, this is classified as a warm heat. If the child's body heat is accompanied by a hot sensation in the mouth, continuous crying, yawning, signs of restlessness, and a bluish complexion, this indicates wind heat, which may also lead to fright. If the child exhibits body heat with anxiety over drinking water, trembling hands and feet, looking upwards while moving the tongue, visible blue veins on the inner hands, red palms, and fear of objects causing salivation, this is deemed startling heat. If a child has body heat with a red face that does not subside over time, disturbed sleep with cries, rapid breathing and thirst, elevated chest with phlegm stagnation, this represents accumulated heat. It resembles strong heat but is distinct due to the phlegm accumulation in the elevated chest, indicating a build-up of heat and toxins in the organs, causing stagnation in the three burners. Also, if the child shakes their head and has a stiff neck, it too indicates stagnation in the three burners. All of the above may lead to convulsions in severe cases, and treatment should be approached through the gate of fright and convulsion.[55p]
    When a child has a fever, experiences shortness of breath, nasal congestion, clear runny nose, sneezing, chills, tearing, or possibly produces phlegm, this is classified as a cold injury, treated according to the protocols for a cold injury.

    If a child has a fever that comes and goes, with a hot belly during the fever; or if they have a nighttime fever with a yellow face, abdominal bloating, vomiting, diarrhea, and food not digesting well, with a sour and foul-smelling stool, this indicates food injury, treated according to the protocols for food injury.

    When a child has a nighttime fever that resolves by morning, excessive salivation, and seems to enjoy sleeping, this suggests that the child has a deficiency of the lungs causing the fever, which can resemble a food injury. It is crucial to differentiate between the two, as the residual symptoms vary: in food injury, one can use purgatives; in lung deficiency, one should not, as doing so will lose vital fluids, causing thirst and a desire for drinks.

    In the past, Qian Yi treated a five-year-old who had a nighttime fever that resolved by morning. Many physicians characterized it as a heat condition and prescribed cooling medicines, but it did not improve.[56p]
    The patient had excessive salivation and frequent spitting, and when medicine was administered to reduce the saliva, the illness worsened. After five or six days, I asked Yi to treat him. Yi said: "Do not administer a laxative." He then prepared three sheng of decoction from Atractylodes powder, allowing the patient to take as much as he needed. Zhu asked: "If he drinks too much, won’t it cause diarrhea?" Yi replied: "With no living water, it cannot cause diarrhea. Even if there is a discharge, it is not alarming; just don’t use a laxative!" Zhu further inquired: "What illness was treated first?" Yi responded: "To stop diarrhea, treat phlegm, reduce fever, and calm the spirit—all with this medicine." After the prescription was fully taken, it was given again twice, and the child was no longer thirsty and had no phlegm. Then, two doses of Ejiao powder were given, and he was at peace. This is indicative of that condition. This is recorded in the collected works of Qian Yi.

    For children with fever, emaciation, and excessive thirst, whose diet does not lead to muscle growth, it indicates intestinal heat, which should be treated by addressing the intestinal issue.

    For children with abundant blood and energy, excessive thirst leading to drinking, hard yellow stools, scant red urine, and heat in the limbs and body, it indicates heat in the stomach, which should be treated with a laxative.[57p]
    When a young child has a slight fever and is slightly startled, with cold ears and white blisters appearing on the upper lip like fish eyes, and either has sweat or does not, this indicates a condition called "transformation steaming," which is treated under the category of "transformation steaming."

    When a child has a fever, is lethargic and startled, enjoys sneezing, and has cold ears, this indicates symptoms of measles, treated under the category of "measles." This is similar to illness caused by food injury leading to transformation steaming, where cold ears are hot in cases of cold damage, while the dual steaming with white warts and blisters on the lips is different.

    Fever in children may derive from both internal and external causes. Internal causes often arise from excessive water consumption, while external causes are typically due to wind and cold. According to Qian, when a child has an internal fever and drinks a lot of water, it indicates internal heat, while if a child has a fever and does not drink water, it indicates external heat. This is a general diagnostic principle. For internal causes, treatment should focus on purging, while for external causes, treatment should focus on dispersing.

    Yan Xiaozhong discusses the patterns of high fever from wind chill and illnesses like warm epidemic and cold damage, as well as wind-heat measles and food injury, which are all quite similar and often difficult to distinguish. However, treatments like Shengma Gegen Decoction, Xingsingsan, and Xiao Chaihu Decoction have proven to be very effective.[58p]
    These several medicines can be used for treatment without causing harm. For those with dietary injuries causing foul-smelling stools, undigested milk, food aversion, or vomiting, it is advisable to use a mild purgative.

    Master Sun discussed that children with excess internal and external energy might experience slight fright during sleep or mild symptoms of wind or dietary injury, as well as a concern for heat in the body. For such cases, using Ziyuan or Longdan Decoction is appropriate. These two medicines can treat a wide range of ailments. Although they may slightly purge to reduce excess energy, they do not deplete the body’s strength.

    If a child's stools are yellow and foul, it indicates hidden heat in the abdomen, and Longdan Decoction should be administered. If the stools are white and sour-smelling, it indicates lingering cold and indigestion, and Ziyuan should be given. Administer in small doses to help with internal digestion, and if symptoms are severe, slightly increase the dosage to facilitate mild loose stools. It is essential to limit breastfeeding for a day or two to regulate stomach energy. If not restricted, the illness may easily recur, leading to repeated purging, which could harm the stomach's energy and cause abdominal bloating. If purging occurs multiple times, it would lead to excessive depletion.

    After the beginning of summer, if a child has a feverish illness, be cautious not to recklessly induce vomiting or purging. Instead, use heat-clearing decoctions for bathing, apply heat-clearing powders, or use red friction ointments.[59p]
    Jaundice

    When a child has all their skin and face turning yellow, this is called jaundice. It results from excessive rest or overindulgence in food, causing heat in the spleen and stomach, which conflicts with the air from grains, leading to evaporation outward. The spleen and stomach resemble earth, and their color is yellow, affecting the muscles and thus causing the illness. Care must be taken not to moxibust, as that would worsen the heat. If there is body pain, stiffness in the back, difficulty in urination and defecation, abdominal distension, the whole body is yellow, and the eyes and nails are also yellow, with urine like the color of dust, this is jaundice. If there is thirst, difficulty in urination, abdominal fullness, and a deep, fine pulse, it is difficult to treat. The yellow illness is slightly lighter, while jaundice is extremely severe. There is also jaundice that presents as deep yellow in the lower body; this is fetal jaundice due to the mother’s organ heat affecting the fetus. As the classics state, all jaundice that turns a deep yellow is similar. If the body is slightly yellow, it indicates stomach heat. If only the face is yellow and the abdomen is distended, accompanied by a desire to eat dirt, this indicates spleen deficiency.

    Thirst

    When a child is thirsty and drinks water, it is because there is heat within the organs. Heat leads to dryness in the organs, causing the body to feel hot and thirsty, thus prompting a loss of fluids that creates a desire for water to relieve it. There are also symptoms of deficiency thirst, thirst due to vomiting and diarrhea, and thirst due to cholera; each has its specific causes and conditions. Yan Xiaozhong states: For all children's thirst, caused by the loss of fluids, make them drink by giving them a decoction of Qian's white atractylodes powder freely, and the more they drink, the better.[60p]
    Pediatric Remedies

      Formula

    Efficacious Chaihu Powder: For treating childhood bone heat, with symptoms of feeling like it's steaming at night, effective within a few days at most. Use local Chaihu, washing it clean and roasting until yellow, not overly charred, not needing silver variety. Grind to a powder, taking two qian with a cup of water, add two pieces of earth bone skin the size of a finger, boil until reduced to seven parts, and take warm after meals. If the child is thin and weak, take tonic medicines on an empty stomach, and after meals take several doses, drinking like water occasionally.

    Dan Shen Red Paste: For treating heat in the abdomen of young children. Ingredients: Dan Shen, Lei Wan, Mang Xiao, Rong Yan, and Da Huang, each two liang. Crush these five ingredients, soak in half a sheng of bitter wine overnight to refine into one jin of pig fat, boil three times, strain, then add Mang Xiao, and when the paste forms, use it for heart application. This can be used in winter and summer. Alternatively, using just Dan Shen and Lei Wan is also good.[61p]
    Five substances form a sweet licorice ointment, useful for treating young infants who are delicate and weak, often affected by wind evils, feeling strong heat in their bodies, or suffering from major wind, leading to trembling hands and feet. The ingredients are: sweet licorice and protective wind (each one tael), white atractylodes and platycodon (each twenty zhu), and two taels of thunderbolt herb.

    Grind these ingredients, and then using one pound of unsalted pig fat, cook over low heat until it reduces to a thick ointment, straining out the residue. Take a piece about the size of a marble and warm it in your hands to rub on the child a hundred times. If the child feels cold, warm them further; if hot, cool them down. Even if a child seems healthy, it is advisable to apply the ointment on their forehead and the palms of their hands and feet upon waking up to effectively ward off wind and cold.

    Li Leaf Bathing Decoction: For treating slight heat in young bodies.

    Use an unspecified amount of li leaves, grinding them up. Boil in water and strain, then use to bathe the child.

    Willow Branch Bathing Decoction: For infants from one month to five months old, experiencing fluctuations of cold and heat.

    Use a non-specified amount of finely chopped willow branches. Boil to extract the juice and wash the child. If the child is thirsty, strain winter melon juice for them to drink.

    Green Wood Fragrance Bathing Decoction: For treating young children suffering from intense heat and emaciation.

    Ingredients include four ounces of green wood fragrance, one sheng each of hemp seeds and bamboo leaves, five ounces of tiger bone, and three ounces of white atractylodes. Grind these five ingredients together and boil in two dou of water to extract one dou of liquid, then bathe the child gently.[62p]
    Twelve substances: cold water stone disperses heat, used to treat small children with vigorous heat, who cannot take medicine. Cold water stone, mirabilite, talc, gypsum, red resin, rhubarb,青木香 (a type of herb), licorice, scutellaria, saposhnikovia, ephedra root. All in equal parts, to be ground and sifted together, one sheng of powder, mixed with two haos of medication residue, and sifted again until fine, to be taken three times a day.

    Li Gen Decoction: used to treat children with sudden fevers lasting two to three days. Li gen, cinnamon bark, and mirabilite, eighteen zhu each; dried ophiopogon root, and licorice, one liang each. The five ingredients should be chewed and boiled in three sheng of water, reducing to one sheng, divided into five doses.

    Sheng Ma Decoction: used to treat children's febrile diseases that switch to toxic heat, with symptoms like fever, red face, dry mouth, firm abdominal pain, difficulty in urination and defecation, or mouth sores; or due to vigorous heat causing limbs to twitch and convulsions, with intermittent waking up and a body hot like fire afterwards. For this, use one liang of scutellaria, half liang each of sheng ma, white atractylodes, ephedra, stemona, and bupleurum, and half liang of licorice; six zhu each of mirabilite, rhubarb, and vine root. All ten ingredients should be chewed, boiled in three sheng of water, first boiling the ephedra to remove the foam, then adding the other ingredients until one sheng is left. For children aged thirty to sixty days, take two haos; from sixty to one hundred days, two and a half haos; from one hundred to two hundred days, three haos.[63p]
    Dahuang Decoction - Treats children with longstanding internal heat and emaciation, with irregular eating patterns.
    Ingredients:

    • Rhubarb: 1 ounce
    • Glauber's salt: 1 ounce
    • Licorice: 1 ounce
    • Cinnamon: 8 ounces
    • Gypsum: 1 ounce
    • Dates: 5 pieces

    Prepare by grinding the above six ingredients, boil with 3 liters of water to extract 1 liter, and administer 2 danti (about 60 ml) each time.

    Shuqiang Decoction - Treats children with tidal fevers.
    Ingredients:

    • Chinese lacquer: 1 ounce
    • Licorice: 1 ounce
    • Anemarrhena: 1 ounce
    • Dragon bone: 1 ounce
    • Oyster shell: 1 ounce

    Prepare by grinding the above five ingredients, boil with 4 liters of water to extract 1 liter, then strain. For children under one year, administer a small amount twice daily.

    Gypsum Decoction - Treats children with abdominal distension and shortness of breath; those showing signs of fluctuating heat, with digestive distress leading to food not being properly processed.
    Ingredients:

    • Rhubarb: 1 ounce
    • Scutellaria: 1 ounce
    • Licorice: 1 ounce
    • Ophiopogon: 1 ounce
    • Glauber's salt: 1 ounce
    • Gypsum: 1 ounce
    • Cinnamon: 8 grains

    Prepare by grinding the above seven ingredients, boil with 3 liters of water to extract 1.5 liters; administer three doses. For children under one year, give five doses.[64p]
    Bamboo Leaf Decoction: Treats children suffering from abdominal heat in summer, causing warmth and movement; or those with diarrhea, which may be white or yellow, indicating issues in the three burners.

    Ingredients:
    Bamboo leaves and wheat, each five dou; Bupleurum, Ophiopogon, Ginseng, and Licorice, each half liang; Poria, eighteen zhui; Scutellaria, one liang and six zhui.

    Preparation: Combine these eight ingredients, slice them, and use four sheng of water to boil the bamboo leaves and wheat, extracting three sheng. Remove the bamboo leaves and wheat, add the remaining herbs, boil down to one sheng and half, and divide into three doses.

    If a child suddenly has a strong heat in summer, marked by a yellow, watery diarrhea and weak energy, with a rapid pulse, add two liang of Rhubarb to this formula. If it causes a bowel movement, the child will recover.

    Additionally, this treats children aged five or six with excess heat, a tight abdominal feeling, ineffective breathing, or slight swelling; it also addresses extreme thinness with poor appetite, hard distension, and cold hands and feet.

    Ingredients:
    One sheng of bamboo leaves; half sheng of wheat; one liang each of Licorice, Scutellaria, Trichosanthes root, Alisma, Poria, Anemarrhena, Atractylodes; two zhui of Cinnamon bark; one and a half liang of fresh ginger; two liang each of Ginseng, Ophiopogon, and Pinellia; eighteen zhui of Angelica.

    Preparation: Combine these sixteen ingredients, slice them, and use seven sheng of water to boil the bamboo leaves and wheat, extracting four sheng. Remove the residue and boil the remaining herbs down to one sheng and six liu, dividing into four doses.[65p]
    Dashuang Muli Soup treats children with high fever, retained food that does not pass, intermittent chills and heat, and mild palpitations.

    Ingredients:

    • 1 tael of Dahuang (rhubarb)
    • 18 zhu of Huangqin (Scutellaria baicalensis)
    • 18 zhu of Guolou root (Trichosanthes fruit)
    • 18 zhu of Gancao (licorice)
    • 2 taels of Huashi (talcm)
    • Half tael of Guixin (cinnamon heart)
    • Half tael of Danyi (calcined oyster)
    • Half tael of Renshen (ginseng)
    • Half tael of Longgu (dragon bone)
    • Half tael of Ningshuishi (congealed water stone)
    • Half tael of Baishizhi (white stone fat)
    • Half tael of Xiaoshih (niter)

    Prepare these twelve ingredients by grinding together. Add 4 sheng of water and boil down to 1.5 sheng. Take 3 he (a measure) each time, to be taken day and night until finished; it can still be given even if vomiting occurs. One version adds half tael of Zishiqing (purple quartz).[66p]
    Tiao Zhong Decoction: Used for children in spring and autumn who are exposed to cold mornings and evenings. Cold air can cause their limbs to feel weakened; if heat cannot be released, it will lead to strong fever. Cold air entering the stomach can cause diarrhea or obstruction, with symptoms such as abdominal distention and severe pain, strong heat, and rapid pulse. Administering this will alleviate heat and resolve the condition; it is also effective for those with strong heat who do not vomit or have bowel movements.

    Ingredients:

    • Pueraria (Ge Gen),
    • Scutellaria (Huang Qin),
    • Poria (Fu Ling),
    • Platycodon (Jie Geng),
    • Peony (Shao Yao),
    • Atractylodes (Bai Zhu),
    • Licorice (Gan Cao),
    • Rhubarb (Da Huang),
      each six zhū (a weight measure).

    The above nine ingredients should be chewed and boiled in two sheng (about 4 pints) of water until reduced to five he (about 1.3 pints). Dosage is as follows: for a child born within one month, take one he divided into three doses; for eight to fifteen days, one and a half he divided into three doses; for sixteen to twenty days, two he divided into three doses; for twenty to thirty days, three he divided into three doses; for thirty to forty days, five he divided into three doses, but if five he seems excessive, adjust accordingly; for children from one hundred to three hundred days, use this recipe but add ingredients from the previous Long Dan Decoction.

    Sheng Di Huang Decoction: Used for children with alternating cold and heat, irritability, and abdominal pain.

    • Fresh Rehmannia (Sheng Di Huang),
    • Cinnamon (Gui Xin),
      each two liang (about 75 grams).

    Boil the two ingredients in three sheng (about 6 pints) of water to yield one sheng (about 2.6 pints). For children under one year, administer two he; for those over one year, three he. Another formula comprises seven ingredients: Peony, cold water stone, Scutellaria, Angelica (Dang Gui), and Licorice, each half a liang (about 19 grams).

    Xi Jiao Decoction: Used for children with heat in the heart.[67p]
    Rhinoceros horn 18 zhu, Polygala 1 tael, Ophiopogon 1.5 taels, Licorice 0.5 taels, Atractylodes 6 zhu. The above five ingredients (mouth father) are chewed, combined with 9 cups of water, decocted to yield 4 cups, to be divided for consumption. Adding 1 tael of dragon's teeth is preferred.

    Modified Xiao Chai Hu Decoction 【from "Qian's Straightforward Method", same below】. Used for treating liver fire heat in nursing mothers, which causes issues for the child; both mother and child may take it. Chai Hu 1 qian, Huang Qin 7 fen, Ren Shen, Ban Xia each 4 fen, Gan Cao 3 fen, Shan Zhi, Dan Pi each 5 fen. The above are to be decocted in water.

    Chai Shu Ren Ling Decoction treats liver fire and blood heat, resulting in generalized itching, red rashes, or muscle spasms and nodules. Bai Zhu (fried) 1 qian, Ren Shen, Fu Ling each 1 qian, Chai Hu, Chuan Xiong, Shan Zhi, Shao Yao (fried), Gan Cao (fried) each 5 fen, Shu Di Huang (self-prepared), Dang Gui each 8 fen. The above are to be decocted in water for consumption.

    Shao Yao Ren Ling Powder treats liver wood overpowering spleen earth, leading to eye strain and facial pallor, decreased appetite, and fatigue. Shao Yao (fried), Ren Shen, Fu Ling, Bai Zhu, Chen Pi each 7 fen, Chai Hu, Shan Zhi (fried), Gan Cao (fried) each 5 fen. The above are to be decocted in ginger water.

    Long Dan Xie Gan Decoction treats liver channel damp heat, or abscesses or toxins, with dysuria. Long Dan Cao (fried in wine) 5 fen, Che Qian Zi (fried) 3 fen, Mu Tong, Dang Gui Wei, Ze Xie each 3 fen, Gan Cao, Huang Qin, Sheng Di, Shan Zhi each 3 fen. The above are to be decocted in water for consumption.[68p]
    Cool Drink
    For treating internal consumption leading to thinness, accompanied by dryness of the mouth, spontaneous sweating, hard dry stools, and frequent urination.
    Each ingredient: Qianghuo, Chaihu, roasted Licorice, Zhimu prepared with wine, fried Huangqi, Huangqin prepared with wine, one qian each; raw Licorice and Fangji - five fen each; Shengdi prepared with wine and Fangfeng - five fen each; Danggui - six fen; a pinch of Honghua; five each of apricot kernels and peach kernels; Shengma - four fen; gypsum, Chuan Huangbo, and Caolongdan - one qian five fen each.
    Preparation: Take one to two qian per dose, simmer with water and add a little wine before consuming.

    Huanglian Xiangru Drink
    Xiangru: four taels; Houpu: two taels; Huanglian: one tael.
    Preparation: For each dose of one to two qian, stir-fry Houpu and Huanglian with fresh ginger until purple, then add Xiangru. Simmer with one cup of water and wine each, and take when cool.

    Lianqiao Drink (from "Ben Shi Fang")
    For treating adults and children with internal heat accumulation in the five zang organs, causing restlessness, thirst, cracked lips, constricted throat, red eyes, and hardened nose; symptoms of Yangming syndrome with cold-induced mania, hallucinations, and difficult urination and defecation, as well as all types of wind accumulation.
    Each ingredient: Shan Zhi, Licorice, Chishao - one tael each; Dahuang, (Shibu) Nitrate, Lianqiao, Bohe, and dry Kudzu - two taels each.
    Preparation: Grind into a powder, take two qian per dose, simmer with one cup of water, seven pieces of bamboo leaves, and three spoonfuls of honey until reduced to seven parts, then strain and take after meals. Note: For Yangming symptoms of cold, avoid purging.[69p]
    Quanniao San (Full Scorpion Powder) is primarily used for treating children's convulsions from heat. It consists of the following ingredients: one portion of the heart of Tian Nanshen (South Star), three portions of ginseng, and three portions of snake skin, all ground into a fine powder. This is mixed with honeyed water; alternatively, it can be mixed with peppermint and honeyed water.

    Xixin San (Heart-Soothing Powder) treats children who have an overall strong fever, headaches, tightness in the back and sides, intense heat rising, a bitter mouth and dry lips, a dry tongue at night, swollen and painful throat, thick and sticky mucus, phlegm blocking the throat, loss of appetite, restlessness, dry eyes, and painful vision. It is also effective for those with a cold, nasal congestion, heavy limbs, inability to speak, joint pain, and difficulties with urination and defecation. This powder is recommended for smallpox, seasonal epidemics, excessive thirst, and children's night terrors.

    Three taels of rhubarb should be soaked in rice wash for one cooking session and then drained and slowly fried until cooked. Add four taels each of cooked angelica, white peony, fried licorice, schizonepeta, and ephedra, and one tael of fried white atractylodes. Grind all these into a fine powder. The standard dosage is two grams mixed with one cup of water, adding a slice of ginger and two leaves of peppermint, and then simmering until reduced to about 80%. Let it cool, strain, and the medicine should be taken while lying on one's back, without a pillow, for a short time. If there is obstruction in the five organs, seven to nine grams of the main ingredients can be boiled. Should the patient require a softer effect, use a hotter preparation.[70p]
    Xingxing San is used to treat children suffering from wind-heat and seasonal febrile diseases, with symptoms such as rash and fever, severe headache, strong heat, excessive sleepiness, coughing with wheezing, and nasal congestion with clear discharge. The ingredients include equal parts of Radix Platycodonis, Asarum, Ren Shen (Ginseng), Bai Zhu, Radix Trichosanthis, honey-fried Licorice, Bai Fu Ling, and Chuan Xiong.

    These should be ground into a fine powder. Each dose is two qian (a traditional measure), mixed with one cup of water, two slices of ginger, and two leaves of mint, and then decocted until reduced by a third. For children under three years old, administer four to five doses; for those under five, divide into two doses. For any fever in children, regardless of whether it's caused by a cold or wind-heat, this powder should be given in several doses, and often it proves effective. "The Complete Book of Pediatrics" adds Ma Huang. "A Hundred Questions for Infants and Children" does not include Chuan Xiong.[71p]
    Ephedra and Scutellaria Decoction: For treating children's typhoid with no sweating, headache, fever, and aversion to cold.
    Ingredients: Ephedra without nodes (1 liang), Scutellaria (0.5 liang), Red Peony (0.5 liang), Honey-fried Licorice (0.1 liang), Cinnamon Twig without skin (0.1 liang).
    Preparation: Grind the above into a fine powder. Each dose is 2 qian, mixed with boiling water, to be taken three times daily. It's also used for treating pestilential heat causing slow recovery from lumps, restlessness, and body heat.

    Siberian Ginseng and Scutellaria Decoction: For treating children's wind-cold with sweating, headache, fever, and aversion to cold.
    Ingredients: Siberian Ginseng (0.3 liang), Kudzu Root (0.3 liang), Scutellaria (0.3 liang), Peony (0.3 liang), Honey-fried Licorice (0.15 liang).
    Preparation: Shred to the size of soybeans. Each dose is 2 qian, boiled with 1 medium cup of water until reduced to 6 parts, then strained and taken warm. If there's delayed recovery from smallpox or chickenpox with restlessness and insomnia, add 1.5 qian of Wood Fragrance.

    Sweet Dew Drink for Children: For treating children's stomach-heat with bad breath and loss of appetite, or hunger and reluctance to eat, swollen painful gums with pus and blood, ulcers on the tongue and throat, red eyes and swollen eyelids, with rashes that are both active and inactive.
    Ingredients: Cooked Rehmannia, Raw Rehmannia, Asparagus Tetracentrus (heart removed and baked), Fritillaria Leaves (hairs removed), Bitter Orange Peel (stir-fried and husked), Scutellaria, Dendrobium, Mountain Wormwood, Honey-fried Licorice, all in equal parts.
    Preparation: Grind to a fine powder. Each dose is 2 qian, boiled with 1 cup of water until reduced to 6 parts, strained, to be taken warm after meals and before resting.[72p]
    Double Pills: Treats children's body heat and headaches, poor digestion, abdominal bloating or pain in the heart and abdomen, difficulty with urination and defecation, or recurrent heaviness. If not healed, it can be taken again. For children with steaming symptoms, reduced appetite, uncomfortable breathing, and night crying without sleep, it indicates internal imbalance. This pill is suitable for such cases.

    Ingredients:

    • Half a tael of Guan Sui
    • One qian of Zhu Sha (Cinnabar), ground separately
    • Two and a half taels of Mai Men Dong (Ophiopogon)
    • Four and a half taels of Rui He (Mulberry kernel), remove the kernels and grind
    • Two taels of Mu Li (Oyster shell)
    • One tael of Zhi Gan Cao (Honey-fried Licorice)
    • Sixty pieces of Ba Dou (Croton seed), remove the skin and membrane, grind, then use fresh cloth to squeeze out the oil, sun-dry at noon until white as frost

    Preparation: Grind Mai Men Dong, Gan Cao, Guan Sui, and Mu Li into fine powder, then mix with Ba Dou, Zhu Sha, and Rui He. Pound together with two thousand pestle strikes, add a little honey and pound until very fine, then shape into pills.

    Dosage: For a child of six months, take one pill the size of a sesame seed; for one year, take half a pill divided into two; for two years, one pill the size of a hemp seed, divided into two; for three to four years, take two pills the size of hemp seeds; for five to six years, take two pills the size of big hemp seeds; for seven to eight years, take two pills the size of small beans; for ten years, slightly larger than two small beans.

    Administration: Take at crowing time (dawn). If not effective by sunrise, consume hot congee and take a few doses; it will induce a response, and both the pills will be expelled. If there is severe diarrhea, consume thick boiled cold congee to stop it.[73p]
    Gypsum and Cinnamon Bark Decoction: Treats children with typhoid, not yet febrile, with cough and flushed face.

    Ingredients:

    • Ephedra Decoction
    • Huangqin (Scutellaria) - 1 tael each
    • Honey-fried Licorice - 0.5 tael
    • Gypsum - 0.5 tael
    • Peony - 0.5 tael
    • Cinnamon Heart - 1 fen
    • Apricot Kernels - 10 pieces, skin and tip removed.

    These seven ingredients are to be ground into a powder. Each dose is 2 qian, mixed with 1 medium cup water, adding 3 slices of fresh ginger, and decocted until it reduces to half a cup. Strain and consume. If the child is very small, adjust dosage accordingly.

    Forsythia Drink: Treats all fevers in children.

    Ingredients:

    • Forsythia
    • Siler
    • Licorice
    • Gardenia fruit - equal parts.

    These ingredients are to be pounded and sieved into a powder. Each dose is 2 qian, mixed with 1 cup of water, decocted for 7 minutes, and taken warm.

    Ophiopogon Decoction: Treats children under 100 days with typhoid, nasal bleeding, body heat, and vomiting.

    Ingredients:

    • Ophiopogon - 3 fen
    • Gypsum - 0.5 tael
    • Cold Water Stone - 0.5 tael
    • Honey-fried Licorice - 0.5 tael
    • Cinnamon Heart - 3.5 qian.

    These are to be chopped into pieces the size of broad beans. Each dose is 3 qian, mixed with 1 cup of water, decocted for 7 minutes, and taken warm.

    Five Herbs Ginseng Powder: Treats children with seasonal high fever, cough, and abdominal distension.

    Ingredients:

    • Ginseng - 0.5 tael
    • Licorice - 0.5 tael
    • Honey-fried Ophiopogon - 1 tael, heart removed
    • Fresh Rehmannia - 1.5 tael (if unavailable, use 0.5 tael of dried Rehmannia).

    These are to be grated into pieces the size of broad beans. Each dose is 3 qian, mixed with 1 cup of water, adding half a handful of Clematis root, decocted until it reduces to 7 minutes, strained, and taken warm.

    Eight Herbs Ophiopogon Drink: Treats various fevers in children.[74p]
    Mai Men Dong (3-2 taels), removing the heart, Zhi Gan Cao, and Ren Shen (each 1 fen), Zi Yuan and Sheng Ma (each 2 taels), Bei Mu (1.5 fen). Grind to the size of a soybean. For each dose, take 3 qian, add to 1 cup of water, include half a handful of Mao Gen, and decoct until reduced to 7 parts, strain, then add a little Zhu Li and re-decoct for warm consumption.

    Jujube Leaf Decoction: Treats children with continual heat after five days of Tianxing. Take half a handful of jujube leaves, half a tael of Ma Huang (removing root nodes), 1 he of Dan Chi, and 1 he of chopped 葱白. Combine these with 2 cups of the child’s urine and decoct until reduced to 1 cup. Strain and divide into two doses.

    Cool Barrier Powder: Also known as Lian Qiao Decoction. Used for treating unresolved exterior symptoms of cold damage that have partially entered the interior, or for down syndrome not entirely resolved, or for internal dryness and heat causing irritability and sleeplessness; also for various conditions of adults and children with accumulated heat in their organs, exhibiting symptoms such as irritability, increased thirst, hot face, dizziness, dry lips and throat, swollen tongue, blocked throat, red eyes, nosebleeds, stiff jaws and cheeks, sores in the mouth and on the tongue, thick phlegm not easily expelled, coughing up sticky sputum, restlessness during sleep, talking nonsense or in a frenzied state, damp-heat in the stomach and intestines, constipation or urinary obstruction; applicable to all wind-heat blockages, wind dizziness, sores, and skin conditions; for those with Yangming stomach heat causing rashes with incomplete symptoms; also for those who have mistakenly taken excessive warming medicines or those with severe heat conditions exacerbated by alcohol or severe heat toxins, alongside children's rashes or pox not fully resolved, or those already critically ill with severe heat.[75p]
    Gardenia seeds, forsythia, mint, yellow root, and licorice, each one and a half taels; rhubarb and mirabilite, each half a tael. The above should be ground into a coarse powder. For each tael, add two cups of water, seven pieces of bamboo leaves, and boil until reduced to one cup. Strain, add a little honey, and take after meals; it is also acceptable to decoct with ginger. To clear heat from the six channels, reduce rhubarb and mirabilite, and add balloot, licorice, ginseng, and windbreaker. For treating evil heat in the lung channel with cough and phlegm, add pinellia. For cooling the diaphragm, take it mixed with the Four Substances, in equal parts, which can nourish blood and disperse heat; this is called Double Harmonizing Powder. The Qian family replaces forsythia with fragrant stick and gypsum to create a formula for purging yellow. "Treasury of Prescriptions": Four taels of forsythia, two taels each of mirabilite and yellow root, and the rest one tael each.

    Chaihu and Kudzu Muscle Releasing Decoction: Chaihu, kudzu, yellow root, cinnamon twig, red peony, ginseng, and licorice. Add seven pieces of bamboo leaves and ginger dates as guidance, and decoct to take.

    Adjusting the Original to Nourish the Vessels Powder.[76p]
    Huangqi, Ren Shen, Mai Men Dong, Gan Cao, Wu Wei Zi - these are to be decocted in water and taken.

    Shen Su Decoction
    Ren Shen, Ban Xia, Fu Ling, Gan Cao, Jie Geng, Zhi Ke, Gan Ge, Qian Hu, Mu Xiang, Chen Pi, Su Ye - these are to be simmered with ginger and jujube to be taken.

    Ludou Fen Decoction [from "Secret of Infant Care," same for the following]
    If a child mistakenly takes too much heat-clearing medicine resulting in restlessness, confusion, vomiting, mania, or thirst, it's necessary to first detoxify; this decoction is the main remedy.
    One tael of Ludou Fen, half a tael each of Huang Lian Zhi, Gan Ge, and Sheng Gan Cao, grind these three together. For each dose, take five to ten grams, mixed with warm diluted Dou Chi soup.

    Dou Juan Powder
    If a child is startled and treated with too warm or heat-inducing medicine, there may be lingering heat syndrome or a new heat syndrome after recovery, or a severe reaction resulting in urgent panic. It is important to inquire about the days prior to illness and what medicines were taken. Detoxifying medicines can be administered; none fail to rescue. This powder is the main remedy.
    Big soybean yellow rolls soaked in water until they sprout and are black beans, dried; roast Gan Cao, Guan Zhong, and Ban Lan Gen, each one tael ground together. For each dose, take five to ten grams, decoct and take after filtering.[77p]
    Jade Liquid Pill
    Treats wind obstruction, transforms phlegm to relieve the diaphragm, clears heat and agitation from the head and eyes, and alleviates cough.
    Calcined cold water stone, 2.5 taels; processed pinellia, 1 tael; five qian of burnt alum, together ground into powder, mixed with rice paste the size of millet, taken with ginger soup. For cough caused by wind and cold, take mulberry root soup; for coughing blood, take reed root soup; for persistent cough, take tea soup; for cough that persists, take simmered ginger soup.

    Stomach Ling Pill
    Differentiates yin and yang, reduces tidal heat, stops vomiting and diarrhea, dissipates edema and jaundice, regulates the spleen and stomach, and stops turbid stools, commonly used for children.
    Atractylodes soaked in rice wash, scraped to remove black skin and dried; thick bark stir-fried with ginger juice; aged tangerine peel; white atractylodes, each 5 qian; licorice roasted; cardamom, each 2 qian; poria, alisma, and white poria, each 3 qian; one qian of cinnamon, all ground into powder, mixed with water to form pills the size of millet, taken with roasted rice soup. For vomiting, take simmered ginger soup; to regulate the stomach, take roasted rice soup; for white discharge, take salt soup; for diarrhea, take roasted rice and plantain soup; for jaundice, add 5 qian of yarrow and take light bamboo leaf soup; for tidal heat, take roasted rice and bamboo leaf soup; for edema, simmer long flowing water and take light bamboo leaf and additional dogwood soup; for hernia, take fennel soup.[78p]
    Shen Xiong Wan: Treats children's accumulation of heat in the upper burner, convulsions due to obstruction, red-swollen head and eyes, closed throat, red and profuse urine and stool, as well as phlegm and wheezing. All these conditions are treated. Ingredients include: Da Huang (Rhizoma Rhei) and Huang Qin (Radix Scutellariae) each 1 qian, black Qian Niu Zi (Semen Euphorbiae) ground to powder, and Hua Shi (Talc) each 4 qian, Huang Lian (Rhizoma Coptidis), Chuan Xiong (Rhizoma Chuanxiong), and Bo He (Herba Menthae) each 5 qian. Grind them into a powder, form into pills the size of millet using water, and take with bamboo leaf decoction.

    Bai Du San: Treats children with cold damage, epidemic diseases, wind and dampness, dizziness, limb pain, aversion to cold and strong heat, stiffness in the neck, and eye pain. It also addresses ordinary wind dizziness and fatigue from phlegm, neck pain, as well as coughing and nasal obstruction due to cold. Ingredients include: Chai Hu (Radix Bupleuri) rinsed, Qian Hu (Radix Peucedani), Chuan Xiong, Zhi Ke (Fructus Aurantii) roasted, Qiang Huo (Rhizoma Notopterygii), Chuan Du Huo (Radix Angelicae), Bai Fu Ling (Poria), Jie Geng (Radix Platycodi) roasted, and Ren Shen (Radix Ginseng) each 1 liang; Gan Cao (Radix Glycyrrhizae) 0.5 liang. Grind them into a coarse powder, take 2 qian each time with a decoction of ginger and mint, added with Di Gu Pi (Cortex Lycii) and Tian Ma (Rhizoma Gastrodiae); or, if ground, add Chan Tui (Periostracum Cicadae) and Fang Feng (Radix Ledebouriellae). For treating high fever, add Shao Yao (Radix Paeoniae), Gan Cao, and Huang Qin. If there is no sweating, add Ma Huang (Herba Ephedrae).[79p]
    Four Parts Harmonizing Cool Beverage: Treats children's blood vessels that are blocked and full, internal organs filled with heat, flushed cheeks, excessive thirst, restlessness in the heart, poor sleep, and jerky limbs; also addresses issues caused by irregular nursing, excessive cold or heat, leading to unbalanced blood and qi, gastrointestinal disorders, scant urination, and loose stools; or lingering heat due to consumption; or persistent strong heat wanting to trigger convulsions; treats wind-heat blockages, sores and boils on the head and face, red eyes, throat pain, skin rashes, and all forms of blockages.

    Ingredients: Red Peony, Angelica Sinensis, Licorice, and Rhubarb in equal parts.

    Preparation: Grind and mix. For children over three years old, take two qian (a traditional weight measurement), with one cup of water, boil until reduced to seven parts, to be taken in two doses. For cases of heat-related diarrhea that won't stop, add Areca Nut and prepare Rhubarb with moderation. To support urination, use Red Peony; for cases needing additional measures, add Alisma and Mutong. For deficiency heat, increase Licorice and decrease Rhubarb. If exposed to wind, add Qiang Huo without the joints. For strong symptoms of wind stroke and upward gaze, add Angelica Pubescens, adjusting amounts based on the child's size and condition, keeping a moderate balance of slightly loose stools. Addition of Schizonepeta is permissible.[80p]
    Chai Hu San: This formula is used to treat children with typhoid fever who have no sweating and exhibit exterior symptoms, such as strong fever, headaches, body aches, dry mouth, thirst, reddish urine, constipation, and swollen cheeks with tremors. The ingredients include:

    • Gypsum
    • Huang Qin (Scutellaria)
    • Licorice
    • Chi Shao (Red Peony)
    • Ge Gen (Kudzu)
      Each ingredient is 2.5 qian (a Chinese weight unit).
    • Ma Huang (Ephedra) without stems: 5 liang
    • Chai Hu (Bupleurum): ½ liang

    Grind and mix these together. For a child of three years old, use 2 qian of the mixture, one small cup of water, a small amount of fresh ginger, three inches of green onion, and a pinch of fermented soybean, boil down to six parts, and administer warm.

    Yin Chen Tang: This formula treats fevers with sweating in Yangming disease. It indicates that heat cannot properly manifest as sweat. If there is sweat on the head but none on the body, dryness in the mouth, difficulty urinating, and a need for drinking water, this indicates residual heat inside, leading to possible jaundice. In cases of typhoid fever lasting seven to eight days, if the skin turns orange-yellow, with difficulty urinating and mild abdominal fullness, the herbs are:

    • Fresh Yin Chen: 1 liang
    • Da Huang (Rhubarb): 3.5 qian
    • Zhi Zi (Gardenia): 3 large pieces

    Grind and mix these, using one large bowl of water. First, boil the Yin Chen and reduce it by half; then boil the other two ingredients for eight parts, strain, and take warm. This should be taken three times a day. Urination should improve, resembling the juice of soapwort, with a proper reddish color. This will help reduce body yellowing overnight, with the yellow being expelled through urination. Adjust the dosage as needed according to size.[81p]
    Gardenia and Coptis Decoction: Treats severe fever and jaundice.
    Ingredients: 8 pieces of gardenia, 1 tael of coptis, 0.5 tael of roasted licorice.
    Preparation: Grind and mix these ingredients. Take 2 qian (a traditional unit of weight) with 1 cup of water, decoct for 6 minutes, strain, and take warm.

    Rhinoceros Horn Powder: Treats jaundice in children, turning the whole body yellow.
    Ingredients: 1 tael of rhinoceros horn, 0.5 tael each of Artemisia capillaris, kudzu root, licorice, radish, and gentian. 7.5 qian of limestone.
    Preparation: Grind into a powder and decoct in clear water.

    Kudzu Root Juice: Treats sudden onset of yellow complexion in children, with skin and flesh entirely yellow.
    Preparation: Use juice from kudzu root, mixed with honey to take.

    Forsythia and Red Bean Decoction: Treats febrile disease and jaundice in children.

    Preparation: Grind these ingredients and decoct in clear water.[82p]
    Wheat Sprout Juice
    Crush wheat sprouts to extract juice. Take it for immediate effect.

    Yinchen Wuling Powder
    Mix ten parts Yinchen Decoction and five parts Wuling Powder well. Take one qian with warm water, three times daily.

    Danggui Powder
    To treat children who cry at night due to internal cold and abdominal pain, with a pale face and cold hands, and refuse to nurse. Use this prescription: Licorice, Platycodon, Aged Tangerine Peel, and Danggui, each one qian. Grind to powder, decoct in half a cup of water, and give in small amounts at intervals. If there is also heat pain and continuous crying at night, with a red face and dry lips, and dark red urine, use Sanhuang Pills or Ginseng Decoction.

    Small Banxia Decoction
    To treat jaundice, with urine color unchanged, wanting to relieve, with fullness in the abdomen and shortness of breath. Do not eliminate heat, as removing heat will cause vomiting. Wash Banxia seven times. Take this powdered mixture: three qian each, with one cup of water, a slice of ginger, decoct to seven parts, and take warm.

    Digestive Pills
    Regular consumption can ease the stomach and promote digestion of dairy and food, restoring proper complexion. Use: Roasted Sand, Roasted Aged Tangerine Peel, Stewed Sparganium, Stewed Atractylodes, Fried Shenchifu, Fried Malt, Rice Water soaked overnight and fried, Bitter Orange Peel, Betel Nut, and Black Plum, each half a liang, and Clove two and a half qian. Grind to powder, form into pills the size of mung beans, and take twenty or thirty pills after meals with Perilla Decoction.[83p]
    Xiao Chai Hu Decoction: For treating children's typhoid with alternating fever, Shaoyang sweating, thirst with warmth, fever and aversion to wind, headache and neck stiffness, aching limbs, alternating chills and heat, side pain and ear deafness, vomiting with phlegm, heat stroke, and malaria. Take the following:

    • Ginseng, prepared licorice, each 9 grams
    • Huang Qin (Scutellaria), 6 grams
    • Chai Hu (Bupleurum), 24 grams
    • Ban Xia (Pinellia), dry and roasted after washing in broth seven times, 12.5 grams

    Grind to powder, take 6 grams each time, mixed with a cup of water. Add three slices of fresh ginger and one date, boil to remove residue, and take warm, without time restrictions. Wang Kentang states: I believe if there is wind-heat in the liver and gallbladder, liver fire nodules, alternating fever and chills, afternoon fever, less desire to eat or drink, possible anger with bitter mouth and ear deafness, coughing or side pain with abdominal fullness, difficult urination, possible diarrhea with sour bitter fluid, or spasms in limbs, lip and eye twitches, and if the nurse has previous symptoms causing the child to be affected, it is advisable to take this.

    Ge Gen Huang Lian Huang Qin Decoction: For treating Taiyang disease with Gui Zhi presentation, if purging leads to continuing diarrhea and a rapid pulse, the evil has not been resolved yet, and if wheezing with sweating occurs. Use the following:

    • Ge Gen (Pueraria), 120 grams
    • Huang Qin, Huang Lian, each 22.5 grams
    • Licorice, 25 grams

    Grind to powder, take 9 grams each time, mixed with a cup of water, boil to 70% of the original amount, remove residue and adjust dosage. If wheezing is severe, add Teng Feng Zi (Clematis).[84p]
    San Huang Wan is used to treat children's three jiao stagnation heat, excessive thirst with desire to drink, red and swollen eyes, sores on the mouth and tongue, irritability of the heart, lack of appetite, constipation or difficult urination, excess heat in the five organs, and possibly sanguine conditions such as fresh blood in stools or hot sores and boils. The ingredients are: 10 taels each of Huanglian, Huangqin, and Da Huang (boiled). Grind these into powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of tung seeds. Take 30 pills each time, to be swallowed with warm water. If there is significant fullness and heat in the organs, increase the dosage.

    Zhuye Tang is used to treat children suffering from cold damage with thirst, weakness, and shortness of breath, with reversed Qi leading to nausea, and heat in the limbs. The ingredients are 2 taels of Shigao, 4 qian of Banxia, 2 qian each of Ren Shen and Zhi Gan Cao, and 6 qian of Mai Men Dong (with the heart removed). Grind these to powder; each time, take 2 qian with a cup of water, adding 4 pieces each of fresh bamboo leaves and ginger, along with 70 grains of polished rice and simmer. If nausea occurs, add fresh ginger and bamboo leaves.

    Xiangru Drink is used to treat heat stroke in summer; it is effective as soon as it is taken.

    The ingredients are: 1 tael of Xiangru, half a tael each of fried Bai Bian Dou, and thick bark ginger. Grind them to powder; each time, take 3 qian with a cup of water, and simmer with three pieces of fresh ginger. In one formula, add Huanglian to treat diarrhea and dysentery. In another formula, add Xuanshu and Xiangsu powder to treat cholera with vomiting and diarrhea, and symptoms caused by heat exposure in summer.[85p]
    Cheqianzi Powder: This is used to treat heat in the summer months, as well as cholera symptoms like vomiting and diarrhea. Equal parts of Bai Fu Ling, Zhu Ling, Xiang Ru, and Cheqianzi, with Ren Shen reduced by half. Grind these into a powder. For each dose of one qian, mix with lampwick tea. If there is abdominal pain, add Shao Yao; if diarrhea persists, add Shi Lian flesh.

    Huanglian Jiedu Decoction: This is for treating severe heat with restlessness, thirst, and fainting; it revives upon swallowing. The ingredients are: three qian of Huang Lian, five qian of Huang Bo, four pieces of split Zhi Zi, and one liang of Huang Qin. Prepare by grinding finely. For each dose of three qian, mix with one cup of water, boil down to six parts, strain, and take warm.

    Yulu Powder: This treats discomfort, restlessness, red cheeks, dry throat, body heat, headache, along with heat stroke and thirst, dullness, and difficulty urinating. If shock enters the kidneys, and teeth grinding occurs in dreams, add Jin Zhu Powder and take with mint tea. Ingredients include: two liang each of Han Shui Shi and Shi Gao, water-refined; three qian of Gan Cao. Grind into a powder, with each dose being half a qian, to be taken with Mai Men Dong decoction as preferred. If adding Chen Sha and gold leaf, it is called Tao Hong Powder, also for acute shock. Adding Zhi Zi Ren makes it Jin Lian Powder. Adding half a liang of Hua Shi forms Yu Zhen Powder. According to Tang’s teachings: This formula treats children suffering from autumn and summer heat, commonly showing signs of heat, with yellow sputum, warm forehead, five hearts burning, scanty red urination, or dry vomiting without substance; it is advisable to take Xiang Ru drink or Yulu Powder, mixed with ginger juice and white broth. Just using ginger juice alone can halt the situation.[86p]
    Da Chi San - Treats internal unease and excessive heat resulting from a deficiency of the heart.

    Ingredients:

    • Raw Rehmannia
    • Licorice
    • Muxiang
      Each in equal parts.

    Preparation: Cut and boil with bamboo leaves. Add Huangqin, Chishaoyao, Qianghuo, and light heart to decoct and take.

    Zhibao Dan - Treats confusion of spirit and excessive heart agitation resulting in wind.

    Ingredients:

    • Raw Rhinoceros Horn powder
    • Tortoise Shell powder
    • Amber, ground
    • Cinnabar, finely ground and filtered in water
    • Realgar, finely ground and filtered in water, each one tael
    • Fifty pieces of gold leaf, half as wrapping
    • Fifty pieces of silver leaf, ground
    • One fen of white lead, ground
    • One qian of musk, ground
    • One and a half taels of benzoin, powdered

    Preparation: Use a non-ashy wine to filter out sand and stones, taking about one tael. Slowly simmer to create a paste. Use half a tael of Niu Huang, and blend the finely crushed rhinoceros horn and tortoise shell with the other herbs to make a uniform mixture. Cook the benzoin paste in heavy soup until it congeals, then mold into pills. If too dry, add a bit of warmed honey. Store in a sealed container, shaping each pill to the size of a tongzi (Chinese sweet). For a two-year-old, give two pills, dissolved in ginseng soup. Adjust the dosage according to size.

    This also treats adults who are suddenly speechless due to evil spirits, poisoning from various substances, excessive heat, dark wind, postpartum blood collapse, and retained dead fetus. Use a small amount of children’s urine and three to five drops of fresh ginger juice, warming them together. Dissolve five pills to achieve immediate effect.[87p]
    Amber powder treats restlessness and dispels wind and phlegm.

    Ingredients:

    • 1.5 qian of realgar
    • Amber
    • Cattle bile
    • Fried silkworms (remove the silk)
    • Noxious star (Nanjing star) soaked in water: three days in summer, five days in spring and autumn, and seven days in winter, best processed with cattle bile
    • Full scorpion (to remove toxins)
    • White attached herb
    • Earth vermilion
    • Gastrodia
    • Frankincense
    • Cicada molting, each one qian
    • Musk, five fen
    • A single character of powdered brain

    These should be ground together into a fine powder and taken with a mint decoction. For lingering fright, add white attached herb.

    Detox pill is used for children with accumulated heat in the five organs, toxic energy attacking upward, chest discomfort, sore throat, red eyes with swelling, fever in the head and face, dryness of lips and mouth, sores on both cheeks, mental confusion, heart palpitations and agitation, restlessness in sitting and lying; also for those suffering from heat injury after exposure, with red face and hot body, irritability and thirst, and inability to eat.

    Ingredients include:

    • 8 liang of cold water stone
    • 8 liang of gypsum
    • Indigo[88p]
      Crush the above into a fine powder, mix well with indigo to make a paste. Prepare seven steamed cakes and a large round ball the size of a gourd with water. Take one ball after meals, either with newly drawn water or finely chewed with ginger tea. It is effective for toxins; it is also suitable for children experiencing fright and fever, with phlegm and stagnation, agitation in the heart and chest, flushed cheeks, excessive thirst, and instability in sitting or lying. For every three years of a child’s age, give half a grain, adjusting the amount according to size.

    Seven Herbs Huanglian Decoction: Treats summer heat-exhaustion, with painful and feverish limbs, causing agitation, nausea, and a sensation of fullness akin to calamity, as cold and heat clash, leading to restlessness.

    Ingredients: Huanglian (Coptis), Fuling (Poria), and Shaoyao (Paeonia) each seven and a half qian; Huangqin (Scutellaria), Gancao (Licorice), and Ganjiang (Dried Ginger) each one liang; three he of wheat. Chop and grind, then boil in plain water. To stop diarrhea, add half a liang of Zhishi (bitter orange).

    Gold Foil Tranquil Heart Pill: Treats palpitations due to phlegm accumulation in the upper abdomen, causing restlessness and unease.

    Ingredients: One liang of Zhusha (Cinnabar); half a liang each of Baifuling (White Poria), Ren Shen (Ginseng), and Gancao; one and a half liang of Shanyao (Chinese Yam); one qian of brain powder; half a qian of Yashao (Calomel); five fen of musk; two and a half qian of Ziheche (Cordyceps); boiled black beans; twelve sheets of gold foil.

    Grind the above into a powder, form into pills with honey, making fifty pills from two and a half liang. Each pill is wrapped in gold foil; take one pill with mint tea, dissolve in the mouth if preferred. Regular use at night calms the heart, stabilizes the spirit, dispels evil heat, cools the throat, and stops fright and crying.[89p]
    Pear Juice Drink is used to treat damp heat, warm heat, guard heat, miasma heat, occurring every two days or three days; accumulated heat, spleen heat, fullness heat, stomach heat, obsession heat, malaria heat, evil heat, cold heat, spleen malaria, ghost malaria at night, single malaria and solitary heat.

    Soak Qinghao in child’s urine for one day and dry in the sun; add Chaihu, ginseng, pan-fried Huangqin, Qianhu, Qin Jiao, and roasted licorice, all in equal parts. Chew and swallow, with each dose suitable for a year and a half, for two years use one penny, mixed with a small cup of water, cooked with fresh lotus root, fresh pear, mint, and raw Rehmannia, boil until half, strain, and take on an empty stomach before eating.

    Da Chaihu Decoction treats cold damage lasting over ten days, with evil qi accumulating inside, alternating cold and heat, constipation, abdominal fullness and pain, delirium, hard sensations in the heart, and poor appetite; or if there has been no bowel movement for five or six days, with pain around the navel and intermittent irritability; after sweating like malaria, evening fever and if the organs are firm and strong, it can be taken.

    Chaihu, eight qian; Huangqin, red peony, Zhishi (bitter orange), each three qian; Banxia prepared in decoction seven times, sliced and dried, one and a half qian. Grind this into powder, brew with ginger and dates, and adjust the dosage as needed. To promote a bowel movement, add half a tael of Da Huang.[90p]
    Da Chengqi Decoction treats rigidity and distension in the chest, locked jaws, severe heat and thirst, and constipation.

    • Ingredients:

      • Sodium sulfate 15 grams

      • Immature bitter orange 30 grams

    Digu Pi Powder treats internal heat from deficiency, as well as febrile diseases with lingering heat.

    • Ingredients:
      • Anemarrhena and Digu Pi (earth bone cortex) each 30 grams, stir-fried
      • Bupleurum, raw licorice, ginseng, and poria each 15 grams
        Soak half summer tuber in water for seven times, slice and sun-dry, 9 grams.
        Mix and grind, boil with ginger water, taking each dose of 9 grams. The "Complete Baby Formulas" adds gentian, named Gentian Decoction. For shock-related fever, add cicada slough, gastrodia, and scute. According to Haicang, Digu Pi Powder is a modification of Xiao Chai Hu Decoction. For spontaneous sweating, use Digu Pi Powder; for no sweating, use Chai Hu Decoction or San Huang Decoction, as utilized by Zhongjing. Qian Shi modified these into various forms, based on ancient methods.[91p]
        Rhino Horn Decoction: Treats pediatric bone steaming, tidal fever, night sweats, and emaciation.

    Tortoise Shell Decoction: Treats pediatric bone steaming, tidal fever, night sweats, cough, thirst, agitation, pale complexion, and emaciation.

    Ingredients:

    Lingxi Decoction: Treats pediatric bone steaming, tidal fever, night sweats, cough, lack of appetite, excessive thirst, pale complexion, emaciation, abdominal urgency, and coarse breath; effective for residual heat.

    Shengxi Decoction: Treats children with bone steaming and muscle wasting, red cheeks, dry mouth, tidal fever in the afternoon, night sweats, irritability in the palms and soles, fatigue in the limbs, and despite a good appetite, no flesh is gained; also used after major illnesses when residual toxins remain; or after typhoid fever when consuming mutton, the body heat persists.

    Ingredients:

    • Ge Guo Pi (Earth Bone Skin)
    • Qin Jiao (Gentiana)
    • Ren Shen (Ginseng)
    • Xi Jiao (Rhinoceros Horn, powdered)
    • Da Huang (Rhubarb) - steamed
    • Mai Dong (Ophiopogon)
    • Zhi Ke (Bitter Orange Peel)
    • Chai Hu (Bupleurum)
    • Bai Fu Ling (White Poria)
    • Chi Shao (Red Peony)
    • Sang Bai Pi (Mulberry Root Bark)
    • Bie Jia (Tortoise Shell, prepared)

    Each ingredient: one liang (50 grams).

    Method: Grind and use 2 qian (6 grams) with one cup of water, add a little Qing Hao (Artemisia) and decoct. Take warm after meals. For children, divide into two doses. In "Standards," add Huang Qi (Astragalus) and Wu Mei (Black Plum).

    Qinghao Powder: Treats female children with muscle wasting and tidal fever.

    Ingredients:

    • Qinghao (Artemisia) - 3 qian (9 grams)
    • Sheng Gan Cao (Fresh Licorice) - 1 cun (about 3.3 cm)
    • Wu Mei (Black Plum) - 1 piece, crushed
    • Xiao Mai (Wheat) - 50 grains

    Method: Chew the above, use one bowl of river water, decoct until reduced to one-third, then strain and drink.

    Chai Hu Powder: Treats children with bone steaming, tidal fever, and weakness with a pale complexion.

    Ingredients:

    • Chai Hu (Bupleurum)
    • Ge Guo Pi (Earth Bone Skin)
    • Gan Cao (Licorice - roasted)

    Each ingredient: half a liang (25 grams).

    Method: Grind, use one cup of water, for each dose use 2 qian (6 grams), decoct to seven tenths, strain and drink at any time.[93p]
    Liqing Decoction treats disharmony of the spleen and stomach, obstruction ascending, pain in the heart and abdomen, phlegm counterflow nausea and vomiting, vexation and fullness in the chest, blockage and inability to pass, diminished appetite, shortness of breath, and weakness. It warms the middle, expels water, stops sweating, and eliminates dampness. It addresses diarrhea, separation of water and grains, and rumbling in the abdomen. It also addresses the cold from febrile disease, internal cold and external heat, as well as cholera with vomiting and diarrhea, and coldness in the hands and feet.

    Ingredients:

    • Ginseng
    • Atractylodes macrocephala
    • Dried ginger (processed), each in equal parts
    • Licorice (processed), halved

    The right ingredients should be finely powdered. For each dose, take two qian, boil with one cup of water, three slices of ginger, and one jujube. For abdominal pain, add ginseng; for thirst, reduce Atractylodes; for excess cold, add dried ginger and Aconite; for severe vomiting, remove Atractylodes and add fresh ginger; for excessive diarrhea, still use Atractylodes; for palpitations, add Poria. If the limbs are cold, with diarrhea and cramps, you can add Aconite, making it into powdered honey pills, called Liqing Pills. This treats cold in the liver and gallbladder, worms ascending to the diaphragm, expelling long worms, and cold weak stomach, hence Liqing Pills should be taken first. You may add Poria and Bitter Orange.

    Four Gentlemen Decoction treats deficiency of Ying and Wei qi, weakness of the organs, bloating in the heart and abdomen, complete loss of appetite, intestinal rumbling and diarrhea, nausea and counterflow vomiting.

    Ingredients:

    • Ginseng
    • Poria
    • Fresh licorice
    • Atractylodes macrocephala, each in equal parts

    The ingredients should be powdered. For each dose, take two qian, boil with one cup of water until reduced to seven parts, and take orally without regard to time. Add a pinch of salt, and take with warm water. It warms the spleen and stomach, promotes digestion, and dispels cold evils and obstructing vapors.[94p]
    Wuling Powder is used to treat febrile diseases of the six meridians when the condition has not been resolved at both the surface and interior. Symptoms include headache, fever, dry mouth and throat, severe thirst with a desire to drink, possible vomiting upon drinking water, difficulty urinating, sweating indicating resolution of the exterior but with persistent thirst. It also treats cholera with vomiting and diarrhea, and thirst due to dryness.

    Ingredients:

    • 2.5 taels of Alisma Rhizome
    • 1.5 taels each of Polyporus, Atractylodes, and Poria
    • 1 tael of Cinnamon

    Grind the above into a powder. Take 2 qian with hot soup at any time. Drink plenty of hot soup; if sweating occurs, one will recover. It also treats damp-heat internally causing jaundice; take a strong decoction of Gardenia before meals. For jaundice with thirst and heat, or thirst due to summer heat, it can also be taken with water. For children, add a small amount of Atractylodes powder. If there is deficiency, add a small amount of Astragalus and Ginseng powder.

    Baihu Decoction is used to treat febrile diseases with profuse sweating where the exterior is already resolved, but there is great restlessness in the chest and severe thirst. It is also appropriate for conditions 7-8 days after vomiting or diarrhea where poison has not been resolved, with heat trapped internally, signs of exterior and interior heat, frequent aversion to wind, great thirst, dry tongue, and a desire to drink multiple liters. It is also used for summer heatstroke with sweating and chills, body heat, and thirst.

    Ingredients:

    • 3 taels of Anemarrhena
    • 1 tael of roasted Licorice
    • 8 taels of Gypsum, ground separately
    • 3.5 sheng of polished rice

    Crush the above; take 3 qian with 1 cup of water, decoct until six parts remain, cooking the rice until done, then strain and take while warm. In accordance with the "Shenghui Formula," add dried Kudzu.[95p]
    Chai Ling San: For treating children with hidden heat in the abdomen, warming and invigorating. Ingredients: 7.5 grams of Chai Hu, removing the heart of Mai Men Dong, 0.5 liang each of Ren Shen, Chi Fu Ling, and Gan Cao, and 1 liang of Huang Qin. Grind these ingredients into a powder. For each dose, take 2 qian, mix with a cup of water, add a pinch of wheat and three bamboo leaves, decoct for five minutes, strain, and serve warm, adjusting the amount based on the child's size.

    Er Huang Xi Jiao San: For treating children with a warm and strong body, restless spirit, and retained heat in the large intestine. Ingredients: Shavings of xi jiao, Da Huang soaked in wine and steamed, Diao Teng, Zhi Zi, Sheng Gan Cao, and Huang Qin, each 0.5 liang. Grind these into a powder. For each dose, take 0.5 liang, adjusting based on the child's size, and mix with hot water to consume.

    Niu Huang San: For treating children who are warm and strong, and constantly feel hot, or have alternating cold and heat. Ingredients: Ground Niu Huang and Sheng Gan Cao, each 0.5 liang; Chai Hu without sprout, Zhi Zi (lightly roasted), Long Dan Cao, and Huang Qin, each 2.5 qian. Grind these into a powder. For each dose, take 0.5 liang, mixing with Jin Yin Bo He soup, to be taken as needed.[96p]
    Huanglong Decoction: Used for treating persistent fevers due to typhoid, or alternating cold and heat. Ingredients: Chaihu (Bupleurum) 5 qian, Huangqin (Scutellaria) 2 qian, Sheng Gancao (Raw Licorice) 2 qian, Chishao (Red Peony Root) 3 qian. Prepare by grinding and taking 2 qian with a slice of ginger and one jujube. Boil in one cup of water until reduced to a fifth, strain, and take warm, at no specific times.

    Niuhuang Ointment: Treats children with sudden fright, convulsions of hands and feet, red face and lips, phlegm in the throat with a rattling sound, whole body and forehead feeling hot, unresponsive to calling, or spasms only in the left hand or foot, or in the right hand or foot, or tremors in the lips, mouth, eyes, and nose. This condition often presents with a tight, swollen abdomen; if heat is extreme, it may lead to prolonged accumulation of phlegm and sudden onset from external wind. This condition strictly prohibits acupuncture, as it would be a mistake. For this illness, it is essential to recognize the aforementioned symptoms and take this medicine.

    Ingredients: 49 scorpion tails, 1.5 qian of shelled Badu (Croton) seeds, half a character of Meihua (Plum Flower) slice, 2 qian of finely ground Cinnabar, a character of Musk, 3 qian of Yujin (Curcuma), boiled in soap pod water, and a small amount of Niuhuang (Cattle Gallstone). Grind these six ingredients into a powder. When encountering symptoms as described, for children about one and a half years old, use one character for those three to four years old. Also consider the child's body condition (whether fat or thin) and the severity of the illness to adjust dosage.[97p]
    Dissolve one or two parts of honey water and take it down, or peppermint soup is also acceptable. After taking the medicine for a long time, suppress phlegm and disperse the wind, which should be excreted in two or three streams; if it comes out like egg white, it is the desired effect. If there is a buildup of phlegm in the chest cavity causing fullness and discomfort, this medicine should induce vomiting of wind and phlegm, which is also beneficial. After taking the medicine, whether through vomiting or diarrhea, the hands and feet are stable, the throat is silent, the forehead and abdomen gradually cool down, the eyes do not roll back, the patient is aware of their surroundings, and the face is slightly red, but there may be occasional warmth and a stirring sensation from wind, indicating heat has not yet fully subsided. Then, continue with three doses of Baoshou San and one or two doses of Jinfensan, which can be taken again in the morning. These remedies harmonize qi and nourish deficiency, especially if taken with milk. Take Baizhu San once in the morning. After taking these few remedies, if the abdomen feels slightly warm until night and no milk or food is ingested, it is advisable to take a dose of Kuanre San on an empty stomach to mildly expel residual heat and wind phlegm from the abdomen. If there is an ailment and the medicine has slight effects, avoid exposure to wind for two days. Additionally, there is a prescription that includes two qian of powdered frost, known as Zhu Sha Gao.[98p]
    Antelope Horn Decoction: Treats all types of sudden shocks and strong fever.
    Ingredients: Antelope horn shavings, cicada molting, Poria, Ophiopogon, Bupleurum, and Rehmannia root, each one qian; Scutellaria and honey-fried licorice, each five fen. Grind and mix these ingredients. Take two qian per dose, boiled with ginger and dates.

    Gardenia Seed Decoction for Thirst: Treats yang toxin, cold damage with strong fever, joint pain, and unresolved heat after a bowel movement.
    Ingredients: Gardenia seeds, red peony, isatis, Anemarrhena, Bupleurum, each one liang; half liang of licorice; peeled apricot kernels (double kernels), lightly fried until slightly yellow; and each two liang of bulbus peucedani, Scutellaria, and gypsum. Grind and mix these ingredients. Take three qian per dose, boil with one cup of water and three slices of ginger for six minutes, strain, and take warm at any time.

    Forsythia Decoction: Treats rashes with strong fever, urinary obstruction, various sores and boils, and dan-disease.
    Ingredients: Forsythia, cornflower, schizonepeta, akebia, red peony, angelica, saposhnikovia, Bupleurum, talcum, cicada molting, and honey-fried licorice, each one qian; and gardenia and Scutellaria, each five fen. Grind finely. Take one qian per dose, with an additional decoction of lithospermum, warm. For severe heat, add rhubarb. Detailed adjustments according to symptoms are advisable.[99p]
    Longdan Decoction treats fetal fright and excess internal energy leading to fever during the month. It can be used for umbilical wind, mouth convulsions, and severe heat. It treats infants born from the abdomen, with strong and full blood vessels, experiencing chills and fever, tense limbs, and severe vomiting. If they can nurse but have undigested food causing strong heat and lingering effects, or if afflicted by ghostly influences, it is effective for all convulsions and seizures. Children under ten years of age can take it. For infants born from the abdomen, Longdan Decoction is essential. For older children, dosage varies accordingly. If there is known obstruction or excess gas, ginseng and angelica can be added in amounts equivalent to Longdan. For a baby of a hundred days, add three grams; for two hundred days, add six grams; for one year, add fifteen grams.

    Ingredients: Six qian each of Longdan, Tianma, Chaihu, Huangqin, Jiegeng, Shaoyao, Fuling, and raw licorice; two dried beetles, wings removed and roasted; one liang of dahuang, decocted.

    Prepare by grinding and mixing, using one liter of water to boil down to five portions for dosage. The amount of water should be adjusted based on the drug's efficacy. For an infant born from one to seven days, divide into three doses; for eight to fifteen days, divide one and a half doses into three. Gradually increase the dosage and stop upon successful bowel movement. Do not take again. From the "Direct Reference Formula," take one qian each time, decocted with jujube. Alternatively, you can add ficaria or ophiopogon to guide away heart heat, reduce Huangqin by half, or omit the beetles if desired.[100p]
    Zishuang Pill is used to treat food accumulation and is also a remedy for typhoid fever. It addresses issues such as irregularities in breastfeeding, stagnation leading to indigestion, bloating and fullness in the stomach and abdomen, nausea and vomiting, irregular bowel movements, and reduced milk and food intake. Additionally, it treats typhoid fever with excessive heat, stools with a sour odor, and indigestion; it is suitable for cases where sweating has occurred but body heat does not subside; for persistent heat and steaming that doesn't resolve for days; or for convulsions triggered by food, with a pattern of cold followed by heat.

    To prepare it, use one tael of calcined realgar and vinegar steeped seven times, one tael of red ochre, fifty apricot kernels (peeled, roasted), and thirty cowbane seeds (peeled and roasted in oil). First, grind the apricot kernels and cowbane seeds in a mortar until it becomes a paste, then mix in the powdered realgar and red ochre. Form the mixture into small pills, about the size of a grain of millet. For a one-year-old, five pills can be taken with rice water; for an infant one to two hundred days old, three pills are appropriate. Dosages should be adjusted based on the child's body condition, with a mild purging effect as a standard. Generally, this remedy can be treated similarly to typhoid fever, as it addresses both conditions. It is primarily a purgative for food accumulation, with dosage adjusted according to the patient’s condition.[101p]
