    其潮热发歇有时，惊热颠叫恍惚，夜热夕发旦止，余热寒邪未尽，食热肚腹先发，疳热骨蒸盗汗，壮热一向不止，烦热心躁不安，积热颊赤口疮，风热汗出身热，虚热困倦少力，客热来去不定，痰热涎嗽饮水，寒热发如疟状，血热辰已发热，疮疹热耳鼻尖冷。诸证得之，各有所归，其间或有三两证交互者，宜随其轻重而处治之。　　小儿之热，有肝心脾肺肾五脏之不同，气实温壮四者之不一，及表里血气阴阳浮陷，与夫风湿痰食，各当详之。心热者额上先赤，心烦心痛，掌中热而哕，或壮热饮水，巳午时益甚。肝热者，左颊先赤，便难转筋，寻衣捻物，多怒多惊，四肢困倦，寅卯时益甚。脾热者，鼻上先赤，怠惰嗜卧，身热饮水，遇夜益甚。肺热者，右颊先赤，手掐眉目，喘嗽，寒热饮水，日西热甚。肾热者，颏下先赤，两足热甚，骨苏苏如虫蚀，热甚不能起床，夜间益甚。[30p]

    The heat from the tidal fluctuations comes and goes at times, with alarming heat causing delirium. Nighttime heat arises in the evening and subsides by dawn, but residual heat and cold pathogens persist. When hot food is consumed, it first affects the stomach and abdomen, leading to heat and bone steaming, causing night sweats. Continuous strong heat does not subside, resulting in agitation and anxiety. Accumulated heat causes flushed cheeks and mouth sores; wind heat leads to sweating and body heat. Deficient heat results in fatigue and weakness, while guest heat fluctuates. Phlegm heat causes coughing and thirst, with chills alternating like malaria. Blood heat may lead to fever and eventually to ear and nose coldness with sores and rashes. Each symptom manifests distinctly, though some may overlap; treatment should be adjusted according to severity.

    In children, heat varies among the five organs: liver, heart, spleen, lung, and kidney. There are differences in Qi, whether it is abundant or weak, and distinctions in the exterior, interior, blood, Qi, Yin, and Yang, as well as the presence of wind, dampness, phlegm, and food issues that should be examined in detail.

    For heart heat, the forehead first turns red, accompanied by restlessness and heart pain, with palms feeling hot, leading to drinking more water, especially aggravated during the hours of Si (9-11 AM) and Wu (11 AM-1 PM). For liver heat, the left cheek first turns red, resulting in constipation, muscle cramps, increased anger and fright, fatigue in the limbs, worsening between Yin (3-5 AM) and Yang (5-7 AM). For spleen heat, redness appears on the nose first, causing lethargy, a desire for sleep, increased body heat, and worsened symptoms at night. For lung heat, the right cheek first turns red, causing facial twitching, wheezing, and alternating chills and fever, markedly worse in the late afternoon. For kidney heat, the area below the chin turns red first, with significant heat in the feet, and a sensation of worms gnawing at the bones, becoming unable to rise from bed, worsening at night.[30p]

    仍当辨其虚实：实则面赤气粗，口燥唇肿，作渴饮冷，大小便难，或掀衣露体，烦啼暴叫，伸体而卧，睡不露睛，手足指热，宜用表下；虚则面色青白，恍惚神缓，口中虚冷，嘘气软弱，喜热恶寒，泄泻多尿，或乍凉乍温，怫郁惊惕，上盛下泄，夜则虚汗，屈体而卧，睡而露睛，手足指冷，宜用调补。壮热者，肢体大热，热不已则发惊癎。温热者，肢体微热，热不已则发惊搐。阴虚则内热，阳盛则外热。[31p]

    One must still discern between true and false conditions: If true, the face will be flushed and breathing labored; the mouth will be dry, lips swollen, craving cold drinks, with difficult urination and defecation. There may be exposure of the body, restlessness and loud cries, stretching out to lie down, unable to keep the eyes closed while sleeping, with hot hands and feet; in this case, the exterior should be treated. If false, the complexion will be pale and ashen, with a dazed mind and weak spirit; the mouth cold, breath weak; a preference for warmth and aversion to cold, with frequent diarrhea and urination, sometimes feeling alternating hot and cold, tension and vigilance, with a raging upper body and draining lower body. At night, there will be profuse sweating, lying curled up, eyes exposed during sleep, and cold hands and feet; in this case, nourishment and tonics should be used. In cases of strong heat, the limbs will be very hot, and if the heat persists, it may provoke convulsions. In cases of mild heat, the limbs will be slightly warm, and if the heat continues, it may provoke spasms. Yin deficiency leads to internal heat, while excess Yang leads to external heat.[31p]

    以手轻扪之则热，重按之不热，此皮毛血脉之热，热在表也；重按之筋骨之分则热，轻手则不热，此筋骨之热，热在里也；不轻不重按之而热，此肌肉之热，热在表里之间也。以虚实分属表里而言之：壮热恶风寒，为元气不充，表之虚热也；壮热不恶风寒，为外邪所客，表之实热也；壮热饮汤，为津液短少，里之虚热也；壮热饮水，为内火销烁，里之实热也。若夫内外皆热，则喘而渴，齿干烦冤，腹满四肢热，逢风寒如炙于火，能冬不能夏，是皆阳盛阴虚也。脉尺寸俱满为重实，尺寸俱弱为重虚。[32p]

    When lightly touched, it feels hot, but pressing down firmly does not elicit heat; this is the heat of the skin and superficial blood vessels, existing on the surface. When pressed firmly at the tendons and bones, it feels hot, but lightly touching does not evoke heat; this is the heat of the tendons and bones, existing internally. When pressed with moderate pressure and heat is felt, this is the heat of the muscles, located between the superficial and the internal layers.

    In terms of distinguishing between excess and deficiency, we say: strong heat that dislikes wind and cold indicates insufficient vital energy, a superficial deficiency of heat; strong heat that does not dislike wind and cold indicates the presence of an external pathogen, a superficial excess of heat; strong heat accompanied by drinking broth indicates a deficiency of fluids, an internal deficiency of heat; strong heat with water drinking indicates internal fire being consumed, an internal excess of heat.

    If there is heat both internally and externally, then one experiences wheezing and thirst, dry teeth and irritation, a distended abdomen and hot limbs, feeling like being scorched by fire when exposed to wind and cold, unable to tolerate winter but not summer; this all reflects an excess of yang and a deficiency of yin. When both pulse positions are full, this is a condition of strong excess; when both pulse positions are weak, this is a condition of strong deficiency.[32p]

    脉洪大或缓而滑，或数而鼓，此热盛拒阴，虽形证似寒，实非寒也；热而脉数，按之不鼓，此寒盛格阳，虽形证似热，实非热也。发热恶热，大渴不止，烦躁肌热，不欲近衣，其脉洪大，按之无力，或兼目痛鼻干者，此血虚发躁也，当补其血；如不能食而热自汗者，气虚也，当补其气。仲景论内外不足，发热自汗之证，禁不可发汗。如饮食劳役，虽病发热误发其汗，则表必虚也。[33p]

    The pulse is either large and forceful, or it is weak and slippery; it may be rapid and strong, which indicates an excess of heat resisting the yin. Although the symptoms may appear cold, they are not truly cold. If the pulse is rapid yet weak upon pressure, this indicates an excess of cold overcoming the yang. Although the symptoms may seem热, in reality, they are not hot.

    Symptoms include fever, aversion to heat, persistent thirst, agitation, hot skin, and a dislike of clothing. The pulse is large and weak under pressure; if accompanied by eye pain and dry nose, this indicates blood deficiency leading to restlessness, and one should nourish the blood.

    If there is an inability to eat and spontaneous sweating occurs, this indicates qi deficiency and one should replenish the qi. Zhang Zhongjing discusses the insufficiency of both internal and external factors, noting that for symptoms of fever with spontaneous sweating, one should avoid inducing sweating.

    If there is fever due to dietary indiscretion or labor, mistakenly inducing sweating can lead to a deficiency in the exterior.[33p]

    身热而汗出者，风也；发热身疼而身重黄者，湿也；增寒发热恶风，自汗脉浮胸痞者，痰也；发热头痛脉数者，食也。寸口脉数，为阳不足，阴气上入阳中。则恶寒；尺脉弱为阴不足，阳气下入阴中，则发热；阴阳不归其分，则寒热交争也。昼则安静，夜则发热烦躁，是阳气下陷入阴中也；昼则发热烦躁，夜则安静，是重阳无阴也，当急泻其阳，峻补其阴。至若身热脉弦，数战栗而不恶寒者，瘅疟也；发热恶寒脉浮数者，温病也。若四肢发热，口舌咽干，是火热乘土位，湿热相合，故烦躁闷乱也；若身体沉重，走注疼痛，乃湿热相搏，风热郁而不得伸也。
    　　　　　五脏热

    　　肝热，手寻衣领，及乱捻物，泻青丸主之。　　壮热，饮水喘闷，泻白散主之。[34p]

    Those who have a fever and sweat experience wind; those with fever, body pain, and a heavy yellow body experience dampness; those with increased chills, fever, sensitivity to wind, spontaneous sweating, floating pulse, and chest oppression experience phlegm; those with fever, headaches, and rapid pulse experience food issues. A rapid pulse at the inch signifies insufficient yang, with yin energy rising into the yang; thus it leads to aversion to cold. A weak pulse at the cubit indicates insufficient yin, with yang energy descending into yin, resulting in fever; when yin and yang do not return to their proper balance, there is a struggle between cold and heat. If one is quiet during the day but experiences fever and restlessness at night, it indicates that yang energy has sunk into yin; if one experiences fever and restlessness during the day but is quiet at night, it indicates an abundance of yang without yin, and yang must be urgently purged while yin is strongly replenished. If there is body heat, a tense pulse, trembling, and no aversion to cold, it indicates damp malaria; if there is fever, aversion to cold, and a floating rapid pulse, it indicates a warm disease. If the limbs are hot, and the mouth, tongue, and throat are dry, it indicates fire heat overwhelming the earth element, resulting in combined heat and dampness, hence the restlessness and confusion; if the body feels heavy, with swelling and pain, this results from heat and dampness clashing, as wind heat becomes blocked and cannot be released.

    Heat in the Five Organs

    Liver heat: When one seeks their collar or fidgets, administer Qingwan.
    Strong heat: If one drinks water and feels short of breath, administer Baisan.[34p]

    　　肝热者，左颊先赤，便难转筋，多怒多惊，四肢困倦，寅卯时益甚，宜泻青丸、柴胡饮子。　　心热，视其睡口中气温，或合面睡，及上窜咬牙，皆心热也，导赤散主之。　　心气热则心胸亦热，欲言不能，而有就冷之意，故合面卧也。　　心热者，额上先赤，心烦心痛，掌中热而哕，或壮热饮水，巳午时益甚，宜泻心汤、导赤散、安神丸。　　脾热，则目黄肚大，怠惰嗜卧，身热饮水，四肢不收，泻黄散主之。　　脾热者，鼻上先赤，其热在肌肉，遇夜益甚。　　肺热，手掐眉目鼻面，甘桔汤主之；咳嗽寒热，壮热饮水，凉膈散主之；若肺虚热，唇深红色，少服泻白散。　　肺热者，右颊先赤，日西热甚，轻则用泻白散，重则用凉膈散及地骨皮散。　　肾热，两足不喜衣覆，地黄丸主之。　　肾热者，颊下先赤，两足热甚，骨酥酥如虫蚀，热甚不能起于床，夜间益甚，宜用滋肾丸。[35p]

    Those with liver heat will experience redness in the left cheek, difficulty in muscle contractions, irritability, and fatigue in the limbs, worsening during the hours of the tiger and rabbit. It is advisable to take Qing Wan and Chai Hu Yin Zi.

    For heart heat, observe the warmth of the breath from the mouth during sleep; if one sleeps with the face covered or grinds their teeth, this indicates heart heat, treated with Dao Chi San.

    When heart qi is heated, the chest also becomes hot, causing one to struggle to speak, feeling a desire for coldness, hence the tendency to sleep with the face covered. Symptoms include redness on the forehead, restlessness, heart pain, heat in the palms, and excessive thirst, worsening during the hours of the snake and horse. It is advisable to take Xin Tang, Dao Chi San, and An Shen Wan.

    With spleen heat, there will be yellowing of the eyes, a distended abdomen, lethargy, a desire to sleep, body heat, and limbs that cannot be drawn back. This condition is treated with Huang San.

    In cases of spleen heat, the nose will show initial redness, and the heat affects the muscles, worsening at night.

    For lung heat, use Gan Ju Tang for symptoms manifested in the hands, eyebrows, eyes, and face; for cough with alternating chills and fever, excessive thirst, use Liang Ge San. If there is lung deficiency heat, the lips will be deep red, and a small amount of Xie Bai San should be taken.

    With lung heat, the right cheek will initially be red, with increased heat in the afternoon; for mild symptoms, use Xie Bai San, for severe symptoms, use Liang Ge San and Di Gu Pi San.

    In cases of kidney heat, the feet dislike being covered, treated with Di Huang Wan.

    For kidney heat, there will be redness under the cheeks, significant heat in the feet, a sensation of bones being corroded, and an inability to rise from bed, especially worsening at night. The appropriate remedy is Zi Shen Wan.[35p]

    　　　　　实热

    　　实则伸体而卧，睡不露睛，手足指热等证。　　按实中宜分表里：表实宜汗，里实宜下，半表半里宜和解。今一以利下为主，非通论也。治法并方，更于后表里条内求之。　　小儿实热在内者，四顺饮之类；在上者吐之。　　小儿热病，六一散，妙药也。[36p]

    True Heat

    When there is true heat, the body stretches out while lying down and one cannot sleep with their eyes open; there are symptoms such as hot hands and feet. According to true heat, it is appropriate to distinguish between exterior and interior: for exterior heat, sweating is advisable; for interior heat, purging is necessary; for a combination of both, harmonization and resolution are recommended. Currently, the focus is primarily on purging, which is not a universal rule. The treatment methods and prescriptions should be sought within the guidelines for exterior and interior. For children with true heat internally, they should take cooling drinks; if the heat is above, inducing vomiting is necessary. For children's febrile diseases, Liu Yi San is an excellent remedy.[36p]

    　　实热，宜四顺清凉饮加柴胡。

    　　　　　虚热

    　　虚则喜热恶寒，乍凉乍温，怫郁惊惕，上盛下泄，屈体而卧，睡而露睛，手足指冷等证。　　虚热，因病后发热无时，一日三五次者，此客热乘虚而作，先以胃苓汤加黄芪末，温米清汤调服；次投钱氏白朮散，或固真汤，带凉服；及用温盐汤，参入凉水，送下黑锡丹，固守元气。　　风热，邪热，四君子汤加生姜、荆芥煎。　　小儿客热在内，先用导赤散，次用益黄散。　　薛氏以虚实分属表里，及热盛拒阴、寒盛格阳、血虚气虚发热等证，俱仲景、东垣诸圣医辨证妙法，宜详玩而熟记之，则虚热似实热之证，庶几不至误认而全活众矣。　　虚热宜惺惺散。[37p]

    For true heat, it is advisable to take a clear, cool drink with Bupleurum.

    For false heat

    When there is false heat, one tends to like warmth and dislike cold, experiencing alternating sensations of cool and warm, feelings of suffocation and anxiety, symptoms of excess above and deficiency below, curling up to sleep with eyes exposed, and coldness in hands and feet, among other signs. False heat occurs after an illness, presenting with persistent fever several times a day. This is due to pathogenic heat occupying a vacuity. First, take a warming herbal decoction with Astragalus powder, mixed with warm, clear rice soup; then administer Qian's White Atractylodes Powder, or Guhong Decoction, to be taken cool; also, use warm salty water mixed with cool water, and take along with Heixidan to consolidate original qi. For wind-heat and evil heat, use the Four Gentlemen Decoction with fresh ginger and Schizonepeta decocted. For children with internal heat, start with Daohong Powder and then use Yihuang Powder. Xue's distinction between true and false, as well as heat obstructing Yin, cold obstructing Yang, and symptoms of blood deficiency and qi deficiency causing fever, aligns with the diagnostic practices of esteemed physicians like Zhongjing and Dongyuan. It is recommended to study and familiarize oneself with these methods carefully so as to avoid misidentifying false heat as true heat, thus preserving the well-being of the many. For false heat, it is suitable to use Xingseng Powder.[37p]

    　　　　　表里

    　　身热不饮水者，热在外。
    　　身热饮水者，热在内。
    　　四顺饮子，治热在内而不厥。
    　　连翘饮，治热在外而不厥。
    　　薛氏云：壮热恶风寒，为元气不充，表之虚热也；壮热不恶风寒，为外邪客，表之实热也。壮热饮汤，为津液短少，里之虚热也；壮热饮水，为内火销烁，里之实热也。按伤风恶风，伤寒恶寒，岂可以恶风寒为元气不充，而不恶风寒为外邪所客乎？薛氏之意，本圆而语则滞，痴人前岂可说梦？须以东垣外感内伤细辨别之，则无失矣。
    　　　　　表热

    　　热而二便调和，风邪蕴结于里而发者，用惺惺散加麻黄汗之。
    　　　　　余热[38p]

    Exterior and Interior

    If the body is hot but does not drink water, the heat is external.
    If the body is hot and drinks water, the heat is internal.
    For a heat disorder treated with Four Shun decoction, it addresses internal heat and does not cause adverse reactions.
    For heat treated with Lianqiao decoction, it addresses external heat and does not cause adverse reactions.
    Xue argues: intense heat with aversion to wind and cold indicates that the essential energy is insufficient, suggesting virtual heat at the surface; intense heat without aversion to wind and cold indicates external pathogens, suggesting actual heat at the surface. Intense heat treated with soup indicates a deficiency of bodily fluids, suggesting virtual heat inside; intense heat treated with water indicates internal fire blazing, suggesting actual heat inside.
    When discussing wind-cold and aversion to cold, can one differentiate between aversion to wind and cold as a sign of insufficient essential energy, versus not having aversion due to external pathogens? Xue’s point is circular and his language unclear; can one speak dreams before fools? One must distinguish carefully between external influence and internal injury according to Dongyuan, to avoid confusion.

    Exterior Heat

    For heat with well-regulated urine and stools, where wind pathogens are trapped internally and emerge, use the Xingsheng powder with Mahuang decoction.

    Residual Heat[38p]

    　　余热者，谓寒邪未尽传经之遗热也。仁斋曰：伤寒汗下后而热又来，乃表里俱虚，气不归元，阳浮于外，不可再用凉药。盖热去则寒起，古人戒之。法当和胃气，使阳气收敛归内，其热自止，宜参苓白朮散主之。　　有小儿热证用表里药后，其热俱退，既退复热者，何也？热病至此，难以概举。或再解表攻里，或施凉剂，热见愈甚，以阴阳辨之，何者为是？推其原，乃表里俱虚而阳浮于外，阴伏于内，所以又发热，宜用温平之药和其里，则体热自除。投钱氏白朮散去木香如扁豆，水煎，及黄芪六一汤、安神散，自然平复。若日久汗多，烦渴食减，脉微缓，喜饮热，可服真武汤。虽附子性温，取其收敛阳气，内有芍药性寒，一寒一温，停分得宜，用之无不验矣。　　汗后血虚而热益甚者，六神散加粳米；汗后气虚而恶寒发热者，补中益气汤；汗后阴虚，阳无所附而热者，用四物汤加参、芪；汗后阳虚，阴无所附而热者，用四君子汤加芎、归。[39p]

    The residual heat refers to the lingering heat transmitted through the channels by the unfinished cold pathogens. Ren Zhai states: after a cold injury, when sweating and purging have occurred but heat reappears, both the exterior and interior are deficient, qi does not return to its source, and yang is floating outside, making it inappropriate to use cooling medicines again. The ancient sages warned that when heat departs, cold arises. The proper approach is to harmonize the stomach qi, allowing the yang qi to gather inward, which will naturally stop the heat. The formula Shen Ling Bai Zhu San should be used for this purpose.

    In cases of children with heat syndrome, after using both exterior and interior medications, if the heat completely subsides and then reappears, what is the reason? Heat diseases at this stage are difficult to generalize. Some may require re-expelling the exterior and attacking the interior, or applying cooling agents, which can intensify the heat. To differentiate between yin and yang, which is the correct approach? Upon investigation, it is found that both the exterior and interior are deficient, with yang floating outside and yin hidden within, leading to renewed heat. It is suitable to use warming and balancing medicines to harmonize the interior, allowing bodily heat to naturally resolve. The Qian family’s Bai Zhu San should be prepared without mu xiang, boiled in water, alongside Huang Qi Liu Yi Decoction and An Shen San, to allow for natural recovery.

    If sweating excessively leads to blood deficiency and worsens heat, add glutinous rice to Liu Shen San; if sweating causes qi deficiency with aversion to cold and fever, use Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction; for sweating with yin deficiency and no support for yang, use Si Wu Decoction with Ren Shen and Huang Qi; if sweating results in yang deficiency and no support for yin, use Si Jun Zi Decoction with Chuan Xiong and Gui.[39p]

    　　　　　壮热

    　　壮热者，一向不止，血气壅实，五脏生热，蒸熨于内则眠卧不安，精神恍惚；熏发于外则表里俱热，烦躁喘粗，甚则发惊癎也。轻剂火府丹、地黄煎，重剂双解饮、七宝散、大黄(石卜)硝汤。
    　　　　　温壮

    　　温壮与壮热相类而有小异：一向热而不止是壮热也；但温温然不甚盛，是温壮也。若大便臭而黄者，此腹内有伏热，以四顺饮子治之。若粪白而酸臭则挟宿食不消，当服紫霜丸，轻者少服；重者节乳哺，增加丸药，当取微利可也。[40p]

    Zhuang Re (Strong Heat)

    Strong heat is persistent, with blood and qi congested and the five viscera generating heat. When this heat steams internally, it causes restless sleep and mental confusion; when it manifests externally, it results in heat both inside and outside, causing irritability and labored breathing, and in severe cases, it may lead to seizures. For mild cases, administer Fire Mansion Pill or Earth Yellow Decoction; for severe cases, use Double Relief Drink, Seven Treasures Powder, or Large Yellow (Shi Bu) Nitrate Decoction.

    Wen Zhuang (Warm Strength)

    Warm strength resembles strong heat but differs slightly: it is heat that persists but is not overwhelming, referred to as warm strength. If the stool is foul and yellow, this indicates hidden heat in the abdomen, which can be treated with the Four Harmonizing Drink. If the stool is white and has a sour smell, it indicates undigested food; one should take Purple Frost Pill, using it sparingly for mild cases; for severe cases, reduce breastfeeding and increase the pill dosage, seeking a slight profit in treatment.[40p]

    　　　　　惊热

    　　惊热者，遍身发热，或热而不甚，面青自汗，睡梦虚惊，颠叫恍惚。有因惊而生热者，有因热而生惊者。钱氏导赤散、凉惊丸安神之类，皆其治也。
    　　　　　骨蒸热

    　　小儿一岁至十岁，衣絮皆不得着新绵，又不得冬月以火烘衣被，勿冷食桃杏杨梅果实，又不得食炙煿热面之类，皆令儿体热。或因伤寒后食肉太早，令儿体热者有之，或作骨蒸者，宜服生犀散、克效汤、地骨皮饮、七宝散、金莲饮子治之。　　骨蒸热，身体虚羸，遇晚而发，有热无寒，醒后渴汗方止。此乃疳病之余毒，传作骨蒸，或腹内有癖块，有时微痛，用参苓白朮散，姜枣三棱煎汤调服，或投化癖丸先疗脾虚宿滞，次以柴胡饮为治。仍忌鸡酒羊面毒物。
    　　　　　潮热[41p]

    Surprising Heat

    Surprising heat manifests as a sensation of heat throughout the body, sometimes mild, with a pale face and sweaty skin. Individuals may experience nightmares, sudden awakenings, and confusion. It can arise from shock causing heat, or from heat causing shock. Remedies like Qian's Dao Chi Powder and Liang Jing Pills help calm the mind.

    Bone Steaming Heat

    For children aged one to ten, they should not wear new cotton clothing, nor should they heat clothing or bedding over a fire in winter. They should avoid cold foods like peaches, apricots, and feijoa, as well as roasted or heated foods, all of which can cause internal heat. Sometimes, early consumption of meat after a cold can cause this heat. For bone steaming heat, one should take Shengxi Powder, Kexiao Decoction, Digubupi Decoction, Qibao Powder, or Jinlian Decoction. Bone steaming heat is characterized by a weak and thin body, often worsening in the evening, with heat present but no chill, and thirst that subsides only after sweating. This is a lingering toxin from dysentery that manifests as bone steaming, sometimes accompanied by internal masses or mild pain. Treatment includes Shenling Baizhu Powder, ginger and jujube decoction, or Huafei Pills to address spleen deficiency and retained food, followed by Chaihu Decoction for further treatment. It is also advised to avoid chicken, alcohol, mutton, and toxic substances.

    Tidal Heat[41p]

    　　热有作止，每日应时而发，谓之潮热，如潮信之不失其期也。　　潮热有风寒、疳积、食癖之分，阴阳、虚实、五脏之异。如汗出身热，呵欠面赤者，风热也；伤寒时疫，阴阳相胜，外感热也；肌瘦口干，骨蒸盗汗，疳热也；大小便秘濇，汗下不解，积热也；腹背先热，夜发旦止，饮热也；涎嗽饮水，乳食不消，癖热也。又有烦热者，气粗喘促，心躁不安，颊赤口疮，兼发癎证；疮疹热者，耳鼻尖冷；血热者，已午间发，至夜则凉；虚热者，困倦少力，发于病后。阳邪干心则来去不定，阴阳相胜则寒热如疟。前证在小儿，有因乳母或妊娠七情厚味遗热，或饮食停积，衣衾过暖，及频浴热汤而为患。若寅卯辰时热而力盛饮水者，肝经实热也，用柴胡清肝散；热而力怯饮汤者，肝经虚热也，用六味地黄丸。巳午时热，心经也，实用导赤散，虚用秘旨安神丸；申西戌时热，肺经也，实用泻白散，虚用秘旨保脾汤；亥子丑时热，肾经也，用地黄丸。[42p]

    Heat has its onset and cessation; it appears daily at the appropriate times, known as tidal heat, like the tide that does not fail to arrive on schedule. Tidal heat can be differentiated into categories: wind-heat, damp-heat, food stagnation, each influenced by yin and yang, deficiency and excess, and the various organs. For example, if sweating and body heat are present with yawning and a flushed face, it indicates wind-heat; in cases of epidemic diseases or exogenous heat, yin and yang conflict leads to external heat; symptoms like emaciation, dry mouth, and bone steaming with night sweats signify damp-heat; constipation or diarrhea with unresolved sweating indicates accumulated heat; abdominal and back heat that arises at night and ceases by dawn relates to drinking of heat; if there is phlegm and cough, inability to digest milk, it pertains to food stagnation heat.

    Additionally, those with vexatious heat manifest coarse breathing, a rapid pulse, restlessness, red cheeks, mouth sores, and may also experience seizures; skin rash heat results in cold tips of the ears and nose; blood heat presents at midday, cooling down by night; deficient heat leads to fatigue and weakness, emerging after illness. Yang pathogens disturb the heart leading to irregularities, and the conflict of yin and yang results in alternating cold and heat similar to malaria.

    In children, such symptoms may arise from the mother’s excessive emotions or rich diets during pregnancy, or from dietary stagnation, overly warm bedding, and frequent hot baths. If heat occurs during the hours of Yin (3-5 AM) or Mao (5-7 AM) with vigorous drinking, it indicates excess heat in the liver channel; use Chai Hu Qing Gan San. If heat is present but with weakness while drinking soup, it indicates deficiency heat in the liver channel; use Liu Wei Di Huang Wan. If heat appears during the hours of Si (9-11 AM) or Wu (11 AM-1 PM), it relates to the heart channel; use Dao Chi San for excess, and Mi Zhi An Shen Wan for deficiency. If heat arises during the hours of Shen (3-5 PM), Xu (5-7 PM), or Hai (9-11 PM), it implicates the lung channel; use Xie Bai San for excess, and Mi Zhi Bao Pi Tang for deficiency. If heat appears during the hours of Zi (11 PM-1 AM), Chou (1-3 AM), it relates to the kidney channel; use Di Huang Wan.[42p]

    大凡壮热饮水，大便秘结，属实热，用二黄犀角散下之；热渴饮汤，大便如常，属血虚，用四物汤补之。若下后阴虚，阳无所附而仍热，用四物参芪；汗后阳虚，阴无所生而仍热，用四君芎归。若汗下后烦渴面赤，血虚发躁也，当归补血汤；若见惊搐等证，肝血虚而内生风也，用四物、天麻、钓藤钩。颊赤口干，小便赤濇，大便焦黄，表里俱实热也，用清凉饮子。如大便已利，或热未止，表邪未解也，惺惺散；未应，加麻黄微汗之。既汗而仍热，此表里俱虚，气不归源，阳浮于外而虚热也，六神散加粳米。阳气下陷于阴中而发热者，用补中益气汤。若乳下婴儿，当兼治其母。　　曾氏先用百解散发表，次以当归散及三解散治之。脉实者以大柴胡汤下之，虚浮数者百解散微汗之；若发热而呕者，小柴胡汤和解之。　　小儿潮热盗汗，胡黄连、柴胡等为细末，炼蜜丸芡实大，每二丸，酒化开，入少水煎小沸服。　　潮热有时，胸满气短者，桃枝丸。[43p]

    Generally, if one has a strong fever accompanied by thirst and constipation, it indicates excess heat. To treat this, administer the Erhuang Xijiao San to clear it. If there is heat and thirst but normal stools, this suggests blood deficiency, and the Siwu Decoction should be used for supplementation. If there is deficiency after treatment, with yang failing to support and heat persisting, add Renshen and Huangqi to the Siwu Decoction. If sweating leads to yang deficiency, where yin fails to generate heat yet there is still warmth, use the Sijunzi Decoction with Xuangui. In cases of thirst, flushed face, and irritability post-sweating, this indicates blood deficiency causing agitation; the Danggui Bu Xue Tang is appropriate. If there are signs of shock or convulsions, indicating liver blood deficiency and internal wind, utilize the Siwu Decoction along with Tianma and Diaoteng. For a flushed face, dry mouth, red urine, and scorched yellow stools, indicating heat both inside and outside, employ the Qingliang Yinzi. If stools have improved or heat persists while the external pathogen is unresolved, the Xing Xing San should be applied; if needed, add a slight amount of Mahuang for mild sweating. If there is continued heat post-sweating, this shows deficiency inside and outside, with qi not returning to its source, and yang floating outside leading to false heat; apply the Liu Shen San with polished rice. If the yang energy descends into the yin and causes fever, the Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang should be administered. If treating a nursing infant, also treat the mother.

    The Zeng family first used Baijie San for the exterior, then applied Danggui San and Sanjie San for further treatment. For a firm pulse, use Da Chaihu Tang; for a weak, floating pulse, a slight sweat with Baijie San is appropriate. If there is fever and vomiting, use Xiao Chaihu Tang for harmonization.

    For children with tidal fever and night sweats, a fine powder of Hu Huanglian and Chaihu formed into pills with honey and Qian Shizi, taking two pills dissolved in a little water and decocting briefly.

    For intermittent tidal fever and chest fullness with shortness of breath, use the Taozhi Wan.[43p]

    　　　　　昼热

    　　《全婴方》：小儿每早食后发热，夜则凉，世医多谓虚劳，或为疳热，不知此血热证也，宜龙胆丸、地黄膏之类，时时与服即瘥。　　按《全婴方》所云血热者，巳午发热，遇夜则凉，与东垣所谓夜则发热，昼则明了不同。然束垣所云血热者，指阴虚而生内热也；夜则发热，昼则明了，取其昼阳夜阴也。郑氏所云血热者，指小儿血盛实而言也。盖谓巳午者，心火用事之时也。心主血，血气行至巳午则阳气盛，阳气与正气相搏，故至期而发热。非其时者，非血热也。[44p]

    Daytime Heat

    In "Complete Pediatric Formulas": When children experience a fever after eating in the morning and are cool at night, many doctors attribute this to deficiency-induced labor or malnutrition heat, not realizing that this is a case of blood heat. It is advisable to administer Long Dan Pills or Rehmannia paste, which, when taken regularly, will lead to recovery. According to "Complete Pediatric Formulas," blood heat refers to fever occurring at the hour of the Snake (9 AM to 11 AM) and Horse (11 AM to 1 PM), which then cools at night, differing from Dongyuan's description of fever at night and clarity during the day. The explanation from Shuyuan points to blood heat as arising from Yin deficiency creating internal heat; thus, fever at night and clarity during the day reflects the cycle of Yin at night and Yang during the day. Zheng's interpretation of blood heat refers to children having abundant and full blood. The reason for referencing the hours of the Snake and Horse is due to the heart's fire being active at this time. The heart governs blood, and when the blood and Qi circulate to the hours of the Snake and Horse, Yang energy is strong, clashing with the righteous Qi, which causes the fever at that designated time. If it occurs outside this period, it is not considered blood heat.[44p]

    　　　　　夜热

    　　海藏云：夜热属阴，四顺饮之类，此血热在夜也。　　《脉经》云：小肠有宿食，尝暮发热，明日复止，此宿食夜热也。　　风痰热，晚热早凉，吃水无时，此候乃痰作潮而生风热，即宜金星丸下之；或气弱者，不可下，宜夺命散以控下涎，次服惺惺散加南星、白附子。
    　　　　　积热

    　　积热者，久热也。疳热亦久，但兼面黄吃炭土，鼻下烂也。　　小儿表里热，去后又发热者，非热证也，只用六神散入粳米煎，和其胃气，则收阳归内，身体便凉；热重者用银白散。　　积热眼泡浮肿，面黄足冷，发热从头至肚愈甚，或闻饮食之气，恶心及肠疼呕吐，治法详载伤积论中。　　按曾氏所谓积热，乃指腹中有癖而热，与久积之积不同，不妨并存之。[45p]

    Night Heat

    Hai Cangyun: Night heat belongs to Yin; among the four seasons, it is related to drinking, which indicates that this blood heat occurs at night. The "Pulse Classic" states that if there is residual food in the small intestine, there will be a tendency to heat in the evening, which will stop by the following day; this is the night heat from residual food. Wind phlegm heat causes evening heat and morning coolness with irregular water intake; this situation suggests that phlegm brings about wind heat, and it is appropriate to administer the Jinxing Pill. If the Qi is weak, do not purge; instead, use the Duoming Powder to control the salivation, followed by the Xingsheng Powder with added Nansheng and Baifuzhi.

    Accumulated Heat

    Accumulated heat refers to persistent heat. Consumption heat also lasts long but is accompanied by a sallow complexion, similar to eating charcoal or earth, with ulcers under the nose. For children with both exterior and interior heat, if fever reappears after the exterior has been addressed, this is not a heat syndrome. Use the Liu Shen Powder into polished rice decoction to harmonize their stomach Qi, which returns the Yang inward, making the body cool. For those with severe heat, use the Yinbai Powder. Accumulated heat can lead to puffy eyelids, a sallow face, and cold feet, with fever emanating from the head to the abdomen, possibly accompanied by food odors, nausea, abdominal pain, and vomiting. Treatment methods are detailed in the discussion on injury from accumulation. According to Zeng, the so-called accumulated heat refers to heat from intestinal masses and differs from long-standing accumulation, and they may coexist.[45p]

    　　　　　寒热

    　　寒热者，证如疟状，阴阳相胜也。先寒而后热，阳不足；先热而后寒，阴不足。寒多而热少，阴胜阳也；热多而寒少，阳胜阴也；寒热相半，阴阳交攻也。寒热隔日，阴阳乍离也；阳盛发热，阴盛发寒也。其有头疼汗出者，有呕吐不食者，有增寒而饮水者，壮热而饮汤者，有筋骨疼痛者。或泻或秘，或内寒而外热，或内热而外寒。又有寒而腹中痛，热而腹中鸣，是有食积也。治法因于食积者，当用白饼子下之；次行补助，以钱氏白朮散。寒多热少者，小柴胡汤加桂；热多寒少者，白虎汤加桂；寒热相半者，并用小柴胡汤主之。　　经曰：阳虚则外寒，阴虚则内热，阳盛则外热，阴盛则内寒。寒热往来，此乃阴阳相胜也。故寒气并于阴则发寒，阳气并于阳则发热。[46p]

    Cold and Heat

    Cold and heat refer to symptoms resembling those of malaria, arising from the struggle between yin and yang. When cold comes first and heat follows, it indicates insufficient yang; when heat comes first and cold follows, it indicates insufficient yin. When there is more cold and less heat, yin overcomes yang; when there is more heat and less cold, yang overcomes yin. When cold and heat are balanced, yin and yang are in mutual conflict. If cold and heat alternate daily, yin and yang are briefly separated; when yang is strong, it causes heat, and when yin is strong, it causes cold. Symptoms may include headache with sweating, vomiting with loss of appetite, increased cold with drinking water, intense heat with consumption of soup, or muscle and joint pain. There may be diarrhea or constipation, or internal cold with external heat, or internal heat with external cold. Furthermore, there are cases where one feels cold with abdominal pain and heat with rumbling in the abdomen, indicating food accumulation. For treating food accumulation, one should use white flour for expelling it; then proceed with reinforcement using Qian's white atractylodes powder. For conditions of more cold and less heat, Xiao chaihu decoction with cinnamon should be used; for more heat and less cold, Baihu decoction with cinnamon; for balanced cold and heat, Xiao chaihu decoction should be the principal remedy. The classics state: When yang is deficient, external cold arises; when yin is deficient, internal heat arises; when yang is strong, external heat arises; when yin is strong, internal cold arises. The alternation of cold and heat indicates the struggle between yin and yang. Therefore, cold associated with yin causes cold symptoms, while warmth associated with yang causes heat symptoms.[46p]

    寸口脉微为阳不足，阴气上入阳中则恶寒；尺脉弱为阴不足，阳气下入阴中则发热。阳不足则先寒后热，阴不足则先热后寒，阴阳不归其分则寒热交争也。又上盛则发热，下盛则发寒。阳胜则乍热，阴胜则乍寒。阴阳相胜，虚实不调，故邪气更作而寒热往来，故乍寒乍热也。少阳胆者，肝之腑，界乎太阳阳明之间，半表半里之分，阴阳之气易于相乘，故寒热多主肝胆经证，以小柴胡汤加减调之。若祇见寒热，起居如常，久而不愈，及大病后元气未复，悉属阴虚生热，阳虚生寒，宜用八珍汤补之，甚者十全大补汤。有食积为病，亦令寒热，用保和丸消之；若兼呕吐泄泻，用六君子汤。厥冷饮热，人参理中丸。作渴不止，七味白朮散。食积既消而寒热尚作者，肝邪乘脾，所胜侮所不胜也，用异功散加柴胡、山栀。其疟证寒热，详见疟门。[47p]

    The inch pulse is weak, indicating insufficient Yang, and when Yin energy rises into Yang, it leads to aversion to cold; the ruler pulse is weak, indicating insufficient Yin, and when Yang energy descends into Yin, it causes fever. Insufficient Yang leads to cold first and then heat, while insufficient Yin leads to heat first and then cold. When Yin and Yang do not return to their proper divisions, cold and heat struggle against each other. Additionally, if the upper part is excess, it manifests as fever; if the lower part is excess, it manifests as cold. When Yang is dominant, there is sudden heat; when Yin is dominant, there is sudden cold. If Yin and Yang overcome each other and the deficiencies and excesses are unbalanced, then evil Qi arises, causing alternating cold and heat, resulting in sudden cold and sudden heat.

    The Shao Yang gallbladder is a part of the liver’s organs, situated between the Tai Yang and Yang Ming, half superficial and half internal, making it easier for Yin and Yang energies to interact. Consequently, cold and heat often dominate liver and gallbladder syndromes, which can be adjusted with Xiao Chai Hu Decoction, modified as needed. If only cold and heat are evident, and daily life remains unchanged, prolonged illness without recovery, along with post-serious illness where the Yuan Qi has not restored, indicates Yin deficiency generating heat and Yang deficiency generating cold; thus, it is advisable to use Ba Zhen Decoction for nourishment, and in severe cases, Shi Quan Da Bu Decoction.

    If there's food stagnation causing illness, it can also result in cold and heat, which can be resolved with Bao He Wan; if there are accompanying symptoms of vomiting and diarrhea, use Liu Jun Zi Decoction. For critical cold with hot beverages, Ren Shen Li Zhong Wan is effective. If thirst persists, use Qi Wei Bai Zhu San. After food stagnation is resolved but cold and heat still persist, it suggests that liver evil is overpowering the spleen, indicating a deficiency where it is not overcome; in this case, use Yi Gong San with added Chai Hu and Shan Zhi Zi. For malaria symptoms of alternating cold and heat, refer to the section on malaria.[47p]

    　　　　　烦躁

    　　仲景云：火入于肺则烦，入于肾则躁。夫心者君火也，火旺则金燔，水亏而火独存，故肺肾合而为躁也。《活人》云：但烦热者，虚烦也。诸虚烦热，与伤寒相似。但不恶寒，鼻不疼，故知非伤寒也；头不痛，脉不紧，故知非里寒也。不可发汗攻下，当与竹叶汤；兼呕者，与橘皮汤。又心虚则先烦而后渴，翕翕发热，其脉浮紧而大是也。盖烦者，心中烦扰而内热，故属阳；躁者，肢体躁动，或裸身欲入井中，为外热，故属阴。外热者无根之火也，是以为虚。脉数而实，便秘有热者，神芎丸，此皆实热之治法也。若烦而头痛短气，口干咽燥不渴者，虚也，用四君加芎、归。因药攻伐而作渴者，用竹茹汤。烦而不得眠者，酸枣仁汤。心神颠倒，烦热欲吐者，朱砂安神丸。面戴阳，目内赤，六脉洪大，按之全无者，血虚发躁，用当归补血汤。若躁而裸体欲入井中，脉沉细或浮大，按之如无者，此皆阴盛发躁也，宜用参附汤，有回生之功。[48p]

    Restlessness

    Zhongjing said: When fire enters the lungs, it causes restlessness; when it enters the kidneys, it causes agitation. The heart is the monarch fire; when the fire is vigorous, the metal (lungs) is incinerated, and when the water is depleted, the fire alone persists, thus the lungs and kidneys come together to result in agitation. The "Living Person" states: When one feels hot and restless, it is due to deficiency and agitation. Various instances of deficiency, agitation, and heat resemble those of cold damage, but there is no aversion to cold, and there is no nasal pain; hence, it is known not to be cold damage. There is no headache, and the pulse is not tight, thus it is known not to be internal cold. Sweating and purging are inappropriate; rather, it should be treated with Bamboo Leaf Decoction; if there is also vomiting, use Tangerine Peel Decoction. Furthermore, if the heart is deficient, there will be restlessness followed by thirst, with heat rising and the pulse being floating, tight, and large. Here, agitation arises from inner disturbance and internal heat, hence it is attributed to yang; restlessness involves the limbs being agitated, or a desire to enter a well naked, being outward heat, hence it is attributed to yin. External heat is a fire without root, thus it represents deficiency. When the pulse is rapid and solid, with constipation and heat, use Shenxiong Pill; these are all treatments for solid heat. If there is restlessness with headache, shortness of breath, dry mouth, and throat without thirst, this indicates deficiency; use Four Ginseng Decoction with added Chuanxiong and Angelica. If thirst arises from the medicinal attack, use Bamboo Shoots Decoction. For restlessness and inability to sleep, use Sour Jujube Seed Decoction. For disturbance of the spirit, with restlessness and desire to vomit, use Cinnabar Peaceful Spirit Pill. If the face is flushed, eyes are red within, with all six pulses being large and floating, pressing them yields nothing, indicating blood deficiency leading to restlessness, use Angelica Blood Nourishing Decoction. If agitated and desiring to enter a well naked, with a pulse that is deep and fine or floating and large, pressing gives no response, this indicates excessive yin leading to agitation; it is thus advisable to use Ginseng and A附 Decoction, which has restorative effects.[48p]

    　　　　　注夏

    　　脾为太阴，位属坤土，喜燥而恶湿。故凡脾胃之气不足者，遇长夏润溽之令，则不能升举清阳，健运中气；又复少阳相火之时，热伤元气，则肢体怠惰不收，两脚痿弱，嗜卧发热，精神不足，饮食少思，口中无味，呼吸短乏气促，目中视物(目巟)(目巟)，小便赤数，大便不调，名曰注夏。此皆禀赋阴虚元气不足之证，丹溪补阴论言之详矣，育子者可不知冬月养阳之道乎？治法用补中益气汤去升麻、柴胡，加炒黑黄蘗主之。[49p]

    Notes on Late Summer

    The spleen is associated with the Taiyin, situated in the Earth element, favoring dryness and disliking dampness. Therefore, when the spleen and stomach qi is insufficient, encountering the humid and sultry conditions of late summer hinders the rising of clear yang and the healthy movement of the central qi. Additionally, during the time of the slight yang fire, heat can injure the original qi, leading to lethargy in the limbs, weakness in the feet, excessive sleeping accompanied by fever, a lack of spirit, little appetite, tastelessness in the mouth, shortness of breath, blurriness in vision, frequent and red urination, and irregular bowel movements. This condition is called "Late Summer Affliction." These symptoms all reflect a deficiency of yin and original qi. Danxi discusses the treatment in detail regarding the nurturing of children; should one not also know the method of nurturing yang in winter? The treatment method involves the use of the "Ba Zhen Tang" (Eight Treasures Decoction) by removing the herbs Sheng Ma and Chai Hu, and adding the roasted black Huang Bo as the main ingredient.[49p]

    若因劳役发热，血虚脉大者，用当归补血汤；气血两虚者，八珍汤；肝肾阴亏者，地黄丸；大便作泻者，人参理中汤。若乳母肝火乘脾，寒热少食者，柴胡栀子散；胃火作渴者，竹叶石膏汤。小儿多因乳母之气不调而致，当戒怒气，调饮食，适寒温，则可以远病。又如今人夏月皆以香薷汤浸冷，代茶饮之。殊不知香薷利水，大损元阳；厚朴克伐，大泻真气。况脾性喜温而恶寒，夏月阴盛于内，啜冷伤脾，若胃强有火，湿热为病之人，固无大害，其脾胃虚弱，中气不足者，必为腹痛少食泄泻寒中之疾矣。此大人亦当戒者，况小儿乎？慎之慎之！[50p]

    If one develops a fever due to labor and has deficient blood with a large pulse, use the Angelica Sinensis Blood-Toning Decoction; if both qi and blood are deficient, use the Eight Treasures Decoction; if there is deficiency of liver and kidney yin, use the Rehmannia Pill; if there is diarrhea, use the Ginseng Decoction for Regulating the Middle. If a nursing mother has liver fire disturbing the spleen and experiences chills, heat, and poor appetite, use the Chai Hu and Gardenia Powder; if there is thirst due to stomach fire, use the Bamboo Leaf and Gypsum Decoction. Children often suffer due to the imbalanced qi of their nursing mothers, so they must avoid anger, regulate diet, and adjust to cold and warmth to prevent illness. Nowadays, people commonly use fragrant rush decoction as a cold infusion to replace tea in summer. However, they are unaware that fragrant rush promotes diuresis and greatly diminishes original yang; magnolia bark can inhibit and cause significant depletion of true qi. Moreover, the spleen prefers warmth and dislikes cold; in summer, when yang is abundant internally, drinking cold can harm the spleen. Those with strong stomachs and fire, or those suffering from damp-heat ailments, may not experience significant harm, but those with weak spleens and stomachs, or insufficient central qi, are likely to suffer from abdominal pain, reduced appetite, and diarrhea caused by cold. Adults should also take caution in these matters, let alone children! Be cautious![50p]

    　　　　　黄疸

    　　《难知》云：色如熏黄，乃湿病也，一身尽痛。　　色如橘子黄者，黄病也，身不痛。
    　　干黄，燥也，小便自利，四肢不沉重，渴而引饮者，栀子蘗皮汤。　　湿黄，脾也，小便不利，四肢沉重，似渴不欲饮者，大茵陈汤。　　大便自利而黄者，茵陈栀子黄连三物汤。　　往来寒热，一身尽黄者，小柴胡加栀子汤。　　汤氏云：身疼，髆背疼，大小便濇，皮肤面目齿爪皆黄，小便如屋尘色，利者易治，濇者难治。宜服五苓散加茵陈煎汤调，又宜服导赤散加茵陈煎。或身热宜服小柴胡汤，甚者服承气汤。[51p]

    Jaundice

    The text "Nan Zhi" states: If the color appears as a deep yellow, it is a damp disease, and the entire body aches. If the color resembles that of an orange, it is a jaundice disease, and the body does not ache.

    For dry jaundice, characterized by dryness, with spontaneous urination, limbs not feeling heavy, and thirst leading to drinking, one should use the Lu Hu Zhi Pi Decoction. For damp jaundice, related to the spleen, with difficulty in urination, heavy limbs, and a sensation of thirst without desire to drink, the Da Yin Chen Decoction is appropriate. If there is spontaneous yellow bowel movement, one should consider the decoction of Yin Chen, Zhi Zi, and Huang Lian.

    For alternating chills and fevers, accompanied by a yellow complexion all over, the Xiao Chai Hu Decoction with Zhi Zi is recommended. According to Tang Shi: If there is body pain, pain in the waist and back, difficulty in urination and feces, and the skin, face, teeth, and nails are all yellow, with urine resembling the color of house dust, those with easy urination are easier to treat, whereas those with difficulty are harder to treat. It is advisable to take Wu Ling San with Yin Chen decoction or Dao Chi San with Yin Chen decoction. If there is heat in the body, Xiao Chai Hu Decoction should be taken, and in severe cases, Cheng Qi Decoction may be administered.[51p]

    　　凡黄病者，不可一概而论。标本不同，证治亦异。乃脾胃气虚，感受湿热，郁于腠理，淫于皮肤，蕴积成黄，重发于外，故有此证。或脾胃虚弱，内因症癖攻之而成，然疳泻亦主皮黄发竖，肚大青筋，肌肉消瘦，外无色泽，身必发黄，此文本于疳病而作，致有是证。治法：若感湿热而得身黄，如烟熏之色，以(口父)咀五苓散加麻黄，水姜煎投，汗之即愈；或用茵陈蒿汤调下五苓散亦好。　　若得于疳癖者，其形如黄土相类，以醒脾散、化癖丸，醒脾快胃，磨积理疳。[52p]

    In general, cases of jaundice cannot be treated uniformly. The root and branch differ, and so do the symptoms and treatments. This condition may arise from a deficiency of spleen and stomach qi, leading to the absorption of damp heat, which obstructs the pores and manifests on the skin, accumulating and resulting in yellowing. Alternatively, it may stem from weakness of the spleen and stomach, with internal causes attacking and giving rise to symptoms such as yellow skin, protruding belly with blue veins, muscle wasting, lack of external color, and a必黃色a complexion, which relates to wasting disease.

    Treatment: If the jaundice is caused by damp heat, it resembles smoke-induced color; one should use Wuling Powder with Mahuang, boiled with fresh ginger and taken as a decoction, which will induce sweating and lead to recovery. Alternatively, Yinchenshao Decoction combined with Wuling Powder is also effective.

    If it is due to wasting disease, the appearance resembles yellow earth; in this case use the Lingwai San or Huapi Pill to awaken the spleen and resolve accumulations caused by wasting.[52p]

    胃气已和，饮食倍进，运化精微，荣养百骸，灌溉脏腑，五色各见于本部，精华乃形于面貌，其黄自除。　　经曰：中央黄色，入通于脾。故黄疸者，脾之色也。夫人身之神贵于藏而默用，见于外则内虚矣。其谊皆因脾气有亏，运化失职，湿热留于肌肤，发而为疸。钱仲阳所谓身痛背强，二便濇滞，遍身面目爪甲皆黄是也，小便褐色者难治。疗法宜固脾为先，如专用克伐宽中、淡泄利水之药，则鲜有不致危者矣。若初生及百日半年之间，不因病而身黄者，胃热胎黄也。[53p]

    When the stomach's qi is harmonious and food intake increases, the essence is transformed and refined, nourishing the body and irrigating the organs. The five colors manifest in their respective parts, and the essence and vitality are expressed in one’s appearance, with any yellowish hue fading away. The classics say: "The central yellow corresponds to the spleen." Therefore, jaundice is the color of the spleen. The spirit of a person is more precious when it is contained and quietly utilized; when it is seen externally, it indicates internal deficiency. This is all due to a deficiency of spleen qi, where transformation and transportation fail, causing dampness and heat to linger in the skin, resulting in jaundice. As Qian Zhongyang stated, symptoms like body aches, back weakness, and yellowing of the skin, face, and nails indicate this condition, with brownish urine being difficult to treat. The treatment should focus on strengthening the spleen first; if one relies solely on harsh purgatives and diuretics, it is rarely safe. If jaundice occurs in newborns within the first hundred days or six months, without being due to illness, it is due to stomach heat or fetal jaundice.[53p]

    腹大食土为脾疳，兼作渴饮冷者，用泻黄散；小便不利者茵陈汤；病后发黄肢体浮肿者，用白朮散；清便自调，肢冷嗜卧者，益黄散；身淡黄白者调中丸，及补中益气汤加茵陈；身热膈满，肌肤面目皆黄者，加减泻黄散。辨其所以，若闭目壮热，多哭不已，大小便赤濇，口中热气者，乃妊娠厚味胎毒之候也，母子并服生地黄疡，仍忌酒面五辛热物。设不自慎，误伤脾土，急则变为惊风吐泻，缓则肢体浮肿，小便不利，眼目障闭，多成疳疾矣。又有脾虚发黄者，当于脾胃中求之。[54p]

    If there is a large abdomen with soil eating causing spleen dampness, and also accompanied by thirst for cold drinks, use the Huang San. For difficulty in urination, use Yincheng Decoction. If there is yellowing of the body and edema after illness, use Baizhu San. For those with self-regulating bowel movements, cold limbs, and a tendency to lie down, use Yihuang San. If the body is pale yellow and white, use Tiaozhong Wan and add Yincheng to Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction. If there is heat, fullness in the stomach, and the skin and face are all yellow, then modify and use the Huang San.

    If the symptoms include closed eyes, intense heat, continual crying, and red and thin urine with heat in the mouth, this indicates the signs of pregnancy poison from rich food. Both mother and child should take Sheng Di Huang and avoid alcohol, shallots, and hot foods. If one is not careful and injures the spleen and soil, the condition can quickly turn into convulsions and diarrhea, or slowly lead to edema of the limbs, difficulty in urination, and closed eyelids, resulting in many cases of dampness diseases. There are also cases of yellowing due to spleen deficiency; one should seek solutions within the spleen and stomach.[54p]

    　　　　幼幼近编 【明　陈治】

    　　　　　潮热

    　　小儿初病潮热，或病后潮热，俱属食伤太阴脾经，宜参苓白朮散。有疮疖潮热，八珍汤加贝母。
    　　　　小儿卫生总微论方 【宋　撰人未详】
    　　　　　诸身热

    　　小儿身热，但温而不甚壮热，此为温热。　　小儿身热，口中气热，叫哭无时，呵欠烦闷，面目青色，此为风热，甚亦发惊。　　小儿身热，饮水悸惕，手足摇动，上视弄舌，印内青筋见，掌中赤，怕物生涎，此为惊热。　　小儿身热面赤，时久不退，睡觉颠叫，气急发渴，胸高涎壅，此为积热，与壮热相似，但胸高涎壅为异，乃脏腑积蕴热毒，三焦膈腕壅滞也。又摇头项硬者，亦三焦膈腕壅也。　　已上皆甚则发搐，治在惊癎门中。[55p]

    Chao Re (Tidal Fever)

    When a child initially suffers from tidal fever or experiences it post-illness, it relates to the excess of food harming the Taiyin Spleen Meridian. It is advisable to use Shen Ling Bai Zhu San. If there are sores or boils accompanying the tidal fever, modify Ba Zhen Tang by adding Bei Mu.

    General Theories on Child Health

    When a child has body heat that is warm but not excessively strong, this is classified as a warm heat. If the child's body heat is accompanied by a hot sensation in the mouth, continuous crying, yawning, signs of restlessness, and a bluish complexion, this indicates wind heat, which may also lead to fright. If the child exhibits body heat with anxiety over drinking water, trembling hands and feet, looking upwards while moving the tongue, visible blue veins on the inner hands, red palms, and fear of objects causing salivation, this is deemed startling heat. If a child has body heat with a red face that does not subside over time, disturbed sleep with cries, rapid breathing and thirst, elevated chest with phlegm stagnation, this represents accumulated heat. It resembles strong heat but is distinct due to the phlegm accumulation in the elevated chest, indicating a build-up of heat and toxins in the organs, causing stagnation in the three burners. Also, if the child shakes their head and has a stiff neck, it too indicates stagnation in the three burners. All of the above may lead to convulsions in severe cases, and treatment should be approached through the gate of fright and convulsion.[55p]

    　　小儿身体发热，气促鼻塞，清涕嚏喷，寒毛立，眼泪出，或出痰水，此为伤寒，治在伤寒门中。　　小儿身热，时发时退，退但肚热；或夜发热面黄，腹胀吐泻，乳食不化，粪酸臭异常，此为食伤，治在伤食门中。　　小儿夜发热，晓即如故，多涎喜睡，此肺虚发热也，此与食伤夜发热相似，要须识之。况二证余候，各皆不同：食伤者可下；肺虚者不可下，下之则失津液发渴引饮。昔钱乙治朱监簿子五岁，夜发热，晓即如故。众医作热，以凉药解之不愈。[56p]

    When a child has a fever, experiences shortness of breath, nasal congestion, clear runny nose, sneezing, chills, tearing, or possibly produces phlegm, this is classified as a cold injury, treated according to the protocols for a cold injury.

    If a child has a fever that comes and goes, with a hot belly during the fever; or if they have a nighttime fever with a yellow face, abdominal bloating, vomiting, diarrhea, and food not digesting well, with a sour and foul-smelling stool, this indicates food injury, treated according to the protocols for food injury.

    When a child has a nighttime fever that resolves by morning, excessive salivation, and seems to enjoy sleeping, this suggests that the child has a deficiency of the lungs causing the fever, which can resemble a food injury. It is crucial to differentiate between the two, as the residual symptoms vary: in food injury, one can use purgatives; in lung deficiency, one should not, as doing so will lose vital fluids, causing thirst and a desire for drinks.

    In the past, Qian Yi treated a five-year-old who had a nighttime fever that resolved by morning. Many physicians characterized it as a heat condition and prescribed cooling medicines, but it did not improve.[56p]

    其候多涎喜唾，又以药下其涎，病益甚。至五六日，请乙治之。乙曰：不可下，乃取白朮散煎汤三升，使任意取足服。朱曰：饮多不作泻否？乙曰：无生水，不能作泻。纵利亦不足怪，但不可下耳！朱又曰：先治何病？乙曰：止泻治痰，退热清神，皆此药也。服尽，又作两次与服，其子不渴无痰，又投阿胶散二服而安。是此证也。钱乙方本集载之。　　小儿身热形瘦，多渴饮食不为肌肉，此为疳热，治在疳门中。　　小儿血气旺盛，发渴引饮，大便黄坚，小便赤少，四肢身体翕然而热，此为胃实热也，治宜下之。[57p]

    The patient had excessive salivation and frequent spitting, and when medicine was administered to reduce the saliva, the illness worsened. After five or six days, I asked Yi to treat him. Yi said: "Do not administer a laxative." He then prepared three sheng of decoction from Atractylodes powder, allowing the patient to take as much as he needed. Zhu asked: "If he drinks too much, won’t it cause diarrhea?" Yi replied: "With no living water, it cannot cause diarrhea. Even if there is a discharge, it is not alarming; just don’t use a laxative!" Zhu further inquired: "What illness was treated first?" Yi responded: "To stop diarrhea, treat phlegm, reduce fever, and calm the spirit—all with this medicine." After the prescription was fully taken, it was given again twice, and the child was no longer thirsty and had no phlegm. Then, two doses of Ejiao powder were given, and he was at peace. This is indicative of that condition. This is recorded in the collected works of Qian Yi.

    For children with fever, emaciation, and excessive thirst, whose diet does not lead to muscle growth, it indicates intestinal heat, which should be treated by addressing the intestinal issue.

    For children with abundant blood and energy, excessive thirst leading to drinking, hard yellow stools, scant red urine, and heat in the limbs and body, it indicates heat in the stomach, which should be treated with a laxative.[57p]

    　　小儿身发热微惊，耳骩冷，上唇头有白泡起如鱼目珠子，或汗或不汗，此为变蒸，治在变蒸门中。　　小儿身热，昏睡惊悸，喜嚏，耳尻冷，此为疮疹候，治在疮疹门中。此与食伤变蒸相似，伤寒耳尻皆热，双蒸唇上有白疣泡珠子为异。　　小儿身热者，更有内外。在内者多饮水得之，在外者多因风寒得之。钱氏有云：小儿身热饮水者热在内，身热不饮水者热在外，此大概之验也。在内者宜下之，在外者宜散之。　　阎孝忠论小儿壮热伤风，温疫伤寒，风热疮疹，伤食，率皆相似，未能辨认之间，但与升麻葛根汤、惺惺散、小柴胡汤服之甚验。[58p]

    When a young child has a slight fever and is slightly startled, with cold ears and white blisters appearing on the upper lip like fish eyes, and either has sweat or does not, this indicates a condition called "transformation steaming," which is treated under the category of "transformation steaming."

    When a child has a fever, is lethargic and startled, enjoys sneezing, and has cold ears, this indicates symptoms of measles, treated under the category of "measles." This is similar to illness caused by food injury leading to transformation steaming, where cold ears are hot in cases of cold damage, while the dual steaming with white warts and blisters on the lips is different.

    Fever in children may derive from both internal and external causes. Internal causes often arise from excessive water consumption, while external causes are typically due to wind and cold. According to Qian, when a child has an internal fever and drinks a lot of water, it indicates internal heat, while if a child has a fever and does not drink water, it indicates external heat. This is a general diagnostic principle. For internal causes, treatment should focus on purging, while for external causes, treatment should focus on dispersing.

    Yan Xiaozhong discusses the patterns of high fever from wind chill and illnesses like warm epidemic and cold damage, as well as wind-heat measles and food injury, which are all quite similar and often difficult to distinguish. However, treatments like Shengma Gegen Decoction, Xingsingsan, and Xiao Chaihu Decoction have proven to be very effective.[58p]

    盖此数药通治之，不致误也。催伤食者则大便酸臭，乳不化，畏食或吐，宜与微下。　　孙真人论小儿内外气盛，眠时小惊，或微觉伤风伤食，又虑变蒸身热者，但以紫圆，或龙胆汤为治。此二药无所不疗，虽微利动以减盛气，亦不虚人。小儿粪黄而臭者，此腹中有伏热也，宜服龙胆汤；若粪白而酸臭者，此挟寒不消也，宜服紫圆。但少与令内消，甚者少增令微稀溏，皆须节乳哺一两日，令胃气平和。若不节则病易复，复则复下，伤其胃气，令腹胀满；若至再三下之，则过伤矣。　　小儿于立夏之后，有病身热者，慎勿妄为吐下，但以除热汤浴之，除热粉粉之，赤摩膏涂之。[59p]

    These several medicines can be used for treatment without causing harm. For those with dietary injuries causing foul-smelling stools, undigested milk, food aversion, or vomiting, it is advisable to use a mild purgative.

    Master Sun discussed that children with excess internal and external energy might experience slight fright during sleep or mild symptoms of wind or dietary injury, as well as a concern for heat in the body. For such cases, using Ziyuan or Longdan Decoction is appropriate. These two medicines can treat a wide range of ailments. Although they may slightly purge to reduce excess energy, they do not deplete the body’s strength.

    If a child's stools are yellow and foul, it indicates hidden heat in the abdomen, and Longdan Decoction should be administered. If the stools are white and sour-smelling, it indicates lingering cold and indigestion, and Ziyuan should be given. Administer in small doses to help with internal digestion, and if symptoms are severe, slightly increase the dosage to facilitate mild loose stools. It is essential to limit breastfeeding for a day or two to regulate stomach energy. If not restricted, the illness may easily recur, leading to repeated purging, which could harm the stomach's energy and cause abdominal bloating. If purging occurs multiple times, it would lead to excessive depletion.

    After the beginning of summer, if a child has a feverish illness, be cautious not to recklessly induce vomiting or purging. Instead, use heat-clearing decoctions for bathing, apply heat-clearing powders, or use red friction ointments.[59p]

    　　　　　黄疸

    　　小儿有身体肌肤面目悉黄者，此黄病也。因将息过度，饮食伤饱，脾胃受热，与谷气相搏，蒸发于外，脾胃象土，其色黄，候肌肉，故为是病也。慎不可灸，灸则热转甚矣。若身体痛，背髆强，大小便濇，腹胀满，一身尽黄，及目睛爪甲皆黄，小便如屋尘色，若物皆黄，此疸病也。若发渴，小便濇，腹满，脉沉细，为难治也。黄病者稍轻，疸病极重。又有自生下面身深黄者，此胎疸也，因母脏气有热，熏蒸于胎故也。经言：诸疸皆变色深黄者是也。若身微黄者，胃热也。若但面黄腹大，渴而食泥土者，脾疳也。
    　　　　　渴

    　　小儿有渴而饮水者，此因脏腑有热，热则脏燥，故多体热发渴，亡耗津液，即令作渴欲饮水以解之也。又有疳渴、吐泻发渴、霍乱发渴者，各逐本项具之。阎孝忠云：凡小儿诸渴，因亡失津液，引饮，但多煎钱氏白朮散与服，使任意取足饮之，弥多弥好。古今图书集成医部全录卷四百二十[60p]

    Jaundice

    When a child has all their skin and face turning yellow, this is called jaundice. It results from excessive rest or overindulgence in food, causing heat in the spleen and stomach, which conflicts with the air from grains, leading to evaporation outward. The spleen and stomach resemble earth, and their color is yellow, affecting the muscles and thus causing the illness. Care must be taken not to moxibust, as that would worsen the heat. If there is body pain, stiffness in the back, difficulty in urination and defecation, abdominal distension, the whole body is yellow, and the eyes and nails are also yellow, with urine like the color of dust, this is jaundice. If there is thirst, difficulty in urination, abdominal fullness, and a deep, fine pulse, it is difficult to treat. The yellow illness is slightly lighter, while jaundice is extremely severe. There is also jaundice that presents as deep yellow in the lower body; this is fetal jaundice due to the mother’s organ heat affecting the fetus. As the classics state, all jaundice that turns a deep yellow is similar. If the body is slightly yellow, it indicates stomach heat. If only the face is yellow and the abdomen is distended, accompanied by a desire to eat dirt, this indicates spleen deficiency.

    Thirst

    When a child is thirsty and drinks water, it is because there is heat within the organs. Heat leads to dryness in the organs, causing the body to feel hot and thirsty, thus prompting a loss of fluids that creates a desire for water to relieve it. There are also symptoms of deficiency thirst, thirst due to vomiting and diarrhea, and thirst due to cholera; each has its specific causes and conditions. Yan Xiaozhong states: For all children's thirst, caused by the loss of fluids, make them drink by giving them a decoction of Qian's white atractylodes powder freely, and the more they drink, the better.[60p]

    小儿诸热门

    　　　　方

    　　神验柴胡散 【《中藏经》】 　治小儿骨热，夜间如蒸，甚者不过十数日见效。　　土柴胡不拘多少，去芦洗净，炙黄色，不令太焦，亦不须银州者　　右为末，每服二钱，水一盏，入地骨皮指面大二片子，同煎至七分，食后温服。如虚瘦，但空心服补药，食后煎下数服，时时如水饮之。
    　　丹参赤膏 【《千金方》，下同】 　治少小心腹热。　　丹参　雷丸　芒硝　戎盐　大黄各二两　　右五味(口父)咀，以苦酒半升浸四种一宿，以炼成猪肪一斤煎三上三下，去滓，乃内芒硝，膏成以摩心下，冬夏可用。一方，但用丹参、雷丸亦佳。[61p]

    Pediatric Remedies

      Formula

    Efficacious Chaihu Powder: For treating childhood bone heat, with symptoms of feeling like it's steaming at night, effective within a few days at most. Use local Chaihu, washing it clean and roasting until yellow, not overly charred, not needing silver variety. Grind to a powder, taking two qian with a cup of water, add two pieces of earth bone skin the size of a finger, boil until reduced to seven parts, and take warm after meals. If the child is thin and weak, take tonic medicines on an empty stomach, and after meals take several doses, drinking like water occasionally.

    Dan Shen Red Paste: For treating heat in the abdomen of young children. Ingredients: Dan Shen, Lei Wan, Mang Xiao, Rong Yan, and Da Huang, each two liang. Crush these five ingredients, soak in half a sheng of bitter wine overnight to refine into one jin of pig fat, boil three times, strain, then add Mang Xiao, and when the paste forms, use it for heart application. This can be used in winter and summer. Alternatively, using just Dan Shen and Lei Wan is also good.[61p]

    　　五物甘草生摩膏　治少小新生，肌肤幼弱，善为风邪所中，身体壮热，或中大风，手足惊掣。　　甘草　防风各一两　白朮　桔梗各二十铢　雷丸二两　　右(口父)咀，以不中水猪肪一斤煎为膏，以前药微火上煎，消息视稠浊，膏成去滓，取如弹丸大一枚，炙手以摩儿百过。寒者更热，热者更寒。小儿虽无病，早起常以膏摩顖上及手足心，甚辟风寒。
    　　李叶浴汤　治少小身热。
    　　李叶无拘多少
    　　右(口父)咀，以水煮去滓，将浴儿良。
    　　柳枝浴汤　治小儿生一月至五月，乍寒乍热。　　柳枝无拘多少细切
    　　右煮取汁洗儿。若渴，绞冬瓜汁服之。
    　　青木香浴汤　治小儿壮热羸瘠。
    　　青木香四两　麻仁　竹叶各一升　虎骨五两　白芷三两　　右五味(口父)咀，以水二斗，煮取一斗，稍稍浴儿。[62p]

    Five substances form a sweet licorice ointment, useful for treating young infants who are delicate and weak, often affected by wind evils, feeling strong heat in their bodies, or suffering from major wind, leading to trembling hands and feet. The ingredients are: sweet licorice and protective wind (each one tael), white atractylodes and platycodon (each twenty zhu), and two taels of thunderbolt herb.

    Grind these ingredients, and then using one pound of unsalted pig fat, cook over low heat until it reduces to a thick ointment, straining out the residue. Take a piece about the size of a marble and warm it in your hands to rub on the child a hundred times. If the child feels cold, warm them further; if hot, cool them down. Even if a child seems healthy, it is advisable to apply the ointment on their forehead and the palms of their hands and feet upon waking up to effectively ward off wind and cold.

    Li Leaf Bathing Decoction: For treating slight heat in young bodies.

    Use an unspecified amount of li leaves, grinding them up. Boil in water and strain, then use to bathe the child.

    Willow Branch Bathing Decoction: For infants from one month to five months old, experiencing fluctuations of cold and heat.

    Use a non-specified amount of finely chopped willow branches. Boil to extract the juice and wash the child. If the child is thirsty, strain winter melon juice for them to drink.

    Green Wood Fragrance Bathing Decoction: For treating young children suffering from intense heat and emaciation.

    Ingredients include four ounces of green wood fragrance, one sheng each of hemp seeds and bamboo leaves, five ounces of tiger bone, and three ounces of white atractylodes. Grind these five ingredients together and boil in two dou of water to extract one dou of liquid, then bathe the child gently.[62p]

    　　十二物寒水石散　治少小身体壮热，不能服药。　　寒水石　芒硝　滑石　石膏　赤石脂　大黄　青木香　甘草　黄芩　防风　芎穷　麻黄根　　右，各等分，合治下筛，以粉一升，药屑二合相和，复以筛筛之，以粉儿身，日三。
    　　李根汤　治小儿暴有热，得之二三日者。　　李根　桂心　芒硝各十八铢　麦门冬去心　甘草各一两　　右五味(口父)咀，以水三升，煮取一升，分五服。
    　　升麻汤　治小儿伤寒变热毒病，身热面赤，口燥，心腹坚急，大小便不利，或口疮者；或因壮热，便四肢挛掣惊仍成癎疾，时发时醒，醒后身热如火者，悉主之。　　黄芩一两　升麻　白薇　麻黄　萎蕤　柴胡　甘草各半两　(石卜)硝　大黄　钓藤各六铢　　右十味(口父)咀，以水三升，先煮麻黄去上沫，内诸药，煮取一升。儿生三十日至六十日，一服二合；六十日至百日，一服二合半；百日至二百日，一服三合。[63p]

    Twelve substances: cold water stone disperses heat, used to treat small children with vigorous heat, who cannot take medicine. Cold water stone, mirabilite, talc, gypsum, red resin, rhubarb,青木香 (a type of herb), licorice, scutellaria, saposhnikovia, ephedra root. All in equal parts, to be ground and sifted together, one sheng of powder, mixed with two haos of medication residue, and sifted again until fine, to be taken three times a day.

    Li Gen Decoction: used to treat children with sudden fevers lasting two to three days. Li gen, cinnamon bark, and mirabilite, eighteen zhu each; dried ophiopogon root, and licorice, one liang each. The five ingredients should be chewed and boiled in three sheng of water, reducing to one sheng, divided into five doses.

    Sheng Ma Decoction: used to treat children's febrile diseases that switch to toxic heat, with symptoms like fever, red face, dry mouth, firm abdominal pain, difficulty in urination and defecation, or mouth sores; or due to vigorous heat causing limbs to twitch and convulsions, with intermittent waking up and a body hot like fire afterwards. For this, use one liang of scutellaria, half liang each of sheng ma, white atractylodes, ephedra, stemona, and bupleurum, and half liang of licorice; six zhu each of mirabilite, rhubarb, and vine root. All ten ingredients should be chewed, boiled in three sheng of water, first boiling the ephedra to remove the foam, then adding the other ingredients until one sheng is left. For children aged thirty to sixty days, take two haos; from sixty to one hundred days, two and a half haos; from one hundred to two hundred days, three haos.[63p]

    　　大黄汤　治小儿肉中久挟宿热瘠热，进退休作无时。　　生大黄　芒硝　甘草各半两　桂心八两　石膏一两　大枣五枚　　右六味(口父)咀，以水三升，煮取一升，每服二合。

    Dahuang Decoction - Treats children with longstanding internal heat and emaciation, with irregular eating patterns.
    Ingredients:

    • Rhubarb: 1 ounce
    • Glauber's salt: 1 ounce
    • Licorice: 1 ounce
    • Cinnamon: 8 ounces
    • Gypsum: 1 ounce
    • Dates: 5 pieces

    Prepare by grinding the above six ingredients, boil with 3 liters of water to extract 1 liter, and administer 2 danti (about 60 ml) each time.

    Shuqiang Decoction - Treats children with tidal fevers.
    Ingredients:

    • Chinese lacquer: 1 ounce
    • Licorice: 1 ounce
    • Anemarrhena: 1 ounce
    • Dragon bone: 1 ounce
    • Oyster shell: 1 ounce

    Prepare by grinding the above five ingredients, boil with 4 liters of water to extract 1 liter, then strain. For children under one year, administer a small amount twice daily.

    Gypsum Decoction - Treats children with abdominal distension and shortness of breath; those showing signs of fluctuating heat, with digestive distress leading to food not being properly processed.
    Ingredients:

    • Rhubarb: 1 ounce
    • Scutellaria: 1 ounce
    • Licorice: 1 ounce

    • Glauber's salt: 1 ounce
    • Gypsum: 1 ounce
    • Cinnamon: 8 grains

    Prepare by grinding the above seven ingredients, boil with 3 liters of water to extract 1.5 liters; administer three doses. For children under one year, give five doses.[64p]

    　　竹叶汤　治小儿夏月患腹中伏热，温壮来往；或患下痢，色或白或黄，三焦不利。　　竹叶切　小麦各五合　柴胡　麦门冬　人参　甘草各半两　茯苓十八铢　黄芩一两六铢　　右八味(口父)咀，以水四升，煮竹叶、小麦，取三升，去竹叶、小麦，下诸药，煮取一升半，分三服。若小儿夏月忽壮热烧人手，洞下黄溏，气力惙然，脉极洪数，用此方加大黄二两，再服得下即瘥。　　又　治五六岁儿温壮，腹中急满，息不利，或有微肿；亦治极羸不下饮食，坚痞，手足逆冷。　　竹叶一升　小麦半升　甘草　黄芩　瓜蒌根　泽泻　茯苓　知母　白朮　大黄各一两　桂心二铢　生姜一两半　人参　麦门冬　半夏各二两　当归十八铢　　右十六味(口父)咀，以水七升，煮竹叶、小麦，取四升，去滓内药，煮取一升六合，分四服。[65p]

    Bamboo Leaf Decoction: Treats children suffering from abdominal heat in summer, causing warmth and movement; or those with diarrhea, which may be white or yellow, indicating issues in the three burners.

    Ingredients:
    Bamboo leaves and wheat, each five dou; Bupleurum, Ophiopogon, Ginseng, and Licorice, each half liang; Poria, eighteen zhui; Scutellaria, one liang and six zhui.

    Preparation: Combine these eight ingredients, slice them, and use four sheng of water to boil the bamboo leaves and wheat, extracting three sheng. Remove the bamboo leaves and wheat, add the remaining herbs, boil down to one sheng and half, and divide into three doses.

    If a child suddenly has a strong heat in summer, marked by a yellow, watery diarrhea and weak energy, with a rapid pulse, add two liang of Rhubarb to this formula. If it causes a bowel movement, the child will recover.

    Additionally, this treats children aged five or six with excess heat, a tight abdominal feeling, ineffective breathing, or slight swelling; it also addresses extreme thinness with poor appetite, hard distension, and cold hands and feet.

    Ingredients:
    One sheng of bamboo leaves; half sheng of wheat; one liang each of Licorice, Scutellaria, Trichosanthes root, Alisma, Poria, Anemarrhena, Atractylodes; two zhui of Cinnamon bark; one and a half liang of fresh ginger; two liang each of Ginseng, Ophiopogon, and Pinellia; eighteen zhui of Angelica.

    Preparation: Combine these sixteen ingredients, slice them, and use seven sheng of water to boil the bamboo leaves and wheat, extracting four sheng. Remove the residue and boil the remaining herbs down to one sheng and six liu, dividing into four doses.[65p]

    　　大黄牡蛎汤　治小儿壮热，实滞不去，寒热往来，微惊悸。　　大黄一两　黄芩　瓜蒌根　甘草各十八铢　滑石二两　桂心　牡蛎煅　人参　龙骨　凝水石　白石脂　硝石各半两　　右十二味(口父)咀，以水四升，煮取一升半，每服三合，一日一夜令尽；虽吐亦与之。一本加紫石英半两。[66p]

    Dashuang Muli Soup treats children with high fever, retained food that does not pass, intermittent chills and heat, and mild palpitations.

    Ingredients:

    • 1 tael of Dahuang (rhubarb)
    • 18 zhu of Huangqin (Scutellaria baicalensis)
    • 18 zhu of Guolou root (Trichosanthes fruit)
    • 18 zhu of Gancao (licorice)
    • 2 taels of Huashi (talcm)
    • Half tael of Guixin (cinnamon heart)
    • Half tael of Danyi (calcined oyster)
    • Half tael of Renshen (ginseng)
    • Half tael of Longgu (dragon bone)
    • Half tael of Ningshuishi (congealed water stone)
    • Half tael of Baishizhi (white stone fat)
    • Half tael of Xiaoshih (niter)

    Prepare these twelve ingredients by grinding together. Add 4 sheng of water and boil down to 1.5 sheng. Take 3 he (a measure) each time, to be taken day and night until finished; it can still be given even if vomiting occurs. One version adds half tael of Zishiqing (purple quartz).[66p]

    　　调中汤　治小儿春秋月晨夕中暴冷，冷气折其四肢，热不得泄则壮热，冷气入胃变下痢或赤白滞，起数，小腹胀痛极，壮热，气脉洪大或急数者，服之热便歇，下亦瘥也；但壮热不吐下者亦主之。　　葛根　黄芩　茯苓　桔梗　芍药　白朮　槁本　大黄　甘草各六铢　　右九味(口父)咀，以水二升，煮取五合，服如后法。儿生一月至七日，取一合分三服；生八日至十五日，取一合半分三服；生十六日至二十日，取二合分三服；生二十日至三十日，取三合分三服；生三十日至四十日，取五合分三服，恐吃五合未得，更以意斟酌；百日至三百日儿，一如前篇龙胆汤加之。
    　　生地黄汤　治小儿寒热进退，啼呼腹痛。　　生地黄　桂心各二两
    　　右二味，以水三升，煮取一升。期岁以下服二合，已上三合。一方七味，有芍药、寒水石、黄芩、当归、甘草各半两。
    　　犀角饮　治小儿心脏热感。[67p]

    Tiao Zhong Decoction: Used for children in spring and autumn who are exposed to cold mornings and evenings. Cold air can cause their limbs to feel weakened; if heat cannot be released, it will lead to strong fever. Cold air entering the stomach can cause diarrhea or obstruction, with symptoms such as abdominal distention and severe pain, strong heat, and rapid pulse. Administering this will alleviate heat and resolve the condition; it is also effective for those with strong heat who do not vomit or have bowel movements.

    Ingredients:

    • Pueraria (Ge Gen),
    • Scutellaria (Huang Qin),
    • Poria (Fu Ling),
    • Platycodon (Jie Geng),
    • Peony (Shao Yao),
    • Atractylodes (Bai Zhu),
    • Licorice (Gan Cao),
    • Rhubarb (Da Huang),
      each six zhū (a weight measure).

    The above nine ingredients should be chewed and boiled in two sheng (about 4 pints) of water until reduced to five he (about 1.3 pints). Dosage is as follows: for a child born within one month, take one he divided into three doses; for eight to fifteen days, one and a half he divided into three doses; for sixteen to twenty days, two he divided into three doses; for twenty to thirty days, three he divided into three doses; for thirty to forty days, five he divided into three doses, but if five he seems excessive, adjust accordingly; for children from one hundred to three hundred days, use this recipe but add ingredients from the previous Long Dan Decoction.

    Sheng Di Huang Decoction: Used for children with alternating cold and heat, irritability, and abdominal pain.

    • Fresh Rehmannia (Sheng Di Huang),
    • Cinnamon (Gui Xin),
      each two liang (about 75 grams).

    Boil the two ingredients in three sheng (about 6 pints) of water to yield one sheng (about 2.6 pints). For children under one year, administer two he; for those over one year, three he. Another formula comprises seven ingredients: Peony, cold water stone, Scutellaria, Angelica (Dang Gui), and Licorice, each half a liang (about 19 grams).

    Xi Jiao Decoction: Used for children with heat in the heart.[67p]

    　　犀角十八铢　茯神一两　麦门冬一两半　甘草半两　白朮六铢　　右五味(口父)咀，以水九合，煎取四合，分服。加龙齿一两佳。
    　　加味小柴胡汤 【《钱氏直诀》，下同】 　治乳母肝火发热等证，致儿为患，子母并服。　　柴胡一钱　黄芩七分　人参　半夏各四分　甘草三分　山栀　丹皮各五分　　右，水煎。

    Rhinoceros horn 18 zhu, Polygala 1 tael, Ophiopogon 1.5 taels, Licorice 0.5 taels, Atractylodes 6 zhu. The above five ingredients (mouth father) are chewed, combined with 9 cups of water, decocted to yield 4 cups, to be divided for consumption. Adding 1 tael of dragon's teeth is preferred.

    Modified Xiao Chai Hu Decoction 【from "Qian's Straightforward Method", same below】. Used for treating liver fire heat in nursing mothers, which causes issues for the child; both mother and child may take it. Chai Hu 1 qian, Huang Qin 7 fen, Ren Shen, Ban Xia each 4 fen, Gan Cao 3 fen, Shan Zhi, Dan Pi each 5 fen. The above are to be decocted in water.

    Chai Shu Ren Ling Decoction treats liver fire and blood heat, resulting in generalized itching, red rashes, or muscle spasms and nodules. Bai Zhu (fried) 1 qian, Ren Shen, Fu Ling each 1 qian, Chai Hu, Chuan Xiong, Shan Zhi, Shao Yao (fried), Gan Cao (fried) each 5 fen, Shu Di Huang (self-prepared), Dang Gui each 8 fen. The above are to be decocted in water for consumption.

    Shao Yao Ren Ling Powder treats liver wood overpowering spleen earth, leading to eye strain and facial pallor, decreased appetite, and fatigue. Shao Yao (fried), Ren Shen, Fu Ling, Bai Zhu, Chen Pi each 7 fen, Chai Hu, Shan Zhi (fried), Gan Cao (fried) each 5 fen. The above are to be decocted in ginger water.

    Long Dan Xie Gan Decoction treats liver channel damp heat, or abscesses or toxins, with dysuria. Long Dan Cao (fried in wine) 5 fen, Che Qian Zi (fried) 3 fen, Mu Tong, Dang Gui Wei, Ze Xie each 3 fen, Gan Cao, Huang Qin, Sheng Di, Shan Zhi each 3 fen. The above are to be decocted in water for consumption.[68p]

    　　清凉饮　治消中能食而瘦，口干自汗，大便结燥，小便频数。　　羌活　柴胡　炙甘草　知母酒制　黄芪炒　黄芩酒制，各一钱　生甘草　防己　生地酒制　防风各五分　当归六分　红花少许　杏仁　桃仁各五个　升麻四分　石膏　川黄蘗　草龙胆各一钱五分　　右，每服一二钱，水煎，入酒少许服。
