    　　清燥汤　治小儿自汗，或因热伤元气，大小便秘濇。　　黄芪炒　苍朮各五分　白朮　陈皮　泽泻　人参　白茯苓　升麻　麦门冬去心　当归身　生地黄　神曲炒　猪苓黄蘗酒拌炒，各三分　五味子五粒，杵　黄连炒　甘草炙，各二分　　右，姜一片，水一锺，煎服。

    　　加减泻黄散　此药退脾土，复肾水，降心火。　　黄连　茵陈各五分　黄蘗　黄芩　山栀　茯苓各三分　泽泻二分　　右(口父)咀，都作一服，水一盏，煎至六分，去滓稍热服，食后。一服减半，待五日再服而良愈。经云：土位之主，其泻以苦。又云：脾苦湿，急食苦以燥之。故用黄连、茵陈之苦寒，除湿热为君。肾欲坚，急食苦以坚之，所以黄蘗之苦辛寒强筋骨为臣。湿热成烦，以苦泻之，故以黄芩、山栀子之苦寒，止烦满为佐。湿淫于内，以淡泄之，故以茯苓、泽泻之甘淡利小便，导湿为使也。[120p]

    Qingzao Decoction treats children’s spontaneous sweating, either caused by heat injuring the original qi or by constipation.

    Ingredients:

    • 5 fen each of fried Huangqi (Astragalus) and Cangzhu (Atractylodes)
    • 3 fen each of Baizhu (Atractylodes macrocephala), Chenpi (dried tangerine peel), Zexie (Alisma), Ren Shen (ginseng), Baifuling (white Poria), Sheng Ma (Cimicifuga), and Maimendong (Ophiopogon, heart removed)
    • 3 fen of Danggui (Angelica) body, Sheng Dihuang (fresh rehmannia), and fried Shenchu (fermented wheat), mixed with Zhu Ling (Polyporus) and Huangbai (phellodendron) first sautéed, 3 fen each
    • 5 pieces of Wuweizi (Schisandra berries), crushed
    • 2 fen each of fried Huanglian (Coptis) and honey-fried licorice

    Combine all, with a slice of ginger and water in a bowl. Boil and take the decoction.

    Additions and Subtractions to Xiehuang Powder: This medicine drains the spleen soil, restores kidney water, and reduces heart fire.

    Ingredients:

    • 5 fen each of Huanglian (Coptis) and Yincheng (Artemisia)
    • 3 fen each of Huangbai (phellodendron), Huangqin (Scutellaria), Shan Zhi (gardenia), and Poria
    • 2 fen of Zexie (Alisma)

    All ingredients should be crushed and made into a single dose. Boil with one cup of water until reduced to 6 parts, strain and take warm after meals. Reduce the dosage by half after the first administration, and take again in five days for recovery.

    The classics state: "The soil’s master is treated with bitterness." It also states: "The spleen suffers from dampness; bitter foods must be consumed to dry it." Thus, Huanglian and Yincheng, with their bitter cold properties, are used to clear damp heat as the chief ingredients. The kidney needs to be firm; thus, bitter foods should be consumed to strengthen it, hence Huangbai’s bitter and cold character reinforces the muscles and bones as the minister ingredient. Damp heat creates agitation, thus it must be relieved with bitterness, which is why Huangqin and Shan Zhi, being bitter and cold, are used to calm restlessness and fullness as assistants. Internal dampness is addressed with mild diuretics, hence Poria and Zexie’s sweet, mild properties encourage urination to guide out dampness as the envoy.[120p]

    　　芦根一两　茵陈　山栀　黄芩　甘草各半两　　右件捣罗为细末，每服一钱，水八分，入薄荷三叶，煎至五分，去滓放温服。

    　　黄芩　瓜蒌根　茯神去木，各一两　甘草　胡黄连各半两　　右件为细末，每服一钱，水八分，煎五分，去滓温服。
    　　茵陈汤　治小儿发黄等病，身如橘色。　　山茵陈　山栀子仁各一两　川大黄　川芒硝　木通　寒水石各半两　　右，煎服法同前。

    　　双连丹　治疸病。
    　　川黄连去须　胡黄连各一两
    　　右件捣罗为细末，用黄瓜一枚去穰，留一小盖子，入二药末后，以盖子盖定，用面裹，慢火烧令面焦，去面捣熟，如菉豆大，每服七粒至十粒，温水下。量儿大小，以意加减。[121p]

    Zhang Huan's Reed Root Decoction for treating jaundice.
    One tael of reed root, half a tael each of Artemisia capillaris, Gardenia fruit, Huangqin, and licorice. Grind these ingredients into a fine powder. For each dose, take one qian, mix with eight parts water, add three leaves of mint, and decoct until reduced to five parts. Strain and let it cool before drinking.

    Ziling Powder for treating jaundice.
    One tael each of Huangqin, Trichosanthes root, and Poria without wood, half a tael each of licorice and Hu Huanglian. Grind these into a fine powder. For each dose, take one qian, mix with eight parts water, decoct for five parts, strain and warm before drinking.

    Yinchen Decoction for treating jaundice in children, presenting with a tangerine-like complexion.
    One tael each of mountain Yinchen and Gardenia seeds, half a tael each of Rhubarb, Glauber's salt, and Mutong, and cold water stone. Decoction method is the same as above.

    Shuangliandan for treating jaundice.
    One tael each of Hu Huanglian without whiskers and Chuan Huanglian. Grind these into a fine powder, use one cucumber, remove the seeds, keeping a small cap. After adding the two powdered medicines, cover it with the cap, wrap it in flour, and cook over low heat until the flour is charred. Remove the flour and grind it until fine, forming small pills as large as soybeans. Take seven to ten pills with warm water, adjusting dosage based on the child's size.[121p]

    　　当归丸　治小儿冷热不调，大便青黄，心腹多痛，或腹中气满，或时呕逆，不欲饮食。加枳壳尤妙。亦治阴黄。　　当归　白芍药　人参　川芎各三钱　炙甘草　白朮各半两　　右为末，水煮面糊为丸如麻子大，三岁儿每服十丸，粥饮下，日三服，量儿大小加减。冷甚，加陈皮。
    　　茯苓渗湿汤　治小儿黄疸寒热，呕吐而渴欲饮水，身体面目俱黄，小便不利，不得安卧，不思饮食。　　茯苓五分　泽泻三分　茵陈六分　猪苓　山栀　黄连　防己　白朮　苍朮　陈皮　青皮　枳壳　黄芩各二钱　　右(口父)咀，水煎，徐徐温服。

    　　丹溪棱朮散　治小儿吐泻黄疸。
    　　三棱　蓬朮　青皮　陈皮　神曲　麦芽　黄连　甘草　白朮　茯苓各等分　　右为末，温熟水调服。若伤乳食吐泻，加山楂；时气吐泻，加滑石；发热，加薄荷。[122p]

    Danggui Pill: Used for treating children with imbalance of hot and cold, greenish-yellow stools, abdominal pain, fullness in the abdomen, intermittent vomiting, and lack of appetite. Adding bitter orange peel is particularly effective. It also treats jaundice.

    • Ingredients: Danggui, Bai Shao Yao, Ren Shen, Chuan Xiong (each 9 grams), Zhi Gan Cao, Bai Zhu (each 15 grams).
    • Grind the above into a powder, then mix with water to form small pills the size of sesame seeds. For a three-year-old, each dose is ten pills, taken with congee three times a day, adjusting the amount according to the child’s size. If the cold is severe, add aged tangerine peel.

    Fu Ling Diuretic Soup: Used for treating children with jaundice accompanied by cold and heat, vomiting, thirst for drinking water, yellowing of the body and face, difficulty urinating, inability to rest, and lack of appetite.

    • Ingredients: Fu Ling (5 grams), Ze Xie (3 grams), Yin Chen (6 grams), Pig Mushrooms, Mountain Gardenia, Huang Lian, Fang Ji, Bai Zhu, Cang Zhu, Chen Pi, Qing Pi, Zhi Ke, Huang Qin (each 6 grams).
    • Grind the ingredients, decoct in water, and take warm gradually.

    Dan Xi Ling Zhu San: Used for treating children with vomiting and diarrhea due to jaundice.

    • Ingredients: San Ling, Peng Zhu, Qing Pi, Chen Pi, Shen Qu, Mai Ya, Huang Lian, Gan Cao, Bai Zhu, Fu Ling (each in equal parts).
    • Grind into powder and take with warm,熟水. If due to food injury with vomiting and diarrhea, add hawthorn; for seasonal vomiting and diarrhea, add talcum powder; for fever, add mint.[122p]

    　　搐鼻瓜蒂散　治小儿忽发心满坚硬，脚手心热，变为黄疸，不急治则杀人。　　瓜蒂七枚　赤小豆七粒　秫米七粒
    　　右为末，用一字吹两鼻内，令黄水出；余未尽，水调服之，得吐出黄水即愈。　　又
    　　瓜蒂一两　赤小豆四两
    　　右为末，每一钱，温汤调服，服后即卧，当吐清黄汁为效。虚者不宜服。
    　　秦王九疸散　兼治大人小儿。
    　　胃痘，食多喜饮，栀子仁主之。心疸，烦躁心中热，茜根主之。肾疸，唇干，熬亭苈子主之。脾疸，尿赤出少，惕惕恐，瓜蒌主之。膏疸，饮水尿多，秦椒、瓜蒂主之。膏一作肺。舌疸，渴而数便，锺乳主之。肉疸，小便白，凝水石主之。髓疸，目深，多嗜卧，牡蛎、泽泻主之。肝疸，胃热饮多水激肝，白朮主之。右一十一味等分，随病所在加半，捣筛为散，饮服五分匕，日三；稍稍加至方寸匕。儿小者量与之。[123p]

    Chuan Bi Guo Di San
    For treating children who suddenly develop a full, hard heart, with hot hands and feet, turning into jaundice; if not treated urgently, it can be lethal.

    • 7 gourd seeds
    • 7 grains of red beans
    • 7 grains of glutinous rice
      Grind these into powder, blow a small amount into each nostril to induce the discharge of yellow fluid; for any remaining, mix with water and drink. If yellow fluid is expelled, the patient is cured.

    Another Formulation:

    • 1 tael of gourd seeds
    • 4 taels of red beans
      Grind into powder; take 1 qian mixed with warm water, and lie down after consumption; expectorating clear yellow juice signifies effectiveness. Not suitable for those with deficiency.

    Qin Wang Jiu Dan San
    Applicable to both adults and children.

    • For stomach jaundice, characterized by excessive appetite and thirst, use the seeds of gardenia.
    • For heart jaundice, with irritability and internal heat, use madder root.
    • For kidney jaundice, with dry lips, use prepared licorice.
    • For spleen jaundice, with scanty, red urine and anxiety, use gourd seeds.
    • For greasy jaundice, with excessive thirst and urination, use sichuan pepper and gourd seeds.
    • For tongue jaundice, characterized by thirst and frequent urination, use breast milk.
    • For flesh jaundice, with pale urine, use water stone.
    • For marrow jaundice, with deep-set eyes and excessive drowsiness, use oyster and alisma.
    • For liver jaundice, with stomach heat and excessive water consumption affecting the liver, use white atractylodes.

    Grind all 11 ingredients and combine in equal parts, adjusting the amount based on the location of the illness, and sieve to create a powder. Take 5 fen three times a day, gradually increasing to a larger spoonful for those smaller in size.[123p]

    　　黄黑等疸方 [黄黑等疸方　原作千金翼方，据《千金翼》卷十八改。 ]【《千金翼方》】 　治大人小儿黄黑等疸。　　当归三两　桂心六两　干枣十七枚，去核　麦门冬一升，去心　生大黄一两　茵陈　黄芩　黄芪一本无　干姜　茯苓　芍药　黄连　石膏碎　人参　甘草炙，各二两　　右十五味(口父)咀，以水一斗，煮取三升半，分四服。小儿减服。
    　　赤苓散　主黑疸，身皮大便皆黑。通治大人小儿。　　赤小豆三十枚　茯苓　女萎各六铢　雄黄一铢　瓜丁四铢　甘草炙，二铢　　右六味，以水三升，煮豆、茯苓，取八合；捣四味为散，和半钱匕服之，须臾当吐，吐则愈。亦主一切黄。小儿服半字匕。[124p]

    Yellow and Black Jaundice Decoction

    This formula treats yellow and black jaundice in both adults and children.

    Ingredients:

    • 3 taels of Angelica
    • 6 taels of Cinnamon heart
    • 17 dried jujubes, pitted
    • 1 sheng of Ophiopogon, with the heart removed
    • 1 tael of raw Rhubarb
    • 2 taels each of Artemisia, Scutellaria, Astragalus, dried Ginger, Poria, Peony, Coptis, Gypsum, Ginseng, and Honey-fried Licorice

    In total, there are 15 ingredients. Grind them together, boil with 10 liters of water to obtain 3.5 sheng, divided into four doses. For children, reduce the dosage.

    Red Poria Powder

    This formula is for black jaundice, where the skin and stool appear black. It is effective for both adults and children.

    Ingredients:

    • 30 red beans
    • 6 zhū of Poria and female Ziziphus
    • 1 zhū of Realgar
    • 4 zhū of Gourd vine
    • 2 zhū of Honey-fried Licorice

    Combine these 6 ingredients with 3 sheng of water, boil the beans and Poria to get 8 he. Grind the other four ingredients into a powder, mix with half a qian of water for administration. It will induce vomiting, and once vomited, recovery is expected. This also addresses all types of jaundice. For children, use half a qian.[124p]

    Rhinoceros Horn Powder
    Used for treating children with accumulation of heat and phlegm, and impurities in the Sanjiao (three burners); also for wind-heat causing a red face, and constipation.
    Take 1 part of powdered rhinoceros horn, half a tael each of ginseng, bitter orange, and betel nut; steep and slice rhubarb in wine, then peel 100 grains of croton seed, stick them onto the rhubarb, wrap in paper, and steam three times. Chop and fry until browned, remove croton seeds, and use only the rhubarb.
    One tael each of rhubarb and coptis, remove the roots.
    Grind the above into fine powder, refine with honey to make pills the size of sesame seeds. Take 10 to 20 pills with warm water before sleep. If there is no result, increase the number of pills gradually until stable.

    Victory Gold Powder
    Used for treating children with tidal fever and robust heat.
    One qian of realgar, processed with water; half a qian of white atractylodes; half a tael of honey-fried licorice; half a tael of white peony, boiled ten times and dried; half a tael of tian nanxing (arisaema); one part of schizonepeta spikes.
    Grind the above into powder. Take half a qian with a small cup of water, add three leaves of mint, and boil until reduced to a fifth. Remove dregs and take warm at any time.

    Golden Flower Powder
    Used for treating children with tidal fever and irritability.
    One tael of rhubarb; half a tael of gentian.
    Grind the above into powder. Take one character or half a qian with a small cup of water, add three leaves of wormwood and two inches of green onion, and simmer until reduced to a fifth. Remove dregs and take warm. For those with bone steaming fatigue, use a boy's urine to soak wormwood and green onion for medicinal preparation.[125p]

    Cool Body Pill: For treating children with warmth and vigor, body heat, red face, thirst, and agitation.

    Niu Huang Ointment: For treating children with warmth, vigor, and feverish wind.

    Calming Heart Pill: For treating children with fever and shock from wind heat, causing restless sleep.
    Ingredients:

    Pear Juice Porridge: Treats children's wind-heat, confusion, restlessness, and loss of appetite. Use three goose pears, chopped finely, with two liters of water, boil to extract one liter of juice, strain, add one bowl of polished rice, and cook into porridge for consumption.

    Dragon Tooth Powder: Treats children with fever and agitation like fire; also treats warm afflictions. Grind dragon teeth into powder, mix and administer, or grind burned dragon horn for concentrated juice, taking one to two grams.

    Ginseng and Bovine Bile Powder: Equal parts of ginseng and bovine bile ground into powder, mixed with mint water for a superior remedy.

    Bamboo Juice Decoction: Use two cups of bamboo juice, warm it, and divide into three or four doses. If unavailable, scrape bamboo pith, simmer with vinegar, and take while warm.

    Blue Gold Elixir: Treats children with accumulated heat and crying, with stagnation in the three burners. Use four taels of indigo, two taels of raw licorice, one tael of cicada shells (legs removed), one coin of musk, grind; one part of cinnabar, grind and water extract; three grains each of bovine bile and powdered dragon tooth; half a tael each of turmeric. Grind into fine powder, mix with syrup to form balls the size of a chicken head, divide each into four doses, taken dissolved in warm water at any time.

    Four Harmonious Decoction: Treats various fevers in children. Use equal parts of the following: dried ground root of the earth, lewisia removed from the stem and branches, zhi zi fruit, and forsythia. Grind into fine powder, each dose is one or two pennies, mixed with a small cup of water, add a little lampwick and bamboo leaves, simmer until reduced by half, let cool and consume at any time.[127p]

    Ganlu Powder - Treats various fevers in children.
    Ingredients: 1 tael of peppermint leaves, half tael each of rhubarb and licorice, 1 fen each of gnisosperma, chuanxiong, and water-soluble realgar. Grind into a fine powder. Take half a qian mixed with honey water at any time.

    Niu Huang Powder - Treats various fevers and restlessness in children.
    Ingredients: Large amount of curcuma wrapped in damp paper and cooked over a slow fire until done. Grind into a fine powder, mix in a little niu huang, then dissolve in cold water. Use 1 qian for larger children and half a qian for smaller children at any time.

    Chicken Egg Honey
    Use one chicken egg, mix with white honey and take.

    Heat-Releasing Soup - For children who are ill after the beginning of summer and have a fever; do not recklessly induce vomiting or purging, but use this for bathing.
    Ingredients: Equal parts of white atractylodes root and seedlings. Grind coarsely and boil with clear water. Add a small amount of salt for bathing the child. After bathing, dust them lightly with powder.

    Additional formula:
    Ingredients: White atractylodes, bitter cold medicine, and quinine leaves. Boil as a soup; if other herbs are not available, using any one of these in a soup is sufficient.

    Mulberry Leaf: 1 sheng
    Use 7 sheng of water, boil down to 5 sheng, and use warm for bathing.

    Cool Skin Powder
    Ingredients: Equal parts of white atractylodes, maple leaves, dried stems, bitter cold medicine, and Coptis chinensis. Grind into a fine powder. Each use: 3 qian mixed with 3 large pieces of clam powder, ground finely, and placed in a silk bag. After bathing, pat the body evenly with this powder. It is also extremely effective for treating rashes during hot summer months.[128p]

    　　猪胆圆　治小儿血热，早食后发热，至晚则凉。　　胡黄连　宣黄连去须，各半两　赤芍药一两　　右为细末，以豮猪胆汁和成剂，却入在胆皮中，悬铫上，用浆水煮，勿令浆水入，煮熟取出，圆如菉豆大，每服三十圆，米饮汤下，食后临卧，日三。有生瘰疬一证，亦早食后身热颇相似，但以鼻衄泄泻，宜审辨之。

    Pig gallbladder round: Treats children's blood heat, causing fever after eating in the morning, cooling by evening.

    Hu Huanglian: Cured Huanglian, both half a tael. Chi Shaoyao: One tael.

    The above should be finely powdered, mixed with pig gallbladder juice, formed into pills, and placed in a gallbladder skin. Boil with water, ensuring no water enters, simmer until cooked, then take out, shaped like large mung beans. Each dose is thirty pills, taken with rice soup after meals before lying down, three times a day.

    For a case of active swollen lymph nodes, it also resembles the early morning body heat after eating, but if accompanied by nosebleeds and diarrhea, careful differentiation is advised.

    Shengma Gegen Decoction: Treats children's warm wind-damp seizures, and febrile conditions causing body heat, or sores and rashes; this should also be taken during undetermined fevers.

    Dried kudzu shavings, Shengma, Shaoyao, and honey-fried licorice, all in equal parts.

    The above should be coarsely ground; each dose is two qian, with a small cup of water, boiled down to one-fifth, strain and drink warm at any time.

    Jiegeng Decoction: Treats children's wind-heat and strong warmth, or febrile conditions and unmanifested rashes; it is also good when combined with a small black paste.

    Jiegeng, Xiaosin, Ren Shen, Gua Lou root, Bai Zhu, honey-fried licorice, Chuan Xiong, and Bai Fu Ling, all in equal parts.

    The above should be powdered; each dose is two qian, with a cup of water, adding three slices of fresh ginger and three leaves of mint, and simmer until reduced to seven parts. For children under three years, divide into four doses, at any time.[129p]

    　　小黑膏
    　　川乌　南星各一枚，大者
    　　右入一小瓶子内，用湿纸密搭封口，慢火烧之。候火灭取出，削出中心所存白处，如皂子大用之，须烧数枚，择中度者，方用为末，次入薄荷、元参末各五钱匕，研匀，炼蜜和成剂，每用旋剥豆许圆之，葱白汤下，频频服。若筋脉或缓或急，加乳香，同葱白汤下之。
    　　脑子圆　治小儿发热极甚，因伏留心经，昏迷不醒，或误服热药，蓄热所致，用之神效。　　生梅花脑子半字或一字
    　　右取新杀猪心中血一两滴，同研作一圆，新汲水少许化下，大良。未醒即再服一粒。
    　　薄荷散　治小儿风热温壮，及伤寒伤风，痘疹未辨之间，皆可服之。　　薄荷叶　藿香叶去土　荆芥穗　甘松去土白芷　防风去芦，并桠枝　川芎　桔梗去芦　白僵蚕去丝嘴　甘草炙　槁本去土，各一两　细辛去苗，半两　　右为末，每服一钱，茶调温服。亦治大人风气不顺，头面风等疾，大能清利头目，止昏眩，聪明耳目。[130p]

    Xiao Hei Gao

    One piece each of Chuanwu and Nixing, the larger one enters a small bottle, tightly sealed with damp paper, and heated over a low flame. When the fire extinguishes, take it out and shave off the white part in the center, as large as a soap piece. Several pieces must be heated; select the ones of moderate size to be used as powder. Next, add five qian of peppermint and Yuanshen powder, mix well, and refine with honey to form a paste. Each time, roll into small round pills as big as beans, taken with scallion white soup, to be taken frequently. If the pulse is either slow or rapid, add benzoin and take with scallion white soup.

    Nai Zi Yuan
    For treating severe fever in children, caused by hidden heat in the heart channel, leading to coma and unconsciousness, or due to mistakenly taking hot medicine that retains heat, it is highly effective. One half or one character of fresh plum blossom “Nai Zi”.

    Here, take one or two drops of freshly drawn pig heart blood, mix and mold into a ball, dissipate with a little fresh water, which is very effective. If not awakened, take another pill.

    Bo He San
    For treating children with wind-heat and strong fever, as well as for injuries from cold, or during the early stages of smallpox when differentiation is not yet clear.

    Ingredients: peppermint leaves, patches of aromatic grass, spikes of schizonepeta, angelica, and the white part of dichroa, and fang feng without its roots, all at one liang; chuanxiong, licorice roasted, and white silk rearing worm without its threads, all at one liang; xiaxian, half a liang.

    Grind them into a fine powder, each dose of one qian, taken with warm tea. It also treats adults with wind-related issues, head and face wind ailments, effectively clearing vision, stopping dizziness, and enhancing hearing.[130p]

    　　《古今医统》曰：小儿饮水不歇，面目黄者，灸阳刚二穴各一壮，在十四椎下两傍各开一寸陷中。
    　　　　医案

    　　《钱氏直诀》曰：朱监簿子五岁，忽发热。医曰：此心热也。腮赤而唇红，烦躁引饮。遂用牛黄丸三服，以一物泻心汤下之。来日不愈，反如无力而不能食；又下之，便利黄沫。钱曰：心经虚而有留热在内，必被寒药下之致此，虚劳之病也。宜先用白朮散，生胃中津海我陨⒅沃Ｖ煸唬捍蟊泓S沫如何？曰：胃气正，即泻自止，虚热也。朱曰：医用泻心汤如何？钱曰：泻心汤者，黄连一吻耳。黄连性寒，多服则利，能寒脾胃也。坐久众医至，皆曰实热。钱曰：虚热。若实热，何以泻心汤下之不安？又加面黄颊赤，五心烦躁，不食而引饮。医曰：既虚热，何大便黄沫？钱笑曰：便黄沫者，服泻心汤故也。钱与胡黄连丸治愈。[135p]

    For children with excessive heat, whose hair is dry and who speak in their sleep and appear startled: take six fen of niuhuang and five qian of zhusha, grind them together, then mix with rhino horn juice and take one qian.

    Acupuncture

    The "Ancient and Modern Medical Compendium" states: If a child drinks water incessantly and has a yellowish face, moxibustion should be applied to the Yanggang points, each with one strong application, at a depth of one cun beside the fourteen vertebrae.

    Medical Case

    The "Qian's Direct Guidelines" states: A five-year-old named Zhu suddenly developed a fever. The physician said: This is heat in the heart. His cheeks were red and his lips were red, and he was irritable and thirsty. Consequently, three doses of niuhuang pills were used, followed by a purging heart decoction. The next day, he did not improve, but instead appeared weak and could not eat; after further purging, he passed yellow foam. Qian remarked: The heart is deficient, and there is retained heat within, caused by the cold medicine, which has resulted in this condition of deficiency and wasting illness. It is better first to use baizhu powder, which promotes the body's fluid in the stomach. When asked how the yellow foam is produced, he responded: When the stomach's qi is right, it will naturally stop purging; this is deficiency heat. Zhu asked: What about the use of the purging heart decoction? Qian replied: The purging heart decoction contains only a bit of huanglian. Huanglian is cold in nature; prolonged use will cause purging and can chill the spleen and stomach. After sitting for a long time, many physicians arrived, all asserting heat is present. Qian insisted it was deficiency heat. If it were real heat, why would the purging heart decoction not settle it? In addition, with a yellow face and red cheeks, anxiety in the five hearts, and not eating but feeling thirsty. The physician inquired: Since it is deficiency heat, why is the stool yellow foam? Qian laughed and said: The yellow foam stool is due to taking the purging heart decoction. Qian treated him with Hu huanglian pills and cured him.[135p]

    　　郑人齐郎中者，家好收药散施。其子忽脏热，齐自取青金膏三服，并一服饵之。服毕至三更，泻五行，其子困睡。齐言子睡多惊，又与青金膏一服，又泻三行，加口干身热；齐言尚有微热未尽；又与青金膏。其妻曰：用药十余行末安，莫生他病否？召钱氏至，曰：已成虚羸。先用白朮散时时服之，后服香苽丸十三日愈。
    　　朱监簿子五岁，夜发热，晓即如故。众医有作伤寒治者，有作热治者，以凉药解之，不愈。其候多涎而喜睡，他医以铁粉丸下涎，其病益甚。至五日，大引饮。钱曰：不可下之。乃取白朮散一两，煎药汁三升，使任意取足服。朱曰：饮多不作泻否？钱曰：无生水不作泻，纵多不足怪也，但不可下耳。朱曰：先治何病？钱曰：止泻治痰，退热清神，皆此药也。至晚服尽。钱视曰：更可服三升。又煎白朮散三升，服尽得稍愈。第三日又服白朮散三升，其子不渴无涎，又投乌胶散二服而安。[136p]

    A man from Zheng, the physician of Qi, was known for collecting and distributing medicinal herbs. His son suddenly developed a fever; the father self-prescribed three doses of Qingjin ointment and administered one dose as a pill. After taking them, at around midnight, the son experienced diarrhea five times and became drowsy. The father remarked that the son was excessively sleepy and gave him another dose of Qingjin ointment, resulting in three more episodes of diarrhea, accompanied by dryness in the mouth and feverishness of the body. The father noted there was still a slight remaining heat, so he administered more Qingjin ointment. The mother said, "Using medicine more than ten times hasn't helped; what if he develops another illness?" They called in Dr. Qian, who stated, "He has become thin and weak." Initially, he used Baizhu powder, taken at intervals, then after thirteen days, he prescribed Xiangji pills, and the son recovered.

    Zhu's five-year-old child developed a fever at night and returned to normal in the morning. Various doctors attempted to treat it as typhoid or as a heat illness, prescribing cooling medicines, but it did not improve. The child exhibited excessive salivation and was very sleepy. Other doctors tried giving iron powder pills to alleviate the salivation, which worsened the condition. After five days, they insisted on giving him a large drink. Dr. Qian said, "It should not be purged." He then took one tael of Baizhu powder, boiled it down to three sheng of medicinal broth, allowing the child to take as much as he wished. Zhu asked, "Won't drinking too much cause diarrhea?" Dr. Qian replied, "Water alone won't cause diarrhea, even if he drinks a lot, it's not surprising, but it should not be purged." Zhu asked, "What was the initial illness?" Dr. Qian explained, "It stops diarrhea, treats phlegm, and clears heat to calm the spirit; all of this is due to this medicine." By evening, the medicine was fully consumed. Dr. Qian checked and said, "He can still take three sheng." They boiled another three sheng of Baizhu powder, and upon consuming all of it, he began to improve slightly. On the third day, they again administered three sheng of Baizhu powder, and the child no longer felt thirsty or had excessive salivation. They also gave two doses of Wujiao powder, leading to his stability.[136p]

    　　曹宣德子三岁，面黄，时发寒热，不食饮水。或用牛黄、麝香二丸，不愈；用止渴干葛散，反吐。师谓食伏于胃脘，先以白饼子下之，又以消积丸磨之而愈。
    　　《儒门事亲》曰：蔡寨成家一童子，年十五岁，病疸一年，面黄如金，遍身浮肿乏力，惟食盐与焦物。戴人以茶调散吐之，涌涎一盂，临晚又以舟车丸七八十粒、通经散三钱，下四五行。待六七日，又以舟车丸、浚川散，下四五行。盐与焦物见而恶之，面色变红。后再以茶调散涌之，出痰二升方愈。
    　　万氏《幼科发挥》曰：一儿发热，至日晡尤甚，其医作疟治不效，又作潮热治亦不效。予曰：此胃虚有宿食也。谓疟疾则寒热有发有止；谓潮热则发有时如水之潮，过即退，次日依时复发。此儿身尝温热，至申酉时则甚，故知是宿食发热也。彼曰：有所据乎？曰：出仲景伤寒正理论阳明病证云：潮热者实也，宜下之。以三化丸下之愈。[137p]

    Cao Xuande's child was three years old, had a yellowish face, intermittently suffered from chills and fevers, and did not eat or drink. Some used two pills of ox bile and musk, but there was no improvement; when the thirst-quenching dry kudzu powder was used, he vomited in return. The teacher said that food was lodged in the stomach, so first, a white biscuit was given to remedy it, then the digestion pills were ground and administered, and he was cured.

    The "Rumen Shiqin" states: In Caizhai, a household had a young boy of fifteen years old who had been ill with jaundice for a year, his face was yellow like gold, his body was swollen and weak, and he only consumed salt and burnt food. The Dai people used tea to adjust a powder which caused him to vomit a bowl of saliva. By evening, he was given seventy to eighty pills of Zhuoche combined with three qian of Tongjing powder, and four to five doses were taken. After six to seven days, he was administered Zhuoche pills and Jun Chuan powder, again taking four to five doses. He developed a dislike for salt and burnt food, and his complexion turned red. Later, more tea was used to adjust the powder and he expelled two liters of phlegm before fully recovering.

    According to Wan’s "Youke Huafen," a child developed a fever, particularly worsening in the evening. His doctor treated for malaria but it was ineffective, and then attempted treatment for tidal fever, which also failed. I said: this is a case of weak stomach with retained food. If it were malaria, there would be chills and fevers that start and stop; if it were tidal fever, the onset would occur at specific times like the tides, rising and then receding, only to return the next day at the same time. This child's body was usually warm, but became quite severe during the evening hours. Hence, it's understood this is a case of retained food causing a fever. He asked: is there a basis for this? I replied: refer to the theory of Zhang Zhongjing where it discusses the Yangming disease in the case of a febrile illness: tidal fever indicates an excess, which should be purged. Using the Sanhua pills results in recovery.[137p]

    　　一儿惊风时热不退，群医有议用小柴胡汤者，有欲用竹叶汤者，有欲用凉惊丸者。予曰：大惊之后，脾胃已虚，宜温补之。三药寒凉，不可服也。乃作理中汤，用炒干姜，一剂热除。
    　　《明医杂着》曰：李阁老子患潮热，饮食如故，自申西时甚，至子丑时方止，遍身似疥，大便秘结，小便赤濇，热渴饮冷。余以为脾胃实热，传于肺与大肠，先用清凉饮四剂，结热始退；又用四物汤加柴胡、黄连数剂，其疮渐愈。彼欲速效，另用槐角丸之类，诸证益甚，遂求于施院长。亦用四物汤加柴胡、黄连，加桃仁、赤芍药，至百剂而愈。[138p]

    A child suffered from a sudden fever that would not subside. Many doctors debated whether to use Xiao Chai Hu Decoction, some preferred Zhu Ye Decoction, while others suggested Liang Jing Wan.     　　《保婴金镜录》曰：一小儿四岁，发热饮冷，口内生疮，额鼻黄赤，吐舌流涎。余谓心脾有热，用导赤、泻黄二散而愈。后复作，余因他往，服清热化痰等药，前证益甚，更弄舌。余用异功散加钓藤钩而安；又用六君子汤而愈。盖吐舌者，为脾经实热而舌长出也；弄舌者，乃脾脏虚热也，令舌时舒而即收也。治者审之！
    　　一小儿发热，饮食少思，大便不实，常服芦荟等丸。视其鼻赤，此寒凉之剂，复伤脾土而虚热也。用五味异功散数剂而元气复。
    　　一小儿小便不利，鼻干衄血，鼻间色赤，属脾肺有热，用济生犀角地黄汤，前证已愈。后颏间常赤，作渴有痰，此禀赋肾气不足，用地黄丸而诸证皆瘥。
    　　一小儿发热咳嗽，右腮色赤，此肺金有热，用泻白散而愈。复感冒风邪，前证更作，又加声重流涕，用参苏饮加杏仁、桑皮而愈。但右腮仍赤，兼额微赤，此兼心火乘肺金也，用人参平肺散，一剂遂痊。[139p]

    　　一小儿五岁，作渴，右腮鼻准微赤，或饮冷水，或服凉药，即时呕吐。余曰：右腮微赤，肺经虚热也；鼻准微赤，胃经虚热也。此胃虚不能生肺耳。先用四君子加升麻一剂，服之而不吐；又用白朮散二剂而不渴；再用四君子四剂而安。

    　　一小儿五岁：发热作渴，右腮鼻准微赤，或与冷水凉药，即时呕吐。余曰：右腮微赤，肺经虚热也，鼻准微赤，胃经虚热也，此胃虚不能生肺耳。先用四君子加升麻三分一剂而不吐，又用白朮散二剂而不渴，再用四君子四剂而顿安。

    A five-year-old child had a fever and thirst, with a slightly red right cheek and nasal tip. When given cold water or cool medicine, he immediately vomited.     　　一小儿寅卯时发热，或兼搐有痰，服抱龙泻青二丸而愈。后复患，服前药，兼咳嗽气喘，不时发搐，面赤色或青黄，或浮肿，或流涎。予谓咳嗽气喘，脾肺气虚也；不时发搐，肝木乘脾也；面青而黄，肝入心脾也；浮肿流涎，脾气虚也。用益智丸以养心血，补中益气汤以补脾气而愈。

In the morning, the Five-Flavor Odd Function Powder was taken, with a slight addition of Sheng Ma and Chai Hu, and in the evening, the Four-Flavor Fattening Pill was used for eventual recovery.[144p]

    　　一小儿禀赋肾虚，患注夏之疾，因乳母大劳，则发热益甚，用补中益气汤，令母子并服而愈。后因乳母多食膏梁，又患疮疾，烦躁作渴，先用竹叶石膏汤及补中益气汤将瘥；母着怒气，大热发搐，用柴胡栀子散、加味逍遥散而痊。
    　　一小儿注夏，食生冷之物，腹中作痛之甚，则发搐厥冷，用人参理中丸而愈。
    　　一小儿吐泻后患渴证，饮食少思，肌体消瘦，用七味白朮散渴渐止；五味异功散加升麻，饮食渐进；又用补中益气汤，肌肉顿生。
    　　一小儿嗜膏梁甘味，发热作渴，小便白浊，用四味肥儿丸，佐以泻黄散，稍愈；复伤食吐泻，服消食丸；胃气复伤，饮食少思，肢体倦怠而渴，先用七味白朮散而渴止，次用五味异功散而痊。
    　　一小儿面目色白，患渴证，吐痰发热，服清热化痰之药，大便洞泻，小便频数，此脾肾虚而复伤也，朝用补中益气汤，夕用四神丸，诸证渐愈；又佐以六味地黄丸而愈。[145p]

    A young child, with a constitution of kidney deficiency, suffered from summer illnesses. After the wet nurse exerted herself greatly, the child's fever intensified. The treatment involved using the Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction, which was administered to both mother and child, resulting in recovery. Later, due to the wet nurse's excessive consumption of rich foods, the child developed sores, restlessness, and thirst. First, the treatments included Bamboo Leaf and Gypsum Decoction along with Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction, leading to improvement. However, the mother became angry, which caused a severe reaction, so the treatment was adjusted to include Chai Hu and Zhi Zi Powder, along with a modified Xiao Yao San, and the child healed.

    In another case, a child who had a summer illness and consumed cold foods suffered severe abdominal pain, leading to convulsions and coldness. The use of Ren Shen Li Zhong Wan resulted in recovery.

    Another child experienced thirst after vomiting and diarrhea, with reduced appetite and noticeable weight loss. The Qi Wei Bai Zhu San helped to gradually alleviate thirst; later, adding Wu Wei Yi Gong San with Sheng Ma improved appetite and led to the use of Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction, resulting in nourishment of the muscles.

    Another child craved rich foods and sweet flavors, experienced fever and thirst, and had cloudy urine. The treatment included Si Wei Fei Er Wan and was supplemented with Xie Huang San, leading to slight improvements. Afterward, the child suffered from food damage, resulting in vomiting and diarrhea, which required the use of Xiao Shi Wan. With a compromised stomach Qi and reduced appetite, causing fatigue and thirst, first Qi Wei Bai Zhu San was administered to stop the thirst, followed by Wu Wei Yi Gong San, leading to complete recovery.

    Lastly, a child with a pale complexion suffered from thirst, productive cough, and fever. Treatments with heat-clearing and phlegm-resolving medicine led to diarrhea and frequent urination, indicating the injury of the spleen and kidneys. In the morning, Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction was used, and in the evening, Si Shen Wan, resulting in gradual recovery. Additionally, the application of Liu Wei Di Huang Wan led to healing.[145p]

    　　一小儿烦躁惊悸，热渴饮冷，额间色赤，此心经实热，先用泻心汤一服稍缓，又用柴胡栀子散而瘥。
    　　嘉靖甲寅，敬臣之女年十二，患脾胃素弱，自夏入秋，时泻时止，小腹微痛。至八九月间，随成疳积之证，发热凡二十余日不止，汗泄热解，汗已复热。自中脘至小腹，膨胀坚直，大便溏，气喘咳嗽，作嗳，俱昼轻夜重，彻夜烦躁不睡，鼻塞眼暗，讝语，其家以为必死矣。余诊之曰：脉浮大而无根，此大虚证也，非独参汤不可。乃用参一两，加熟附三分，煨生姜三片，日进二剂，乃并渣煎服之，大下疳积，其气则腥，腹渐宽，热渐减，脉渐敛，然手犹寻捻不已，鼻孔出血。余曰：此肝证也，煎六味丸料与之，一服如脱。乃昼服独参姜附汤，夜服六味丸料，脉渐有根，诸证渐退。先此手足恒热，至是乃始觉寒。余喜曰：此病邪尽退，而真气见矣。然犹饮食不进，乃单用六君子汤加炮姜，遂能食；咳嗽独甚，与补中益气汤，嗽遂止，夜始安睡前痊。[146p]

    A young child was restless and anxious, suffering from heat and thirst, drinking cold water, and showing a red hue on the forehead. This indicated internal heat of the heart. First, I administered a dose of Xie Xin Tang to alleviate the condition slightly, followed by Chai Hu Zhi Zi San, which brought recovery.

    In the year of Jia Jing, during the Jia Yin year, the daughter of a loyal official, aged twelve, suffered from inherent weakness of the spleen and stomach. From summer to autumn, she experienced intermittent diarrhea and slight abdominal pain. By August and September, she developed symptoms of accumulation and heat, with a continuous fever lasting over twenty days. She sweated out the heat, but the fever persisted. The abdomen from the center to the lower area was swollen and hard, with loose stools, wheezing, coughing, and belching, all worsening at night and accompanied by restlessness, nasal congestion, darkening of the eyes, and incoherent speech, leading her family to believe she would surely die. Upon examination, I noted the pulse was large and floating with no root, which indicated severe deficiency. I deemed it necessary to prescribe Shen Tang.

    I used one liang of ginseng, three fen of roasted aconite, and three slices of fresh ginger, taken twice a day. This resulted in a significant discharge of the accumulated heat, causing a fishy odor, the abdomen gradually relaxed, and the heat decreased. The pulse began to strengthen but hands continued to tremble, and there was nosebleed. I stated it was a liver condition and prescribed Liu Wei Wan. After one dose, she seemed to have recovered. During the day, she took only the ginseng and ginger soup, and at night, the Liu Wei Wan, her pulse gradually regained strength, and the symptoms lessened.

    Before this, her hands and feet were always hot; now she began to feel cold. I was glad to see that the evil was completely expelled and the true qi was apparent. However, she still had no appetite, so I used only Liu Jun Zi Tang with added roasted ginger, enabling her to eat. The cough was particularly severe, so I administered Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang, which stopped the cough, and she finally slept well and recovered completely at night.[146p]

    　　《证治准绳》曰：罗谦甫治一小儿季夏身体蒸热，胸膈烦满，皮肤如渍橘之黄，眼中白睛亦黄，筋骨痿弱，不能行立。此由季夏之热，加以湿气而蒸热，搏于经络，入于骨髓，使脏气不乎，故脾遂乘心，湿热相合而成此疾也。盖心火实则身体蒸热，胸膈烦满，脾湿胜则皮肤如渍橘之黄，有余之气，必乘己所胜而侮不胜，是肾肝受邪，而筋骨痿弱，不能行立。《内经》言脾热者色黄而肉糯动，又言湿热成痿，信哉斯言也！所谓子能今母实，实则泻其子也。盖脾土退其本位，肾水得复，心火自乎矣。又《内经》曰：治痿独取于阳明，正谓此也。加减泻黄散主之。[147p]

    According to the "Guidelines for Diagnosis and Treatment": Luo Qianfu treated a young child whose body was steaming from summer heat, with a full and troubled chest, skin colored like orange peel, and yellowing of the white of the eyes. The child exhibited weak muscles and bones, unable to stand or walk. This condition arose from the summer heat, compounded by humidity, which steamed and obstructed the meridians and penetrated the bone marrow, causing the organ energies to falter. Thus, the spleen seized control over the heart, leading to the combination of damp heat that resulted in this illness. Indeed, when heart fire is excessive, the body steams with heat, the chest is filled with distress, and when spleen dampness prevails, the skin takes on an orange hue. Excess energy must thereby suppress its own weakness; this indicates that the kidneys and liver have been invaded by evil, resulting in weakened muscles and bones, unable to support standing or walking. The "Inner Canon" states that heat in the spleen results in a yellow color and a glutinous texture of the flesh, and it further mentions damp heat leading to atrophy; these words are truly credible! What is said about the son being nourished by the real mother implies that by nourishing the child, one must reduce its condition. Hence, when the spleen’s earth is diminished from its original position, the kidney's water can return, and the heart's fire will naturally decrease. Furthermore, the "Inner Canon" indicates that the treatment for atrophy specifically focuses on the Yangming channel, and this precisely refers to that principle. A modified version of the Xiaohuang San should be used to address this condition.[147p]

    　　《景岳全书》曰：余之仲儿，生于乙卯五月，于本年初秋，忽尔感寒发热，脉微紧。然素知其脏气属阴，不敢清解，遂与芎、苏、羌、芷、细辛、生姜之属，冀散其寒。一剂下咽，不惟热不退而反大泻作，连二日泻不止而喘继之，愈泻则愈喘。斯时也，将谓其寒气盛耶，何以用温药而反泻？将谓其火刑金耶，岂以清泻连日而尚堪寒凉？将谓其表邪之未除耶，则何以不利于疏散？束手无策，疑惧已甚，且见其表里俱剧，大喘垂危，又岂浅易之剂所能挽回？因沉思良久，渐有所得。乃用人参二钱，生姜五片，煎汁半盏，然未敢骤进，恐再加喘，必致不救。[148p]

    The "Complete Book of Jingyue" states: My second son was born in the year of Yimao, in the fifth month. In early autumn of that year, he suddenly caught a chill and developed a fever, with a weak and tight pulse. However, knowing that his internal organs were prone to cold, I dared not dispel it directly. So I combined herbs such as Chuanxiong, Suye, Qianghuo, Zhizi, Xixin, and fresh ginger, hoping to dispel his cold. After one dose, not only did his fever not subside, but he developed severe diarrhea instead, which did not stop for two consecutive days and was followed by wheezing; the more he diarrheaed, the more he wheezed. At this moment, I wondered if the cold was too strong. Why did warming herbs lead to diarrhea? Could it be that fire was attacking metal? How could days of clearing and purging still be vulnerable to cold and damp? Was it likely that the exterior pathogen remained? If that were the case, why was there no relief when I attempted to disperse it? At a loss, my anxiety grew. I could see his internal condition was severe; he was wheezing and in danger. How could a simple remedy bring him back? After deep contemplation, I gradually understood some things. I decided to use two qian of ginseng and five slices of fresh ginger, decocted into half a cup of liquid, yet I did not dare to administer it hastily, fearing it would worsen the wheezing and lead to a situation beyond remedy.[148p]

    因用茶匙挑与二三匙，即怀之而旋走室中，徐察其呼吸之进退。然喘虽未减，而亦不见其增甚，乃又与三四匙。少顷则觉其鼻息似乎少舒，遂放胆与以半小锺，更觉有应。自午及酉，完此一剂。适一医至，急呼曰：误矣！误矣！焉有大喘如此而尚可用参者？速宜以抱龙丸解之。余诺之而不听，乃复以人参二钱五分，如前煎汤，自酉至子，尽其剂，剂完而气息遂平，齁齁大睡，泻亦止而热亦退矣。此所以知其然者，观其因泻反喘，岂非中虚？设有实邪，自当喘随泻减，是可辨也。向使误听彼医，易以清利，中气一脱，即当置之死地，必仍咎余之误用参也。孰是孰非，何从辨哉？余因纪此，以见温中散寒之功，其妙有如此者。
    [149p]

    Using a tea spoon, I administered two or three doses, then watched closely as the breaths entered and exited. Although the wheezing had not lessened, it also did not increase significantly, so I administered three or four more doses. After a little while, I noticed that the breathing seemed to ease somewhat, so I boldly gave half a small cup, and then there was a noticeable response. From noon until dusk, I completed this one dose. Just then, a physician arrived in haste, calling out: "Mistake! Mistake! How can someone with such severe wheezing still take ginseng? Quickly use Baolong pills to resolve this." I agreed but did not heed his advice, and instead, administered two and a half drachms of ginseng, brewing a decoction as before. From dusk until midnight, I completed the dosage. When the medication was finished, the breathing became steady, and he fell into a deep sleep; the cough ceased, and the fever retreated. This teaches us that the wheezing was a result of the diarrheal reaction, indicating a deficiency in the middle. If there were real pathogenic factors, the wheezing would diminish as the diarrhea lessened, which is distinguishable. Had I mistakenly heeded the physician's advice and switched to cleansing agents, it would have depleted the middle qi, leading to certain danger, and I would have been blamed for wrongly using ginseng. Who is right and who is wrong? How to discern? I record this to demonstrate the efficacy of warming the interior and dispersing cold, showcasing its subtlety.[149p]
